401 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Arlitt v. Weston


No. 04-98-00035-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8912



December 1, 1999, Delivered  
December 1, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 23, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 225th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-CI-07792. Honorable Juan Gallardo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed this appeal from judgments in the 225th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, in favor of defendants on their counterclaims in a dispute arising over legal and equitable title to real property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought declaratory judgment to declare title to real property, injunctive relief and damages arising out of other claims including breach of contract, fraud, and usury. Defendants, various persons holding instruments regarding the property, filed counterclaims and cross-claims against appellant's ex-husband. Before trial, the court dismissed many claims on summary judgment, granted legal title to defendant investment company and a money judgment in favor of defendant noteholder. The jury then returned a verdict against appellant on all remaining claims, except for the fraud claim against appellant's ex-husband. Judgments, including interest and attorney fees, entered for defendants. The appellate court reversed the judgment against appellant for property taxes for the tax foreclosure sale because appellant was no longer responsible. Furthermore, the appellate court reversed judgments on two counterclaims because they either did not support the pleadings or raised a new controversy under the Declaratory Judgment Act. The remaining judgments were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment against appellant for property taxes reversed and reimbursement of property taxes to defendant reversed because appellant was not longer responsible for taxes after foreclosure sale; judgment counterclaims requesting alternative or declaratory relief reversed as neither supported the pleadings or raising a new controversy; remaining judgments were affirmed.

 

402 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 06-99-00058-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


10 S.W.3d 48; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8740


November 22, 1999, Submitted  
November 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 124th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 26,085-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 124th Judicial District Court, Gregg County, Texas, for possession of more than 400 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty without a plea bargain to possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. The court found him guilty and assessed his punishment at 23 years of imprisonment. On appeal, appellant contended that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(f) (Supp. 1999), under which he was convicted and sentenced, was unconstitutional. He contended that it violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, because the punishment it authorized was grossly disproportionate to the crime and as applied to him was inappropriate, and therefore constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The court found that appellant did not preserve this contention for review. Even if he had properly preserved error, his punishment was not cruel or unusual. While the state range of punishment was somewhat higher than that set by the federal statutes for a similar crime, the statute did not necessarily provide an unconstitutional punishment.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The court did not find that, because the state range of punishment was somewhat higher than that set by the federal statutes for a similar crime, the statute necessarily provided an unconstitutional punishment.

 

403 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


TRST Corpus, Inc. v. Financial Ctr., Inc.


NO. 14-98-00051-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


9 S.W.3d 316; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8643



November 18, 1999, Rendered  
November 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied December 7, 2000. Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Denied February 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 334th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-61597. Hon. Russell Lloyd, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant in Part and Denial in Part of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 5, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5826.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing Granted in part and Overruled in part; Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this interlocutory appeal, appellant challenged an order from the 334th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that denied its amended plea to the jurisdiction, arguing that the lawsuit against it was barred by sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: A teacher retirement system that formed a title-holding subsidiary corporation, a state agency, loaned money to a partnership as financing for an addition to an existing office tower complex. The appellant title-holding subsidiary corporation subsequently took title to the property by deed rather than instituting foreclosure proceedings. The appellee management company of the building filed suit alleging various causes of action including tort claims, breach of contract claims, and an unconstitutional "taking" claim, due to the transfer. The trial court dismissed the teacher retirement system from the suit, upon its plea to the jurisdiction, on the basis of sovereign immunity. However, the trial court denied appellant's amended plea to the jurisdiction. The court held that the suit could not be maintained because of defendant's status as a governmental unit, and it was impossible to amend the petition to confer jurisdiction upon the trial court.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded; the suit could not be maintained without legislative permission because of defendant's status as a governmental unit; thus it was impossible to amend petition to confer jurisdiction upon the trial court.

 

404 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Parvin v. Dean


NO. 2-99-135-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


7 S.W.3d 264; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8687



November 18, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 352ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. BONNIE SUDDERTH.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant plaintiff challenged an order from the 352nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which granted appellee's summary judgment in a wrongful death action after an automobile collision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant collided with car of appellee, who was pregnant. Appellant stipulated that he was negligent, that his negligence proximately caused the collision, and that appellee was not negligent. The next day, appellee delivered her child stillborn. Appellees moved for summary judgment during the trial and the trial court granted it, holding that the wrongful death and survival statutes, as construed by the courts of this state, are unconstitutional and the established case law of Texas inflicts upon appellee father gender discrimination that violates the equal protections provisions of the federal and state constitutions. This court held that, on the facts of this case, the Texas wrongful death and survival action statutes unconstitutionally denied redress and equal protection to a mother and father of a viable fetus capable of living outside the womb when viability is wrongly terminated by another's negligent conduct.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Entitling the mother to damages for the mental anguish caused by the experience of losing a viable fetus to another's negligence, while at the same time denying the father an equal right to damages for his mental anguish caused by the same event, was unconstitutional gender discrimination.

Ex parte Huffman


No. 04-99-00404-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


9 S.W.3d 302; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8578



November 17, 1999, Delivered  
November 17, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law No. 8, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 622,798. Honorable Karen Crouch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED FOR WANT OF JURISDICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought relief from an order of the County Court at Law No. 8, Bexar County, Texas, extending community service for two years in order for her to continue making restitution payments on a theft by check charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wrote a check that was returned because the checking account was closed. Defendant was charged with theft by check. She pled nolo contendere, and the court deferred adjudication on the condition that she pay all fines and costs within two years. After missing payments, defendant was arrested on a writ of capias. Before her probationary term expired, the court extended probation for two years for failure to make restitution. Defendant requested an attorney be appointed to assist her in an appeal. The court issued a show cause order, questioning whether the order modifying the terms and conditions of probation was a matter over which it had appellate jurisdiction. Defendant responded by requesting the court to treat this matter as a habeas appeal. The court dismissed, having no jurisdiction because the trial court did not have an opportunity to consider the issue in a proper habeas proceeding.


OUTCOME: Dismissed for want of jurisdiction; the court had no jurisdiction because the trial court did not have an opportunity to consider this issue in a proper habeas proceeding, and defendant presented for review no application for a writ of habeas corpus and no order by the trial court denying relief.

 

406 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


No. 05-98-00661-CR, No. 05-98-00662-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8497



November 15, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 9, Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MA96-78719-K and MA96-78678-K.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the County Criminal Court No. 9, Dallas County, Texas, where separate juries convicted appellant of two misdemeanor obscenity charges and assessed punishment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a clerk at Star Video, a large warehouse that sold and rented adult videotapes. On two separate days, undercover Dallas police officers entered the store and purchased videotapes from appellant. Separate juries convicted appellant of two misdemeanor obscenity charges and assessed punishment. Appellant asserted insufficient evidence to establish that he knew that the videotapes were obscene. However, the state was only required to prove that appellant knew the content and character of the videotapes. Appellant further argued that the statute had no scienter requirement. However, the court disagreed because the obscenity statute requires the state to prove appellant "knew" the content of the videotapes. The court found no abuse of discretion in excluding evidence of another clerk's acquittal for selling the same videotape because proof of prior acquittals in obscenity cases is not admissible in subsequent cases on the issue of community standards.


OUTCOME: Affirmed. All points of error overruled; the trial court did not abuse its discretion.

 

407 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re Abraham


No.08-98-00413-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


22 S.W.3d 512; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8685



November 12, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 3, 2000.



DISPOSITION: Conditionally granted writ of mandamus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, an attorney subject of a contempt proceeding, sought mandamus relief directing the 205th Judicial District Court (Texas) to refer the underlying matter to the presiding judge of the administrative region as required by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002(d) (Vernon Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: Relator, an attorney, was scheduled to appear before the respondent, presiding judge of the district court, in a hearing in a civil suit. Respondent was out of town. Relator advised respondent's secretary that the visiting judge would be unable to preside over any matter involving relator inasmuch as there was a standing order of recusal. A discussion took place. Two days later, relator discovered secondhand that the visiting judge had summarily entered, without notice or a hearing, a judgment holding Relator in contempt. Relator then filed three motions to refer the pending case to the presiding judge, as required by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002(d) (Vernon Supp. 1999), all of which were refused. Relator sought mandamus relief. The appellate court conditionally granted Relator's application for writ of mandamus, finding that Respondent has abused his discretion and violated the clear legal duty in not referring the contempt matter.


OUTCOME: The application for a writ of mandamus was conditionally granted. Respondent abused his discretion and violated the clear legal duty to refer the contempt cause to the presiding judge of the administrative region as required by Texas statute and relator did not have an adequate remedy of appeal from respondent's refusals to act.

 

408 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Montgomery v. State


No. 05-99-00103-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8348



November 9, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 194th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F98-16432-HM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 194th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, for failure to register as a sex offender as required under Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § 62.02(a) (Supp. 1999). Appellant complained that statute was unconstitutionally vague and challenged the factual sufficiency of the evidence supporting conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for failure to register as a sex offender as required under Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § 62.02(a) (Supp. 1999) (statute). The court found that applying the statute to appellant's conduct, complaint that he could not reasonably believe he was required to register as a sex offender in second town was without merit. Appellant lived in second apartment for up to 16 days per month. He signed the lease as an "occupant" and as a "resident." Appellant had fair warning that his living in second town for that amount of time qualified as residing in the municipality for more than seven days under the statute. Thus, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant. Further, appellant could not demonstrate the statute was vague in all of its applications. The trial court's verdict was not against the great weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Affirmed because sex offender registration statute was not unconstitutionally vague; appellant had fair warning that his living in town up to 16 days per month qualified as residing in municipality for more than seven days under statute; further, statute was not vague in all applications; verdict not against weight of evidence.

 

409 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fite v. Cherokee Water Co.


No. 06-99-00028-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


6 S.W.3d 337; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8291


October 21, 1999, Submitted  
November 5, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 188th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 97-1571-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review from a grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee employer, entered by the 188th Judicial District Court, Gregg County (Texas), in a case where appellant challenged the right of appellee to terminate his employment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee sued appellee employer for wrongful termination. Appellant contended appellee terminated him because of appellant's refusal to violate the law, making his termination wrongful. Appellant worked exclusively for appellee as a security officer. Appellee's policy prohibited its security officers from responding to off-premises calls without obtaining permission. The county sheriff's department requested appellant assist off-site in a theft investigation. After he responded, appellee terminated his employment. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. Appellant appealed. The court affirmed. The court held appellant was not required to assist the sheriff's department because no evidence existed anyone from that office had met with resistance in the discharge of his duties. Moreover, the court held, the statutes appellant allegedly was compelled to violate did not have any criminal penalties attached to their violation, so appellant was, in effect, not being asked to break the law.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court affirmed because the criminal statutes appellee employer allegedly had appellant employee violate did not have any criminal penalties attached to their violation, and thus, appellant was subject to termination-at-will by appellee.

411 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. State


NO. 03-99-00235-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8213



November 4, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TOM GREEN COUNTY, 119TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. A-97-1435-C, HONORABLE DICK ALCALA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Tom Green County, 119th Judicial District (Texas), which ordered forfeiture of appellant's cash and automobile on the grounds that the property was considered contraband.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an arrest warrant, appellant was stopped and arrested in his car. Officers observed appellant's wife, who was also present in the car, throwing a rolled-up sock containing cocaine out the passenger window. The trial court found that the items seized during the arrest were contraband and ordered that they be forfeited. The appellate court affirmed the forfeiture because the property was contraband. The court held that since appellant participated in the act giving rise to the forfeiture, he could not be an innocent owner. Furthermore, appellant never affirmatively asserted that he had no knowledge of his wife's criminal activities. Appellant's contention that the warrant was not valid was unsupported by the record. Further, appellant's contention that the seizure of the money exceeded the limits of a search incident to arrest was overruled because the items were located on appellant's person and thus were within his immediate control.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed forfeiture of appellant's cash and car because it was contraband. Since appellant participated in act giving rise to forfeiture, he could not be innocent owner. Seizure did not exceed limits of search incident to arrest because items were located on appellant's person and were within his immediate control.

 

412 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Andress v. MacGregor Med. Ass'n, P.A.


NO. 14-98-00293-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


5 S.W.3d 855; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8034



October 28, 1999, Rendered  
October 28, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 190th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 97-10753-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the order of the 190th District Court, Harris County (Texas) dismissing appellant's medical malpractice cause of action with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed, with prejudice, a medical malpractice suit brought by appellant, an individual, against appellees, including several medical centers and physicians. Appellant brought three issues on appeal: 1) Was it proper to dismiss the lawsuit for failure to timely file a cost bond? 2) Was it proper to dismiss the lawsuit with prejudice for a technical flaw in the cost-bond? 3) Does dismissal violate either the Texas Constitution or the Federal Constitution? Finding the trial court acted properly, this court affirmed. The court found that the legislature imposed the cost-bond requirement under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 13.01 to limit insurance costs and health care costs, to reduce frivolous malpractice claims, and to allow a physician to recoup costs arising from a successful defense. The statute was not unconstitutional, because it was a reasonable means to achieve these purposes.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed; the trial court's dismissal of appellant's medical malpractice action with prejudice for failure to comply with a cost-bond requirement did not violate appellant's right to due process because the cost-bond requirement was a reasonable, non-arbitrary means of controlling medical insurance and health care costs.

 

413 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Carrera v. Yepez


No. 08-98-00186-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


6 S.W.3d 654; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 8062



October 28, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Denied October 12, 2000. Released for Publication January 6, 2000.
Petition for review dismissed for want of jurisdiction by, 08/24/2000
Rehearing denied by, 10/12/2000
Subsequent appeal at Hous. Auth. of El Paso v. Yepez, 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 7187 (Tex. App. El Paso, Aug. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 383rd District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 89-13638).
Housing Authority of El Paso v. Rodriguez-Yepez, 843 S.W.2d 475, 1992 Tex. LEXIS 172, 36 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 361 (Tex., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In case involving claim by public housing residents for violation of right to administrative grievance proceedings, right to organize, and intentional infliction of emotional distress, appellants sought review from order of 383rd District Court of El Paso County, Texas, denying appellants' motion for summary judgment on basis of qualified immunity.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, public housing residents, claimed violation of right to administrative grievance proceedings, right to organize, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. Appellant housing officials sought review from order denying motion for summary judgment based on qualified immunity. The court found that proper inquiry was whether appellants violated due process and equal protection rights by beginning eviction proceedings and denying recourse to standard grievance procedures in retaliation for appellees' exercising their U.S. Const. amend. I rights to freedom of speech and assembly. The court concluded that fact issue existed regarding motive for appellants' actions. Court found that rights of tenants in public housing projects to freedoms of speech and association were sacrosanct and appellants' alleged conduct violated clearly established law. Because violations involved motive-based tort, and because appellees presented objective evidence sufficient to create fact question on motive, trial court properly denied appellants' motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: Order denying summary judgment affirmed because appellants' alleged conduct violated clearly established law, violations involved motive-based tort, and appellees presented objective evidence sufficient to create fact question on motive.

Levario v. State


No. 04-98-00897-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7969



October 27, 1999, Delivered  
October 27, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 10, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 57th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 97-CI-05415. Honorable R. L. Eschenburg, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal of the grant of no-evidence summary judgment in favor of appellee state bar by the 57th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, following appellant's bill of review filed in an attempt to set aside his judgment of disbarment.


OVERVIEW: Following his disbarment as an attorney at law, appellant filed a motion for a new trial and a notice of appeal. The court of appeals dismissed for failure to timely perfect the appeal. The state supreme court then denied appellant's writ of error, and the United States Supreme Court denied his petition for writ of certiorari. Appellant then filed a bill of review in the trial court attempting to set aside the judgment. The trial court granted appellee's motion for no-evidence summary judgment. On appeal, appellant asserted that that Tex. R. Civ. P. 166a(i) was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed, noting that appellant failed to prove that his failure to present his defense at trial was unmixed with his own negligence. The challenge to the statute was raised for the first time in the motion for new trial, and was not preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed, because appellant failed to prove that his failure to present his defense at trial was unmixed with his own negligence, his allegations of perjury would not support a bill of review, and the challenge to the statute was not preserved for appeal.

Ray v. Texas State Bd. of Pub. Accountancy


NO. 03-98-00557-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


4 S.W.3d 429; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7933



October 21, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 261ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-09251, HONORABLE SUZANNE COVINGTON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 261st Judicial District (Texas) which affirmed an administrative order revoking his license to practice as a certified public accountant for violations of 22 Tex. Admin. Code § 501.22.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a certified public accountant licensed by the Texas State Board of Public Accountancy (Board). The office of administrative hearings scheduled a hearing to address allegations that appellant had violated well-established professional standards with respect to audits he had performed. Appellant had three months notice of the hearing. At the end of the hearing the Board revoked appellant's license and denied a motion for rehearing. Appellant filed suit, seeking judicial review of the Board's action. The trial court affirmed the Board's action. Appellant claimed that the Board unconstitutionally delegated its powers to the American Institute of Public Accountants and denied him procedural due process in the hearing. The appeal court affirmed because it found that no delegation of powers occurred and due process was afforded because appellant was given the requisite notice and had a meaningful opportunity to be heard at the administrative hearing.


OUTCOME: The order revoking appellant's license was affirmed because no delegation of powers occurred and due process was afforded because appellant was given the requisite notice and had a meaningful opportunity to be heard at the administrative hearing.

Harris v. State


NO. 01-97-01225-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7666



October 14, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 9, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 743,400.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant appealed from a plea of no contest, a conviction pursuant to Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § 1.15, and a sentence and fine, entered by the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), in a case where appellant was charged with criminally negligent homicide.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellant was charged with criminally negligent homicide. She pled no contest to the charge. Prosecution appellee did not recommend a sentence. The trial court entered a conviction pursuant to Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § 1.15. Also, the trial court sentenced her to ten years in prison and a $ 10,000 fine. Appellant appealed and alleged five points of error. She alleged the statute used to convict her was unconstitutional. The court held her argument was without merit. The court held appellant waived the right to appearance, confrontation and cross-examination of witnesses process. The court also held she waived the right to have the trial court compel witnesses to testify. The court further held that because appellant did not object in the trial court to the remaining points of alleged error, she presented the court with nothing for review. Accordingly, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: Judgment of trial court affirmed because the record reflected that criminal appellant waived compulsory process and since she did not object at trial, her remaining points of alleged error presented nothing for review.

Postive Feed, Inc. v. Guthmann


NO. 01-98-00485-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


4 S.W.3d 879; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7665; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8454



October 14, 1999, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 25th District Court. Colorado County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 18,237.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a no-evidence summary judgment granted on the motion of appellee by the 25th District Court, Colorado County, Texas, in an action by appellant to recover costs from a prior unemployment action.


OVERVIEW: In the prior action in the lower court, appellant successfully sued to set aside unemployment benefits awarded appellee, a former employee. Appellant sued appellee again on two grounds for recovery, in tort for abuse of the civil process and to declare Tex. Labor Code § 207.007, which barred such recovery, unconstitutional. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming inter alia, that appellant did not state a claim on which the court could grant relief. The motion, and the appellant's response thereto, did not address the constitutional argument. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the complaint entirely. On appeal, the court held that the lower court granted more relief than was requested, so the matter was reversed in part and remanded for consideration of the constitutional challenge. However, appellant could not circumvent § 207.007 under a new tort theory, so that aspect of the summary judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded for determination as to whether statute preventing recovery was constitutional; affirmed to preclude appellant from seeking recovery under a new tort theory.

 

419 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Alt v. State


NO. 03-99-00135-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7422



October 7, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 7 OF TRAVIS COUNTY. NO. 459996, HONORABLE BRENDA KENNEDY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed decision by County Court at Law No. 7. Of Travis County, (Texas), which overruled his motion to suppress evidence and special plea of former jeopardy, and found him guilty of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appellant took and failed a breath test following his arrest for driving while intoxicated. Accordingly, the Department of Public Safety suspended his driver's license pursuant to Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 524.012 (West 1999). Defendant appealed the suspension. At the ensuing hearing, the administrative law judge found that the arresting officer did not have probable cause to arrest appellant and ordered the reinstatement of his license. Appellant contended the State was collaterally estopped from relitigating the probable cause issue at his subsequent trial for driving while intoxicated, and therefore the county court at law should have sustained both his motion to suppress evidence obtained as a result of the arrest and his special plea of former jeopardy. The appellate court concluded that an appellant could not invoke the common law collateral estoppel doctrine because the legislature had declared it inapplicable to a criminal prosecution following an administrative license suspension proceeding.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; prosecution for driving while intoxicated following an administrative driver's license suspension proceeding did not constitute a "successive criminal prosecution" or carry the possibility of "multiple criminal punishments," and therefore did not implicate the Fifth Amendment double jeopardy guarantee.

Dziedzic v. Stephanou


NO. 14-97-00163-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7458



October 7, 1999, Rendered  
October 7, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 16, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 270th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-00436.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants appealed from an order of the 270th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted a directed verdict in favor of appellees in medical malpractice case involving alleged failure to remove placental particles at time of delivery and failure to timely diagnose and treat post-delivery problems of excessive bleeding.


OVERVIEW: In a medical malpractice case, appellants alleged that appellee obstetrician failed to remove placental particles at the time of delivery and failed to timely diagnose and treat certain post-delivery problems. On appeal, the court held that appellant's waiver argument was misplaced because the trial court may sua sponte instruct the jury as to the verdict it may return, or it may withdraw the case from the jury and render judgment. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting a directed verdict on the basis that the only offered expert witness was not a qualified expert witness. The court did not err in directing a verdict for appellees on the informed consent issue and further held that the court acted within its discretion in admitting appellee's testimony concerning whether a reasonable person would have refused drug therapy for preterm labor.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The appellate court held that the court did not err in directing a verdict for appellees on the informed consent issue and further held that the court acted within its discretion in admitting the appellee's testimony concerning whether a reasonable person would have refused drug therapy for preterm labor.

In re K.C.M.


NO. 01-98-00133-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


4 S.W.3d 392; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7497



October 7, 1999, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied March 30, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 314th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-98382J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment terminating mother's parental rights reversed, and remanded to trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Mother appealed the judgment terminating her parental rights from the 314th District Court, Harris County, Texas, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support finding that termination was in the best interests of the child.


OVERVIEW: The child was removed from his parents' care when he was 19 months old and the parent-child relationship was terminated thirteen months later. Though the evidence of mother's drug addiction and her ability to parent was legally sufficient to find that termination was in the best interest of the child, after the court weighed the totality of the evidence, it concluded that termination was not in the best interest of the child. The court held that termination was against the great weight and preponderance of the evidence and was clearly unjust in light of the uncontroverted evidence of the progress mother had made while in jail. Mindful that a strong presumption that the best interest of the child was served by keeping custody in the natural parent, a "firm belief or conviction" that the best interest of the child required termination of mother's parental rights could not be fairly reached.


OUTCOME: Order terminating mother's parental rights reversed and remand because the factual sufficiency of the evidence failed to support the "best interest" of the child finding.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the dismissal of his lawsuit, pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 14.005(b)(1999), entered by the 258th District Court, Polk County (Texas), in a case where appellant challenged the constitutionality of prison grievance procedures.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed challenges in the trial court regarding his prison grievance system. The trial court dismissed his petition. The court also held appellant's challenges were raised more than 31 days after he received a written response from the grievance system and, as a result, he had not complied with statutory requirements necessary to make the administrative grievances subject to judicial review.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing appellant's lawsuit affirmed because appellant did not comply with the statutory requirements to have the results of his administrative grievance made subject to judicial review.

In re Spiegel


NO. 07-98-0418-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


6 S.W.3d 643; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7384



October 5, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. THREE OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 98-503,132; HON. PAULA LANEHART, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The husband appealed from the denial of the County Court at Law No. Three of Lubbock County (Texas) of his request for a temporary injunction in a divorce proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The wife petitioned for divorce. Although the record did not show that the husband filed an answer seeking permanent injunctive relief, it did contain his application for a temporary injunction. After a hearing, the trial court denied the application via two orders. There was nothing in the clerk's record indicating why the court held as it did. The husband appealed; however, absent from the record was the reporter's record transcribing the proceedings at which his request for injunctive relief was considered, because the husband expressly stated that he would not request a record. On appeal, the court held that an injunction requires the presentation of evidence. Thus, the absence of a reporter's record was dispositive, because the court did not know what evidence was presented to the trial court nor was the court able to assess whether the husband satisfied the prerequisites to obtaining the requested relief.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The court affirmed the orders denying the application for a temporary injunction because the husband opted not to provide the appellate court with a complete record.

Burke v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH

October 1, 1999, Delivered

DISPOSITION: As reformed, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for discretionary review of a judgment of the 372nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) in which appellant was convicted and sentenced under both the general aggravated assault and specific intoxication assault statutes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, driving while intoxicated, collided with another automobile and caused serious bodily injury to the driver. Charged with reckless aggravated assault with serious bodily injury and intoxication assault, appellant pled guilty to both, was sentenced to 15 and 10 years' confinement, to be served consecutively. Appellant appealed, arguing the trial court erred in denying a new trial on double jeopardy grounds, and his conviction under general aggravated assault and specific intoxication assault statutes violated his right to due course of law under Tex. Const. art. I, § 19 and due process under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV, since both proscribed same conduct. The court vacated appellant's general conviction, holding specific intoxication assault statute prevailed over general statute; and affirmed his specific intoxication assault conviction because imposing convictions for both offenses involving same victim violated due process and due course of law, even when sentences were concurrent.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's general conviction, holding specific intoxication assault statute prevailed over general statute; and affirmed his specific intoxication assault conviction because imposing convictions for both offenses involving same victim violated due process and due course of law, even when sentences were concurrent.

State v. Boyd

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed orders dismissing prosecutions entered by the County Court at Law No. 2, Brazos County (Texas) in an action involving defendants charged with hazing in violation of Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 37.152(a)(4) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Two defendants were charged with failure to report a specific incident of hazing that occurred on a college campus in violation of Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 37.152(a)(4) (1996). PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 755,344.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the order of the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas, which found appellant guilty of knowingly using, redeeming, or transferring food stamp benefit permits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of knowingly using, redeeming, or transferring food stamp benefit permits, enhanced with two prior felony convictions, and assessed punishment at 25 years in prison. Appellant's conviction was affirmed on appeal. Specifically, the court held that evidence convicting appellant was legally sufficient where a special agent and an undercover officer testified appellant entered a store and obtained cash using an electronic benefit transfer card as prohibited by Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 33.011. Further, the court held that there was no evidence in the record to hold that trial counsel was ineffective for not filing a motion to quash the indictment. Finally, the court held that although it might have been error for the charge to combine offenses from both §§ 33.011(a) and (b), both offenses were valid violations of the code, and a finding of guilt pursuant to either section would have been proper.


OUTCOME: Judgment which found appellant guilty of knowingly using, redeeming, or transferring food stamp benefit permits was affirmed on the grounds that eyewitness testimony provided legally sufficient evidence to support jury verdict and there was no evidence that trial counsel was ineffective.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who was convicted of the offense of sexual assault of a child after a jury trial in the 114th Judicial District Court, Smith County (Texas), sought review from the automatic life sentence he received pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(c)(2) due to a prior conviction.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged a jury's finding of guilt, entered by the 198th Judicial District Court, Kerr County (Texas), in a case where he was charged with two counts of aggravated sexual assault.

The court held the testimony admissible because it was used to refute the psychiatrist's testimony that appellant was a nonviolent person.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the admission of prior assaults was not error, since such evidence was more probative than prejudicial and was used to rebut criminal appellant's defense that he was a very passive person who committed sex acts at the direction of his domineering wife.

Texas Natural Resource Conservation Comm'n v. Accord Agric., Inc.


NO. 03-98-00340-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6898



September 10, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-00159, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 17, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4472.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-profit Texas corporation and defendant Texas Natural Resource Conservation Commission cross-appealed the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District (Texas), declaring the rules promulgated by defendant invalid for failure to state a reasoned justification and striking plaintiff's takings and constitutional claims for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Texas Natural Resource Conservation Commission promulgated new rules regulating concentrated animal feeding operations (CAFOs), which effectively eliminated the right of a party adversely affected by CAFO-generated pollution to request a contested case hearing. Plaintiff non-profit corporation formed to protect property owners from CAFO-generated pollution challenged the rules in the district court, alleging that failure to provide a reasoned justification for the rules, a takings claim, and that the Right to Farm Act, Tex. Agric. Code Ann. § 251.004(a) (West 1982), was unconstitutional. The district court found the rules invalid as alleged, but held that plaintiff lacked standing to raise the other claims. The court affirmed, holding that plaintiff lacked standing to raise its takings claim since the relief requested, damages, required participation of its individual members. Further, defendant failed to substantially comply with the reasoned justification requirement since defendant's conclusory statements did not secure the legislative objectives underlying the requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the contested rules were invalid due to defendant's failure to provide a reasoned justification for the rules. Further, the district court properly struck plaintiff's takings claim and its challenge to the Right to Farm Act for want of jurisdiction since plaintiff lacked standing to bring them.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the County Criminal Court at Law, Harris County (Texas), where he was convicted of driving while intoxicated under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.04 (Vernon Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of nolo contendere to the offense of driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.04 (Vernon Supp. 1999). Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in failing to declare unconstitutional Tex. Transp. Code § 724.061 and in refusing to suppress evidence of the breath test refusal because of the warning officer's erroneous advice to defendant on the consequence of refusal. Cano v. State

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Defendant-appellants were convicted of delivery of a controlled substance. They appealed alleging multiple errors at the trial court level. OUTCOME: Court affirmed the convictions for delivery of a controlled substance because evidence was legally sufficient, evidence was factually sufficient, jury charge concerning delivery was not materially different from indictment, there was no need of corroboration of the "offer to sell" theory, the admission of extraneous offense evidence did not create incurable error that would justify a mistrial, and for other reasons.

Luquis v. State


NO. 09-98-535 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


997 S.W.2d 442; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6735


August 24, 1999, Submitted  
August 31, 1999, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 411th District Court. Polk County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 14,444.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 411th District Court, Polk County (Texas) with respect to its jury charge on punishment, contending that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to a portion of the jury charge on punishment and erred in denying his request that the jury charge on punishment include a definition and description of parole.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and was sentenced to life imprisonment. Appellant sought review of the trial court's jury charge on punishment. Appellant contended that the court erred in overruling his objection to a portion of the charge, describing the effect of good time credit, when appellant was not eligible to have good time credit counted towards his parole eligibility date. The appellate court first recognized that the Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) parole law instruction was required to be included in the charge. The appellate court then rejected the contention, concluding that nothing in the record suggested that the jury discussed, considered or tried to apply what they were told about good time and parole. Appellant also contended that the trial court erred in denying his request that the charge include a definition and description of parole. The appellate court rejected this contention, concluding that the purpose of the instruction was to admonish the jury that they were not to consider parole, and that the court did not have to define for the jury a concept which would not be considered in determining punishment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's rulings, which overruled appellant's objection to a portion of the jury charge on punishment and denied appellant's request that the jury charge on punishment include a definition and description of parole.

Stewart v. State


NO. 12-98-00288-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


39 S.W.3d 230; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 9672



August 31, 1999, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review January 3, 2000. Appellant's Petition for Rehearing Denied November 30, 1999.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 03/15/2000
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stewart v. Texas, 531 U.S. 857, 121 S. Ct. 140, 148 L. Ed. 2d 92, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5630 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 241ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction after an open plea of guilty in the 241st Judicial District Court, Smith County (Texas) for indecency with a child and contended that the indecency with a child statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for indecency with a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1). He contended that § 21.11 violated the due process provisions of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because it was vague and overbroad and that it infringed upon certain marital privacy rights protected by the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. This court disagreed and affirmed the conviction. Appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of the statute was limited to whether it was facially invalid because he did not make the challenge at trial. The court found that § 21.11(a)(1) did not implicate a marital privacy right protected by the First Amendment. The statute included intentionally engaging in sexual contact "with the child" and the court could not say that sexual activity in the presence of a child was constitutionally protected. Absent the implication of a First Amendment right, the overbreadth argument failed and appellant had to prove that the statute was vague in all of its applications. Appellant had already conceded that it was not unconstitutional as to him, thus his due process rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for indecency with a child because the statute did not violate appellant's constitutional rights and was not facially invalid.

Hines v. State


No. 06-98-00283-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


3 S.W.3d 618; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6514


August 24, 1999, Submitted  
August 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 23, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 76th Judicial District Court. Titus County, Texas Trial Court No. CR13,372.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 76th Judicial District Court, Titus County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of a lesser included offense of criminally negligent homicide. Appellant filed a motion for new trial alleging jury misconduct because the jurors discussed the effect and impact of parole laws on his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant indicted for manslaughter in the death of his common law wife was found guilty of the lesser included offense of criminally negligent homicide. Appellant filed a motion for new trial, alleging jury misconduct in that the jurors discussed the effect and impact of parole laws on his sentence. Appellant attached to his motion a juror's affidavit but no hearing was held on the motion and the motion was overruled by operation of law. Appellant contended the trial court abused its discretion in denying his motion for new trial. The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's decision when the court found that the controlling statute was Tex. R. Evid. 606(b), and that it was constitutional. The court held that jurors could testify only to whether any outside influence was brought to bear upon any juror. The court concluded that the affidavit did not reveal any outside influence that was brought to bear improperly on any juror. The juror's statement about the effect of parole on appellant's sentence were statements made by jurors during deliberations and thus emanated from inside the jury. The trial court correctly overruled appellant's motion.


OUTCOME: Appellate court affirmed lower court's decision that convicted appellant of criminally negligent homicide when court found that affidavit did not reveal any outside influence improperly brought to bear on any juror and that statements about effect of parole on appellant's sentence were made by jurors during deliberations and thus emanated from inside jury. The court concluded that the controlling rule of evidence was constitutional.

City of Houston v. Aspenwood Apt. Corp.


NO. 01-97-01378-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6721



August 27, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by, Motion denied by City of Houston v. Aspenwood Apt. Corp., 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 509 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., Jan. 24, 2002)
Petition for review denied by, 06/27/2002
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Yetiv v. City of Houston, 537 U.S. 1047, 123 S. Ct. 600, 154 L. Ed. 2d 520, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8722 (2002)
Related proceeding at Aspenwood Apt. Corp. v. Huey, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 3003 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., Apr. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 215th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9459707.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review from the 215th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which awarded damages and attorney fees to appellees, owner and corporation, for violations of42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and declared parts of appellant's building and rehabilitation ordinance unconstitutionally vague. Appellees, owner and corporation, sought review of a summary judgment on claims against appellee city officials in their individual capacities.


OVERVIEW: The court found no evidence supporting appellant city's liability for any employee's actions and reversed the lower court's judgment awarding appellees, owner and corporation, damages and attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellees failed to prove any unconstitutional custom approved by appellant's legislative body or final policymaker in the inspection of buildings and issuance of permits. Therefore, the trial judge erred in enjoining appellant's inspections of appellee's apartments based upon the jury's finding of § 1983 liability and the injunction issued by the lower court was dissolved. Appellees did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of appellant's building and rehabilitation code for as-applied vagueness and appellee's as-applied vagueness challenge to the remaining code sections, and the facial vagueness challenge to all of the building and rehabilitation code sections, failed as a matter of law. However, summary judgment was improperly rendered against each of appellee's claims against individual city officials because genuine issues of material fact were raised as to immunity and good faith.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court awarding appellees, owner and corporation, damages and attorney fees was reversed because appellant city had not approved any unconstitutional custom on the part of appellant's employees. The judgment of the lower court granting immunity to appellees, public officials, was reversed because there were genuine issues of triable fact as to good faith and immunity and remanded.

 

437 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Rylander v. 3 Beall Bros. 3, Inc.


NO. 03-98-00533-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


2 S.W.3d 562; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6330



August 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of July 15, 1999, Previously Reported at 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5146. Petition for Review Denied March 23, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 261ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-05710, HONORABLE HUME COFER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee in a franchise tax action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a retail corporation, ceased doing business in Texas. Pursuant to Tex. Tax Code § 171.0011, appellee was assessed an additional tax. Appellee initiated an action against appellant for a refund of the additional tax it paid on the grounds that § 171.0011 was unconstitutional because similarly situated taxpayers were treated differently based on their choice of accounting year. The court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment because the additional tax statute was constitutional. The statute did not violate the equal protection clause because the additional tax was assessed evenly. The tax amount was always based on a period of previously untaxed surplus. The tax was rationally related to the state's goal of raising revenue and mitigating the effects of corporate reorganizations. The tax, which was tied to appellee's earnings, was in proportion to appellee's activities in the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision granting appellee summary judgment and rendered judgment in favor of appellant. Appellee was liable for the additional tax because Tex. Tax Code § 171.0011 was constitutional. The statute operated equally within the relevant class and was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose.

St. Joseph Hosp. v. Wolff


NO. 03-97-00718-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


999 S.W.2d 579; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6358



August 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Granted May 25, 2000. As Amended October 14, 1999. Rehearing Overruled October 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 95-11336, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of a decision from the District Court of Travis County Texas, which, following a jury trial, entered a judgment in favor of appellee patient and family who brought a medical-malpractice action against appellant for the alleged negligent treatment of appellee by one its surgical residents.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital sought review of an adverse judgment in a suit brought by appellee patient and her family which asserted claims of medical malpractice against a surgical resident employed by appellant. The court affirmed the judgment and denied appellant's argument that the evidence was insufficient to support the jury's finding that appellant, and the foundation responsible for the placement of its surgical resident, engaged in a joint enterprise. The court held that the trial court, as a matter of law, properly defined joint enterprise, and that the evidence at trial sufficiently supported the jury's finding that the entities were engaged in a joint enterprise. The evidence supported the findings that two entities had a common purpose, shared a common business or pecuniary interest, and had an equal right to control the enterprise, the court found. The court found that appellant's liability as a participant in the joint enterprise was based on the resident's negligence as an employee of the foundation. The court rejected appellant's arguments under the borrowed-servant doctrine, sufficiency of the instructions, and admissibility of insurance evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee patient upon a finding that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding of a joint enterprise by which appellant hospital was liable for the claims of medical malpractice for the actions of its surgical resident.

At&T Corp. v. Rylander


NO. 03-98-00207-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


2 S.W.3d 546; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6360



August 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Denied December 7, 2000. Petition for Review Denied August 31, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-02005, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sued appellee, state comptroller, in the District Court of Travis County (Texas), following appellee's denial of appellant's claim for a refund of public utility assessments and gross receipts taxes paid. Appellant challenged the trial court's entry of judgment for appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant telephone company was denied a refund of public utility assessment and gross receipts taxes, and sued appellant state comptroller, alleging that the taxes were unconstitutionally imposed upon it, but not upon other similarly situated companies. The trial court held that the suit was barred by limitations, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that appellant's suit for refund of the assessments was untimely under the applicable limitations period and that it could not rely on compliance with an intervening change in the law altering the refund claim procedure. It further held that the discovery rule did not preclude appellee from asserting limitations, because the fact that appellant was the only company against which tax was assessed was not inherently undiscoverable. The court held that appellant did not meet the burden of showing the required elements of equitable estoppel or fraudulent concealment, because it did not conclusively establish that appellee engaged in false representations or concealment. The court also held that the claims to recover gross receipts taxes were barred by a settlement agreement entered into by the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for appellee comptroller, holding that appellant telephone company's claims for a refund of the assessments and gross receipts taxes were barred either by the applicable statute of limitations or by a settlement agreement of the parties, and that neither the discovery rule, the doctrines of equitable estoppel, nor fraudulent concealment precluded appellee from asserting the limitations defense.

City of Austin/Travis County Landfill Co. v. Travis County Landfill Co.


NO. 03-98-00455-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


25 S.W.3d 191; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6366



August 26, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Granted May 10, 2001. As Substituted October 12, 2000.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County Texas, which rendered it liable to appellee for taking, by overflights, the airspace over appellee's property, and appellee sought review of the denial of its request for a permanent injunction and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city sought review of a judgment holding it liable to appellee for taking the airspace over its property, and appellee challenged the denial of its motion to enjoin overflights pending the payment of compensation and by failing to award fees. The court affirmed the judgment and found that appellant's argument that federal height restrictions had long burdened appellee's land did not foreclose appellee's claim that its property was taken by physically intruding into the airspace above its land. The court found no merit in appellant's claim that appellee's overflight complaint was barred by the easement burdening its property, nor that its ordinance restricting the airspace around the airport was a valid exercise of its police power, and the court affirmed the award of damages. On appellee's claims, the court stated that a Texas state court may not assume authority over the airspace by issuing an injunction against further overflights under federal law and declined to hold that the trial court abused its discretion by denying a permanent injunction against further flights. Finally the court found no statutory authority for an award of attorney fees or expenses.


OUTCOME: Finding no merit in appellant's arguments, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which held appellant liable for a taking by overflights of appellee's property. Likewise, finding no merit in appellee's challenges, the court affirmed the denial of its motion for injunctive relief and fees.

Apex Towing Co. v. Tolin

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant clients challenged an order from the 58th District Court, Jefferson County, (Texas), in a take-nothing summary judgment in their legal malpractice suit against appellee law firm.


OVERVIEW: Appellee law firm represented appellant clients in a lawsuit. Appellants later discovered that they had a cause of action for legal malpractice against appellees. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees based on a two-year statute of limitations. Although appellants listed eight other contentions in their appeal, including alleged constitutional violations and failure of the judge to recuse himself, the contentions were overruled. The court noted that the constitutional violations were without argument or supporting authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment for appellee law firm because the cause of action for legal malpractice was barred by the two-year statute of limitations.

Johnson v. State


NUMBER 13-97-849-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6492



August 26, 1999, Delivered  
August 26, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 117th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 117th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was involved in a one-car accident and admitted to an officer that he had been drinking. After appellant failed a field sobriety test, a blood sample was taken and showed that appellant was intoxicated. Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. Appellant contended the court erred in admitting his statements to police and challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, which allowed evidence of appellant's prior offense of driving while intoxicated to be admitted during the punishment phase. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. Appellant's statements to police were proven by the alcohol level in his blood sample. Any error in admitting the statements was harmless. Article 37.07 was constitutional because the jury's consideration of a prior unconvicted offense did not constitute additional punishment and did not deprive appellant of liberty without due process. Article 37.07 provided jurors with information to make an appropriate determination of punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because the court did not err in admitting appellant's statements and evidence of a prior offense. Appellant's statements were proven by his blood sample, and the statute that allowed evidence of prior offenses to be admitted during the penalty phase was constitutional.

Smith v. Tilton


No. 05-96-00071-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


3 S.W.3d 77; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6435



August 25, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 101st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-05197-E. Trial Judge: Jay Patterson.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of summary judgment granted to appellee, a religious organization, by the 101st Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and her late husband watched television broadcasts of, received mail from, and became followers of appellees, a church and its pastor. Appellant filed suit against appellees, asserting tort and statutory causes of action arising from representations allegedly made by appellees: (1) in television marketing and mail prophesying cures and soliciting pledges; (2) in a mailing addressed to appellant's husband sent and received after his death that promised him a "miracle day;" and (3) in dunning letters asserting that appellant's husband, after his death, pledged contributions to the church. The trial court granted summary judgment against appellant on all counts. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the causes of action for fraud, negligent misrepresentation, and breach of fiduciary duty arising from representations made in the dun letters, holding that they were not constitutionally protected.

The court affirmed summary judgment on all other claims, holding they were constitutionally protected as free exercise of religion.

Penny v. State


NO. 14-97-00308-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6212



August 19, 1999, Rendered  
August 19, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9504112.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Harris County Criminal Court (Texas) that entered a conviction against him for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. His first trio of arguments claimed that a culpable mental state should have been required to support the conviction. The court noted that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.04 (1998) did not require a criminal or unlawful intent as an essential element of the offense. Appellant next contended that the trial court erred by overruling his motion for a continuance so that he could obtain discovery on the intoxilyzer. The court found no abuse of discretion where the appellant waited until the date that the case was set for trial to try to obtain the continuance, especially because appellant had two years to enforce the discovery order. Appellant's final argument was that the trial court erred when it admitted his videotaped police station interview because it did not contain the warnings required by Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.22, § 3(1), (2) (1999). When the videotape was played at trial, it had no sound, so the officer testified to what was on the tape. The court found that the videotape contained no statements because it had no sound. The court found that appellant preserved no error related to admissibility of the statements.


OUTCOME: The judgment that entered a conviction against appellant for driving while intoxicated was affirmed. The court rejected appellant's arguments that proof of a culpable mental state was required to support his conviction for driving while intoxicated because a criminal or unlawful intent was not an essential element of the offense. The court also found no error in the denial of a continuance or in admitting appellant's videotaped interview.

Blake v. State


No. 06-99-00020-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6052


August 16, 1999, Submitted  
August 17, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 124th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 26,029-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 124th Judicial District Court, Gregg County (Texas), sentencing him to 10 years' imprisonment for driving while intoxicated, subsequent offense. Appellant claimed that the sentence was disproportionate to the offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to driving while intoxicated, subsequent offense, and was sentenced to 10 years imprisonment; his punishment was enhanced by four misdemeanor convictions for driving while intoxicated. Appellant sought review of his sentence claiming that it was disproportionate to his offense. The court affirmed the sentence. The court first explained that appellant failed to preserve the issue for review by presenting the trial court a timely request, objection, or motion stating the specific grounds for the ruling desired, as required under Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a)(1)(A). Further, the court found that had appellant preserved the issue for appeal, the punishment was not disproportionate under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Using the first factor of the Solem test, the court compared the gravity of the offense against the severity of the sentence and determined that the sentence was within the range of punishment prescribed by the legislature for the crime and that it was not disproportionate to the offense or appellant given his record and his repeated offenses. Accordingly, it was not necessary for the court to reach the remaining Solem factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's 10 year sentence for driving under the influence, subsequent offense, explaining that he failed to preserve the proportionality of his sentence for appeal as required under state rules of appellate procedure. Further, the sentence was within the range of punishment prescribed by the legislature for the crime and it was not disproportionate to the offense, given appellant's record of repeated offenses.
