Williams v. State


No. 06-99-00011-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6053


August 16, 1999, Submitted  
August 17, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 188th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 25,512-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted for the offense of possession of a controlled substance, crack cocaine, between one and four grams, with intent to deliver, sought review of the judgment of the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County, Texas, which sentenced her to 12 years' imprisonment. Appellant argued on appeal that the sentence was disproportionate to her offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for the offense of possession of a controlled substance, crack cocaine, between one and four grams, with intent to deliver. She was sentenced to 12 years' imprisonment. Appellant argued on appeal that her 12-year sentence was disproportionate to her offense. The court first noted that appellant had failed to preserve the alleged error for review. Even if appellant had properly preserved the alleged error for review, the court found that her sentence did not amount to the imposition of a disproportionate sentence under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The court concluded that appellant's sentence was not grossly disproportionate to the offense because appellant's sentence was within the range of punishment prescribed by the state legislature for the crime, because appellant had previously been placed on community supervision for possession of a controlled substance, because she had failed to complete community supervision for misdemeanor criminal mischief, because she refused to accept responsibility for her actions, and because rehabilitation was unlikely. Therefore, appellant's contention of error was overruled and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's 12-year imprisonment sentence for the offense of possession of a controlled substance, crack cocaine, between one and four grams, with intent to deliver, was affirmed on appeal after the court concluded that the sentence had not been grossly disproportionate to the offense.

In re Wiese


NUMBER 13-99-268-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1 S.W.3d 246; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5988



August 12, 1999, Delivered  
August 12, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Granted Wiese's petition for writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator applied for a writ of habeas corpus after a contempt and commitment order was issued in connection with a turnover order. In her petition, relator claimed that the contempt order was void as being unconstitutional, and she contended that the turnover order was unenforceable by contempt in that it made no provision for the deduction of reasonable and necessary business expenses.


OVERVIEW: Relator applied for a writ of habeas corpus after a contempt and commitment order was issued in connection with a turnover order. Relator argued the contempt order was void as being unconstitutional, and she contended the turnover order was unenforceable by contempt because it made no provision for the deduction of reasonable and necessary business expenses. The court held that the contempt order was void, and ordered relator discharged. The court found that the automatic stay of the underlying bankruptcy proceeding applied only to the civil contempt provision, and that the court could review the merits of relator's writ of habeas corpus related to the criminal contempt. The court determined that the terms of the turnover order made the judgment merely voidable. However, the contemptuous conduct the justice court found was relator's failure to pay funds into the registry of the court on a daily basis. A portion of those funds included attorney fees that were part of the turnover order. Because Texas law did not allow collection of attorney fees by contempt proceedings, the court held that the entire order was void, and that as a result, relator was illegally restrained.


OUTCOME: Relator's petition for writ of habeas corpus was granted. Texas law did not allow for collection of attorney fees by contempt proceedings. Because the collection of attorney fees was not punishable by contempt, the entire judgment was void. Accordingly, the order illegally restrained relator, therefore, the writ was issued, relator was discharged, and her bond was released.

Jordan v. State


NO. 01-98-00623-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5771



August 5, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted March 22, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 765804.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea agreement, appellant pled guilty to robbery, and the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, deferred adjudication of his guilt and placed him on deferred-adjudication community supervision for six years. The state filed a motion to adjudicate appellant's guilt based upon his alleged possession of cocaine, the trial court adjudicated his guilt and sentenced him to 16 years in prison, and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to robbery, and the trial court deferred adjudication of his guilt and placed him on deferred-adjudication community supervision for six years. The state sought to adjudicate appellant's guilt based upon his alleged cocaine possession, the trial court adjudicated his guilt and sentenced him to 16 years in prison, and appellant challenged. The court held that it could not address appellants' claims that his plea was not voluntary and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because a defendant placed on community supervision was required to appeal issues relating to pleas and pretrial motions when community supervision was imposed; the defendant could not challenge such issues for the first time in an appeal from the trial court's revocation of his community supervision. The court further held that pursuant to Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b), appellant could not challenge the trial court's determination to proceed with an adjudication of guilt, and that art. 42.12, § 5(b) did not violate equal protection guarantees or the Open Courts Clause of the Texas Constitution. The lower court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, holding that it could not address appellant's claims that his plea was not voluntary and that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress; that appellant could not challenge the trial court's determination to proceed with an adjudication of guilt, and that the statute prohibiting such challenge did not violate equal protection or the Open Courts Clause of the Texas Constitution.

Rodriguez v. State


NO. 14-99-00158-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5804



August 5, 1999, Rendered  
August 5, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 806090.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from her conviction for failing to report child abuse, from the 262nd District Court, Harris County's (Texas) denial of relief sought through application for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review from her conviction for failing to report child abuse, from the lower court's denial of relief sought through application of a writ of habeas corpus. On appeal, the matter was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. In support of its ruling, the court held that where a premise of a habeas corpus application was destroyed by subsequent developments, the legal issues raised were rendered moot. The court noted that while appellant sought relief from what she alleged as an unlawful prosecution, because the prosecution had gone forward to conviction, the issue presented was rendered moot. The court, noting that habeas corpus could not be used as a substitute for appeal, further held that appellant had raised an issue that may have been suitable for consideration on appeal of her conviction. The court concluded that appellant had an adequate remedy at law in that her constitutional issue may be raised on direct appeal of her conviction.


OUTCOME: The matter was demised for lack of jurisdiction as the issue presented by appellant was rendered moot because the prosecution had gone forward to conviction.

Scolaro v. State ex rel. Jones


NO. 07-99-0064-CV, NO. 07-99-0100-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 72ND DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NOS. 98-503,598-A and B; HONORABLE BILL MCCOY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed judgments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 72nd District Court of Lubbock County (Texas) granting partial summary judgment in favor of appellee for removing appellant as a county judge for failing to satisfy practice requirement pursuant to Tex. Govt. Code Ann. § 25.0014(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was admitted to the practice of law in Texas and, about four years later, she voluntarily assumed inactive status. Thereafter, appellant changed her status to an active member. Appellant was elected as a judge of a county court of the state. The court held that it was the practice of the state bar to destroy documents after one year. It held that payment by appellant of her active bar dues did not have retroactive effect. The court affirmed the order of the lower court granting partial summary judgment in favor of appellee.


OUTCOME: An order granting partial summary judgment in favor of appellee was affirmed because payment by appellant of her active bar dues after she had been inactive was not retroactive. Thus, her removal as county judge was proper.

Dunn v. State


No. 10-98-023-CR, No. 10-98-024-CR, No. 10-98-025-CR, No. 10-98-026-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


997 S.W.2d 885; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5719



August 4, 1999, Delivered  
August 4, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 87th District Court. Freestone County, Texas. Trial Court Nos. 88-034-CR, 88-035-CR, 88-036-CR, & 88-038-CR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 87th District Court, Freestone County (Texas) that revoked most of appellant's probation terms on the charge of theft of property, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(A) (Supp. 1999), that reduced the term of appellant's confinement in each case, and that sentenced appellant accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to charges of theft of property, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(A). Under the plea agreement, the guilt adjudication was deferred, and appellant was placed on deferred probation. Subsequently, appellant's guilt was adjudicated, and appellant received prison sentences. Later, probation on most of the charges was reduced, appellant's confinement was reduced in each case, and appellant was sentenced. Appellant sought review of the sentences. On appeal, the court stated that appellant only challenged some of the court findings. The court held that the probation revocations were not an abuse of discretion because only one probation violation was required. Furthermore, the sentences were not illegal because the 10-year cap on probation imposed by Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. art. 42.12, § 3 did not apply to deferred adjudication probations, and § 5(b) allowed punishment of appellant regardless of the time that appellant served on the deferred adjudication. Finally, the sentences were not cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII because the sentences were not grossly disproportionate to the offenses. Therefore, judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that sentenced appellant on reduced terms of confinement for appellant's charge of theft after appellant's deferred probation was revoked because the probation revocations were not an abuse of discretion, and the sentences were not statutorily illegal. Furthermore, the sentences did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because the sentences were not grossly disproportionate to the offenses.

Adams v. Baxter Healthcare Corp.


NO. 03-98-00323-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


998 S.W.2d 349; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5530



July 29, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 98TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-06361, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; Appeal of Melba Hyde Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant/appellee residents sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Travis County 98th Judicial District (Texas) that dismissed their claims brought for injuries caused by breast implants. Appellant/appellee company and doctor appealed the condition imposed by the court before granting the dismissal of residents' claims.


OVERVIEW: Appellants/appellees Illinois and Indiana residents joined with Texas residents in an action against appellants/appellees company and doctor alleging claims of products liability, breach of express and implied warranties, negligence, and other claims. Company moved to sever residents' claims and offered a stipulation not to pursue certain defenses if residents were severed. The trial court granted company's forum non conveniens motions but required company to waive any and all defenses based on the statutes of limitations, pursuant to former Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.051(c). Both parties appealed. Residents argued that because their claims arose out of the same series of transactions or occurrences as the Texas residents' claims and because there were common issues of law or fact, the trial court erred in severing their claims. The court affirmed the judgment against residents because distinct factual scenarios would tend to confuse the jury. As to company's appeal, the court found that § 71.051 of the forum non conveniens statute was clear and unambiguous and that company was required to "waive any defense" based on the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant/appellee residents' claims because confusion would result by allowing the residents from Indiana and Illinois to try their claims with the Texas residents. The court affirmed the judgment that made appellant/appellee company and doctor waive defenses because the lower court's order was consistent with the plain meaning of the forum non conveniens statute.

Smith v. Tarrant County Bail Bond Bd.


NO. 2-99-108-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


997 S.W.2d 870; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5640



July 29, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 48TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 48th District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which reviewed de novo, and affirmed, appellee bail bond board's refusal to grant appellant a license that would have let him be the agent for a bail bondsman the board had licensed in Tarrant County.


OVERVIEW: The district court reviewed by trial de novo appellee bail bond board's refusal to grant appellant a license to be an agent for a licensed bail bondsman. The trial court concluded that appellee had properly denied the agent's license to appellant. Appellant complained on appeal that the judgment was not supported by legally or factually sufficient evidence and was an abuse of discretion. The court found that the provisions of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372p-3 exclusively governed the licensing procedure for bail bondsmen and their agents, and it made any person convicted of a felony ineligible for licensing. Since there was more than a scintilla of evidence that appellant was a convicted felon and upholding the legislature's intent to not license felons was not manifestly unjust, the trial court's decision was supported by both legally and factually sufficient evidence, and no abuse of discretion occurred.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; appellant was unable to obtain a license as an agent for a bail bondsman because he was a convicted felon and thus was ineligible for licensing under applicable state statute.

Phelps v. State


No. 11-97-00258-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


999 S.W.2d 512; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5690



July 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 35th District Court of Brown County.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the 35th District Court of Brown County (Texas) that convicted him of injury to a child pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 and sentenced him to sixty years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of injury to a child. In his eleventh, twelfth, and thirteenth points of error, appellant argued that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the verdict. The indictment alleged that appellant intentionally and knowingly caused serious bodily injury to a child younger than fifteen years of age by striking her in the head with his hand. The jury charge tracked the language of the indictment. Appellee State of Texas did not offer any evidence that appellant used his hands to commit the crime. In caselaw, the sufficiency of the evidence was measured by the elements of the offense as defined by a "hypothetically correct" jury charge for the case. The manner and means "by striking her in the head with his hand" was not an element of the offense. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Applying caselaw rationale, the court held that the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to show that appellant committed the crime of injury to a child as measured by a hypothetically correct jury charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found appellant guilty of injury to a child because evidence was sufficient to show that appellant committed the crime as measured by a hypothetically correct jury charge.

Perez v. State


No. 05-98-01288-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5468



July 23, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MA98-14213-B.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 2. Dallas County (Texas), which found the defendant guilty of carrying an illegal knife and assessed a one-day sentence and a $ 10 fine.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court found the defendant guilty of carrying an illegal knife and assessed a one-day sentence and a $ 10 fine. The defendant appealed and argued that the definition of illegal knife was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, and the trial court erred in including the knife's tang in determining the blade's length. The court held that to preserve an attack on the constitutionality of a statute as applied to the defendant for appellate review, the defendant must raise his complaint in the trial court. Failure to raise the issue before the trial court waived the court's review. As to the defendant's second point of error the court held that the defendant's brief must contain a clear and concise argument for the contentions made, with appropriate citation to authorities and to the record. The failure to cite legal authority or to present a legal theory preserved nothing for review. Tex. R. App. P. 38.1(h).The defendant failed to cite to any authority or propound any legal theory, and the court overruled the defendant's second point of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which found the defendant guilty of carrying an illegal knife because the defendant failed to raise the issue of vagueness in the trial court, and therefore he waived the right of appellate review of the constitutionality of that statute as applied to him.

Post-conviction relief denied at Ex parte Estrada, 2004 Tex. App. LEXIS 11150 (Tex. App. Dallas, Dec. 13, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ex parte Estrada, 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 7950 (Tex. App. Dallas, Oct. 13, 2009)
Subsequent appeal at, Appeal dismissed by Estrada v. State, 2014 Tex. App. LEXIS 8561 (Tex. App. Dallas, Aug. 6, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 3. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. F93-26578-PJ and F93-26577-PJ.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of February 4, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 688.
Estrada v. State, 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 688 (Tex. App. Dallas, Feb. 4, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in cause number F93-26578-PJ, REVERSED and REMANDED in cause number F93-26577-PJ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a motion for rehearing of his conviction by the Criminal district Court No. 3, Dallas County (Texas) for sexual assault and aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of sexual assault of a child and aggravated sexual assault of a child under the age of 14. He agreed to enter a plea of nolo contendere in exchange for community supervision and deferred adjudication. Appellant was later found to be in violation of his community supervision agreement and his agreement was revoked. He subsequently filed a motion for rehearing asserting that his plea was involuntary, that the community supervision condition was unconstitutional, that the state did not prove he had violated any law, and that he received ineffective assistance. The court dismissed the plea allegation, and the unconstitutionality allegation for lack of jurisdiction, and found the confession was voluntary. The court noted, however, that the lower court had allowed inadmissible hearsay within hearsay into evidence. Because defense counsel failed to object to the inadmissible hearsay evidence, and because that evidence was the only evidence upon which a revocation could have been based, the court held that appellant's counsel was ineffective and reversed the decision on the sexual assault issue while affirming the decision on aggravated sexual assault.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction on aggravated sexual assault was affirmed, but the conviction on sexual assault was reversed because defense counsel neglected to object to the hearsay evidence admitted upon which the revocation of his community supervision was based.

Green v. State


NO. 2-98-553-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


999 S.W.2d 474; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5376



July 22, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 3 OF DENTON COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed for want of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment by the County Criminal Court No. 3 of Denton County (Texas) denying appellant the relief sought in his pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with evading detention and filed a pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus alleging that the provision under which he was charged, Tex. Penal Code § 38.04 (1994), was unconstitutionally vague. Appellant then entered into a plea-bargain agreement. The court found that appellant's notice of appeal was untimely and did not invoke the court's appellate jurisdiction regarding the trial court's order on the pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus, but that appellant's notice of appeal was timely regarding the final judgment entered. Because appellant entered into a plea bargain, he had to meet the special notice requirements of Tex. R. App. P. 25.2(b)(3), so in order to appeal his conviction, appellant's notice had to truthfully state that the substance of his appeal was raised by written motion and ruled on before trial. The court found that appellant's notice did not meet this requirement because the pretrial habeas corpus application was not a "written motion" as contemplated in rule 25.2(b)(2). Therefore, the court held that appellant failed to invoke the court's jurisdiction over the judgment and sentence in the case.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed and held that any purported appeal from the order denying habeas relief was untimely and appellant otherwise failed to invoke the court's appellate jurisdiction.

Meadows v. State


NO. 01-98-00373-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


998 S.W.2d 318; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5387



July 22, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [**1] PUBLISHED IN PART.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 672,039.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 176th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of sexual assault and granted appellee's motion to cumulate thereby ordering that appellant's sentence was to begin after the completion of his life sentence for a prior murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. The jury assessed punishment at confinement for life. Thereupon, the trial court granted appellee's motion to cumulate and ordered that appellant's sentence was to begin after the completion of his life sentence for a prior murder conviction. Appellant raised various contentions on appeal, contending that the trial court erred in allowing the complainant to testify that another person sexually assaulted her at the behest of appellant. The court held that the trial court, in determining whether to deem evidence relevant to sentencing and thus admissible under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a), should apply Tex. Rs. Evid. 401, 402, and 403. The court found that because appellant objected to the testimony under rule 403, the trial court had to weigh the testimony's probativeness to see if it was substantially outweighed by the potential for unfair prejudice. Since the evidence was clearly probative as to the aggravated circumstances of the offense, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the testimony. The court overruled the other various claims raised by appellant as well.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for sexual assault because the trial court did conduct a balancing of the probativeness and prejudicial effect of the complainant's testimony in its ruling on admissibility.

Kubosh v. City of Houston


NO. 01-98-00933-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


2 S.W.3d 463; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5395



July 22, 1999, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied March 23, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 113th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 98-16236.



DISPOSITION: Reverse and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the order of the 113th District Court, Harris County, Texas, granting appellee's motion for summary judgment in appellants' action for a declaratory judgment that appellee assessed an unauthorized warrant fee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant suspects were assessed a warrant fee by appellee city but were never convicted. Appellants alleged that the fee was statutorily authorized only if appellants were convicted. Appellants filed a declaratory judgment action against appellee for unauthorized assessment of warrant fees. Appellee sought summary judgment and alleged that appellants' claims were barred by the statute of limitations and were moot, that appellee was immune, and that appellants failed to request a refund. Appellants sought partial summary judgment. The trial court granted appellee's motion. On appeal the court reversed and held that genuine issues of material fact existed. Appellee failed to establish when one appellant paid the fee and, therefore, that the statute of limitations barred the action. Appellee was not immune because the charging of unauthorized fees was not the implementation of policy decisions on how to collect taxes. Appellants' claims were not moot because there was no evidence that appellee changed the policy. Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 103.008 was not the exclusive remedy for a refund. Appellants failed to show that the action was filed within the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the granting of summary judgment to appellee in appellants' declaratory judgment action for the unauthorized assessment of warrant fees and held that appellee failed to establish that the statute of limitations barred the action, that appellee did not have immunity, that the action was not moot, and that a state statute was not the exclusive means to obtain a refund.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 183rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of a child on a plea of no contest and sentenced him to 20 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction, after a plea of no contest, for aggravated sexual assault of a child. Holmes v. State


NUMBER 13-97-828-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5450



July 22, 1999, Delivered  
July 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 183rd District Court of Harris County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 183rd District Court of Harris County (Texas) for aggravated assault. Defendant alleged that he received ineffective assistance of counsel and that the jury was improperly charged.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated assault and held that defendant's counsel rendered effective assistance. Defendant had raised several issues on appeal, and the court overruled all of them. First, the court held that evidence of defendant's post-offense conduct was admissible because it met the exceptions to Tex. R. Evid. 404(b), 401, 402, and 403's general bar against extraneous evidence. Defendant had locked himself in his home and threatened the police, which was highly probative of his state of mind following the offense. Second, the court held that because this evidence was admissible, defendant's counsel's failure to object to the evidence did not fall below the standard of reasonable competence. The court ruled that defendant was unable to prove that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because he failed to satisfy the two-pronged test of Strickland, and counsel's actions were part of his strategy. Third, the court found that the jury's charge contained improper language, but held that it was a harmless error because when the charge was read in its entirety, it was unlikely the jury relied solely on the objectionable portion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of aggravated assault was affirmed. The court held that defendant failed to show that his counsel was ineffective; defense counsel's failure to object to post-offense evidence was irrelevant because it met the exception to the general bar against extraneous evidence. The court found that the jury's charge contained improper language, but held that it was harmless because it was unlikely that the jury relied solely on it.

State v. Stephens


No. 05-96-00844-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5366



July 21, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 1. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 1-82370-93.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state, sought review of the decision from the County Court at Law No. 1. Dallas County (Texas) to sustain appellee's motion to suppress evidence that police had found while searching appellee's car.


OVERVIEW: Officers had placed a "Drug Check Point" sign along a freeway. Appellee took an earlier exit and the officers stopped him. He consented to a search and the officers found marihuana. At trial, appellee moved to suppress the evidence. The trial court sustained the evidence concluding the police obtained evidence by violating a statute prohibiting putting unauthorized signs on a state highway right-of-way. Appellant sought review of the trial court's decision to sustain the motion. Appellant argued that even if the initial stop was an unconstitutional detention, it was brief and had ceased to exist at the time of appellee's consent to search, thereby attenuating any taint. The court found that the trial court could have properly concluded the officers' action of placing the "Drug Check Point" sign along the freeway was illegal conduct triggering Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.23. Because the contraband was discovered by exploitation of the primary illegality, and not by means sufficiently distinguishable to purge the primary taint, the trial court properly granted appellee's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to sustain a motion to suppress evidence because the evidence was illegally obtained.

In re C.E.M.


No. 05-98-01866-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5326



July 19, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 304th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. JD-44063-W.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from the 304th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), finding he engaged in delinquent conduct by committing a first degree felony, specifically by intentionally or knowingly causing the sexual organ of a child to contact his mouth pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(1)(B)(iii), (a)(2)(B). Petitioner was assessed a determinate sentence of fifteen years, and committed to the Texas Youth Commission.


OVERVIEW: A jury found petitioner engaged in delinquent conduct by committing a first degree felony, specifically by intentionally or knowingly causing the sexual organ of a child to contact his mouth in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(1)(B)(iii), (a)(2)(B). Following a disposition hearing, the jury found petitioner to be in need of rehabilitation, assessed a determinate sentence of fifteen years, and committed him to the Texas Youth Commission. Petitioner contended the trial court erred in denying his motion for directed verdict, and the evidence was factually insufficient to support his delinquency adjudication. Petitioner argued it was alleged he caused the sexual organ of the victim to contact his mouth, but the evidence showed he used his tongue. He argued that by definition the tongue was not the mouth, and, further, the penal code made contact by tongue an offense of indecency with a child, not aggravated sexual assault. The court found that the legislature intended the word "mouth" to include its parts such as the teeth and tongue. The court rejected petitioner's argument and affirmed the judgment below.


OUTCOME: The court overruled petitioner's issues and affirmed the judgment below. The court concluded that a reasonable trier of fact could have found the elements of the offense of aggravated sexual assault beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, the court concluded the trial court did not err in denying petitioner's motion for a directed verdict.

University of Tex. at Arlington v. Bishop


NO. 2-98-274-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


997 S.W.2d 350; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5160



July 15, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied August 24, 2000. Rehearing Denied August 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 141ST DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 141st District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which awarded a private attorney attorney's fees and expenses out of a self-insured governmental entity's worker's compensation subrogation lien and sanctioned appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant university was a self-insured government entity. Appellant challenged a court order which awarded attorney's fees and expenses to be paid out of appellant's subrogated interest in the proceeds in the court's registry to the private attorney who represent appellee, appellant's former employee, in a third-party claim and sanctioned appellant. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court rejected appellant's argument that the legislature had not clearly waived immunity of state agencies for suits apportioning attorney's fees in third-party actions. Under Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 417.001(b), 417.002(a) (Vernon 1996), the legislature clearly intended self-insured governmental entities to pay attorney's fees and expenses out of an entity's subrogation lien. The statute did not interfere with the attorney general's exclusive constitutional duty to represent the state's interests. The findings of fact supplied the particularities on the sanctioned conduct lacking in the trial court's order. Since appellant failed to bring forth the record from the hearing on the motion for sanctions, the court presumed the trial court had sufficient evidence to support its findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order awarding attorney fees and expenses and sanctioning appellant because the labor code provided for self-insured governmental entities to pay attorney's fees and expenses, and findings of fact supplies particularities lacking in the trial court's order on the basis for sanctions.

Kirschner v. State


NO. 03-97-00786-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


997 S.W.2d 335; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5198



July 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR-95-172, HONORABLE CHARLES E. (CHUCK) MILLER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of conviction for misapplying real estate trust funds under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. §§ 162.031(a) and .032(b), in appellee's favor, in the District Court of Hays County, 22nd Judicial District (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant contractor sought review of conviction for misapplying real property trust funds under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. §§ 162.031(a) and .032(b). Appellant used money deposited for construction on costs other than overhead. The court first rejected appellant's argument that because appellee state included a former statutory exception of use of the funds for non-overhead costs, this particular use became an element of the crime required to be proved at trial. The court explained, under the present statute, the use of the funds to pay actual expenses was an affirmative defense, not a statutory exception. The court noted an unnecessary allegation that did not describe an essential element did not need to be proved at trial. The court further found the sufficiency of evidence for purposes of the verdict was to be measured by the hypothetical correct jury charge and not against the actual charge given as in the present case where the unnecessary element was incorporated into the charge. The court found appellee sufficiently proved appellant diverted funds. The court found that although the case was delayed an inordinate amount of time, much delay was attributable to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for misapplying real property trust funds because appellee state sufficiently proved the essential elements of the offense and was not required to prove an unnecessary description of an affirmative defense contained in the indictment and jury charge. The court found any delay in a speedy trial was attributable in large part to appellant who later did not vigorously assert his speedy trial right.

Hixson v. State


NUMBER 13-97-288-CR, 13-97-349-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1 S.W.3d 160; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5302



July 15, 1999, Delivered  
July 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 28th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) that convicted him of felony driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with felony driving while intoxicated and filed a pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus, which was denied. Defendant was subsequently convicted as charged, and appealed the conviction and denial of his habeas writ. In affirming, the appellate court held that Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. § 28.061 (1999) infringed upon the prosecution's right to obtain an indictment by setting a certain time period; therefore, the statute was found to be unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine. The court held that because the statute was unconstitutional, the state was not barred from prosecuting defendant beyond the statute's time period. The court also ruled that a complaint of untimely indictment must be preserved by a pre-indictment objection. Because defendant failed to preserve his complaint of untimely indictment, he was not entitled to dismissal of the charges against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the statute placing a time limit on the prosecution with respect to bringing a defendant out on bail to trial was found to be unconstitutional as it violated the separation of power doctrine. The court also ruled that defendant did not preserve his complaint of untimely indictment for review.

Smith v. State


NUMBER 13-97-512-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


998 S.W.2d 683; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5303



July 15, 1999, Delivered  
July 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 5, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 144th District Court of Bexar County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of denial of petition for writ of habeas corpus on aggravated robbery conviction, in appellee's favor, in Bexar County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of conviction for aggravated robbery and the denial of discretionary review through a petition for writ of habeas corpus. The court first rejected appellant's argument that the trial court erred in denying his motion to sever. The court found no abuse of discretion when the jury was properly admonished to consider a co-defendant's sexual assault only against the co-defendant. The court further noted during closing argument the jury was further cautioned about considering the testimony in determining punishment against the co-defendant against whom it was admitted only. The court found evidence of prior conviction was properly admitted against appellant in the punishment phase when exhibits of fingerprints were properly identified. The court explained, although the procedure was unorthodox, the prosecution was cautioned that a new punishment trial would be granted in the event appellant's identification was not proven. The court found the denial of appellant's petition for discretionary review was proper when appellant waited nine months before he complained of an untimely indictment. The court found, as a result, that appellant's complaints were waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's robbery conviction and the denial of discretionary review through petition for writ of habeas corpus, in appellees' favor, because denial of appellant's motion to sever was proper when jury was properly admonished to consider testimony against a co-defendant only, prior conviction evidence was properly admitted, and speedy indictment issue was waived by appellant's failure to raise it sooner.

Rylander v. B&A Mktg. Co.


NO. 03-98-00563-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


997 S.W.2d 326; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 7782



July 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-01522, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), granting summary judgment for appellee in appellee's action seeking a refund of additional tax paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation was assessed an additional tax under Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 171.001-.687, which allowed for the assessment of a prospective franchise tax on corporations incorporated in or doing business in Texas. The franchise tax statute was amended to include "earned surplus," but not on companies whose only contacts with a state were solicitation of sales of tangible personal property such as a mail order business. Those companies that were not allowed to be assessed an earned surplus tax were assessed an additional tax under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.0011(a) (1992). Appellee was dissolved in 1992 and did not pay the prospective tax for 1993 but was assessed one anyway. Appellee paid under protest and filed suit to recover. Appellant state challenged the granting of appellee's summary judgment motion, arguing that the statute was not limited to companies who simply reorganized but applied to companies undergoing various types of changes, including dissolution. The court agreed with appellant and found that the statute was rationally related to a legitimate state interest and therefore constitutional. The court then reversed the granting of summary judgment for appellee.


OUTCOME: The granting of summary judgment for appellee was reversed and judgment entered for appellant because the corporation could be assessed an additional tax even after dissolution and the statute enabling this assessment was constitutional.

GTE Southwest, Inc. v. PUC


NO. 03-97-00148-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


10 S.W.3d 7; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5199



July 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion as Amended February 17, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-09155, HONORABLE SUZANNE COVINGTON, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Dissenting Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Dissenting Opinion of July 15, 1999.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), which affirmed appellee Public Utility Commission's order requiring appellant to revise its tariff to include the surrender of its property for use by the property owners.


OVERVIEW: Appellant installed and owned cables and equipment necessary to supply local exchange telephone service to large apartment complexes. Third parties complained to appellee Public Utility Commission that appellant had violated its tariff and appellant's internal guidelines by refusing to collapse its multiple demarcation points into a single point. Appellee ordered appellant to revise its tariff to allow for the surrender of its property for use by property owners. Appellant sought review of appellee's order, which the lower court affirmed. This appeal followed. The court concluded appellee's order amounted to a physical or per se taking of appellant's cables and facilities by requiring that appellant surrender its right to exclude others from physical use of its properties. The court then sought to determine whether appellee possessed the statutory power to issue such an order. The court found the issue was not whether appellee possessed a general power to take private property, but whether the particular action claimed to be a taking in this case was authorized by statute. The court ruled that appellee lacked the statutory power to issue such an order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court and remanded the controversy to appellee Public Utility Commission because the court found that appellee's order amounted to a physical or per se taking of appellant's cables and facilities by requiring that appellant surrender its right to exclude others from physical use of its properties and that appellee lacked the statutory power to take appellant's property.

Jacobs v. State


NO. 14-97-00622-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5016



July 8, 1999, Rendered  
July 8, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 737,245.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a judgment from the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of murder and sentencing him to 50 years in prison, on grounds that the lower court erred in instructing the jury on good-conduct time and that Tex. Penal Code § 19.02(d) and Tex. Code Crim. P. art 37.07, § 4 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 50 years in prison. Defendant appealed the conviction on grounds that the lower court erred in instructing the jury on good-conduct time, and also challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code § 19.02(d) (§ 19.02) and Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 37.07, § 4 (art. 37). Defendant raised the § 19.02 issue for the first time on appeal and waived its review; however, the court found that defendant did not show how § 19.02 was unconstitutional as applied in his case. Section 19.02 allowed defendant to show that he murdered the victim out of sudden passion as a means to reduce the degree of the felony, but did not unconstitutionally compel defendant to incriminate himself. The court also found that the jury instruction did not misstate the law under art. 37. The charge clearly informed the jury that any good-conduct time defendant earned could not reduce his sentence until he served half of his sentence. Although defendant did not preserve his separation of powers challenge, the court found that art. 37 conformed to Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a) because it allowed courts to inform juries about the effect of good-conduct time.


OUTCOME: Criminal defendant's murder conviction was affirmed because the lower court's jury instruction regarding the effect of good-conduct time on defendant's sentence conformed to statutory and constitutional requirements, and defendant did not properly preserve issues for the court's review.

 

473 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ZOOK


NO. 14-98-00611-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5017



July 8, 1999, Rendered  
July 8, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 32,944.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed an order from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County (Texas), which dismissed appellee's re-indictment for the offense of felony criminal mischief.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with engaging in organized criminal activity by an indictment. Thereafter, he was reindicted for felony criminal mischief. The trial court dismissed appellant's reindictment on the ground that it was not filed within the second term of the grand jury, and as such violated Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32.01 (1997). On appeal, the prosecution contended that art. 32.01 only required that a defendant be indicted within the second term of the grand jury from the time of his arrest. Here, appellee was indicted before the second term of the grand jury in the original indictment. Therefore, art. 32.01 was not violated by the indictment. The court agreed. It concluded that art. 32.01 did not preclude prosecution from advancing alternative theories or charges arising out of the same criminal transaction once the prosecution had acted within the timetable prescribed by art. 32.01 for initially securing an indictment. Further, because appellee was indicted prior to the motion being heard, art. 32.01 could not be used to dismiss the indictment, even though it was returned by a grand jury at a subsequent term of court. The court reversed and remanded the action for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of appellant's reindictment for felony criminal mischief because the trial court incorrectly applied the statute. The statute did not preclude the prosecution from advancing an alternative charge arising out of appellant's same criminal transaction once the prosecution had acted within the timetable prescribed by the statute for securing the original indictment.

Healthhelp Servs. Group, Inc. v. Iskcon Asset Managment


NO. 14-97-01300-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5020



July 8, 1999, Rendered  
July 8, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled June 15, 2000. Petition for Review Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction April 13, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Civil Court at Law No. 1. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 681057.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Vacated, Case Ordered Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants appealed a judgment from the County Civil Court at Law No. 1, Harris County (Texas), granting defendant landlord's writ of certiorari, dismissing plaintiffs' reentry action, declaring Tex. Prop. Code § 93.003 unconstitutional, and awarding defendant's attorney fees against plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: When plaintiff tenants sought defendant landlord's consent to assign their lease, defendant locked plaintiffs out of the space. Plaintiffs filed a writ of reentry action in justice court pursuant to Tex. Prop. Code § 93.003 (§ 93.003). Defendant sought review of the writ of reentry by writ of certiorari to the lower court. The lower court granted the writ, dismissed plaintiffs' reentry action, declared § 93.003 unconstitutional, and awarded defendant attorney fees. On appeal, the court noted that neither party could assert new claims or causes of action in the lower court that had not been asserted in the justice court. If defendant did nothing more than resist plaintiffs' right to recover, plaintiffs had an absolute right to nonsuit. The court found that in defendant's prayer for relief, it only asserted matters in denial of or defense of plaintiffs' claim for reentry, including the request to strike down § 93.003. The court also noted that the lower court had no jurisdiction to render a declaratory judgment. Because defendant had no claim for affirmative relief in the lower court, plaintiffs had a right to nonsuit. The judgment was vacated and the case was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting defendant landlord's writ of certiorari to the county court, dismissing plaintiff tenants' reentry action, declaring a reentry statute unconstitutional, and awarding defendant attorney fees was vacated, and the case was dismissed. Because defendant's answer did not include any claims for affirmative relief, plaintiffs had an absolute right to nonsuit. The lower court had no authority to render declaratory judgments.

Sherman v. State


No. 05-97-00621-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


12 S.W.3d 489; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4886



July 1, 1999, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 292nd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F95-43528-HIV.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the 292nd District Court of Dallas County (Texas) finding defendant guilty, on his negotiated plea of guilty, of deadly conduct by discharging a firearm in the direction of an occupied habitation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for and, on his negotiated plea of guilty, found guilty of deadly conduct by discharging a firearm in the direction of an occupied habitation. The appellate court found that defendant was convicted upon his negotiated plea of guilty; therefore, in order to properly invoke the court's jurisdiction, he was required to file a notice of appeal complying with the extra-notice requirements of Tex. R. App. P. 25.2(b)(3). Although defendant's amended notice of appeal complied in form with rule 25.2(b)(3), it did not comply in substance. The record did not support the allegations that were made therein. Also, defendant's due process complaints were not jurisdictional defects. Therefore, the court concluded that defendant's amended notice of appeal did not operate to properly invoke the court's appellate jurisdiction. The appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's appeal from his conviction of discharging a firearm in the direction of an occupied habitation was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction, because his amended notice of appeal did not comply with the extra-notice requirements of Tex. R. App. P. 25.2(b)(3).

Jones v. State


NOS. 01-98-00533-CR, 01-98-00534-CR, 01-98-00535-CR, 01-98-00536-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4904



July 1, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 230th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 765876, 765877, 765878, 767117.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 230th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of charge of robbery and three charges of aggravated robbery under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 508.149(a)(10)-(11) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 29.02-29.03.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for one charge of robbery, where no weapon was observed, and three charges of aggravated robbery, where the individuals robbed were shown a gun. Appellant was convicted on all four counts of robbing grocery stores and sentenced to life imprisonment. Appellant challenged, asserting that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support his convictions because the complainants did not own the stolen property, the trial court erred by instructing the jury that appellant's sentence might be shorted for good behavior, and the statutorily mandated parol charge was unconstitutional. The court found that appellant's convictions were supported by legally and factually sufficient evidence that complainants, as employees, had better rights to the stolen property than did appellant. The jury instructions, though improper, were harmless error because they did not result in such egregious harm as to deny appellant a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; appellant's convictions for robbery and aggravated robbery were upheld because they were supported by legally and factually sufficient evidence, and although the challenged jury instructions were improper, the error was harmless because it did not deny appellant a fair and impartial trial.

Walker v. Texas Dep't of Crim. Justice - Institutional Div.


NO. 01-98-00140-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4948



July 1, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 278th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 19,925-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from a decision by the 278th District Court, Walker County (Texas), which dismissed plaintiff's claim against defendant department of criminal justice as frivolous.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a state prison inmate, sued defendant department of criminal justice for failing to provide plaintiff with records that allegedly pertained to plaintiff under the Public Information Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 552.001-552.353. Defendant moved to dismiss the claim as frivolous, and the trial court granted defendant's motion. Plaintiff appealed and contended the trial court erred in dismissing the case because defendant failed to perform a ministerial act of providing plaintiff with the information he requested. The court found that plaintiff's request for information was controlled by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 552.028, which provided that a governmental body was not required to accept or comply with a request for information from an individual who was imprisoned or confined in a correctional facility. Therefore, defendant did not have a mandatory duty to provide plaintiff with the information he requested. The decision to release information was left to the discretion of defendant. Because defendant properly denied plaintiff's request for information, the trial court did not err in dismissing plaintiff's action as frivolous. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed plaintiff inmate's claim as frivolous. The court found that defendant department of criminal justice was not required by statute to accept or comply with a request for information from an individual who was imprisoned.

Institute of Cognitive Dev., Inc. v. Texas Dep't of Mental Health &Mental Retardation


NO. 03-98-00376-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4780



June 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-03086, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff care facilities appealed the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), entering judgment in favor of defendant Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation and denying plaintiffs attorney's fees in their suit seeking declaratory judgment that rule defendant adopted regarding classification and reimbursement of plaintiffs for Medicaid-contracted beds was unlawfully retroactive.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs operated intermediate care facilities for the mentally retarded (ICF/MRs). Defendant Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation provided notice that it was considering adopting a rule that would classify ICF/MRs based upon the number of beds operated as Medicaid-contracted beds and reimburse them based upon that classification. Since small and medium-sized facilities were to be reimbursed at a higher rate than large facilities, plaintiffs reduced their numbers of Medicaid-contracted beds in anticipation of the adoption of the rule. Defendant then adopted an amended version of the rule which classified plaintiffs on a date prior to the rule's adoption, causing plaintiffs to be classified as larger facilities. Plaintiffs sought judgment that rule was unlawfully retroactive pursuant to Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 22.019. Judgment was entered in favor of defendant, and plaintiffs were denied attorney's fees. Plaintiffs appealed. The appeals court reversed because § 22.019(a) expressly prohibited the retroactive application of a rule enacted by defendant, and denial of attorney's fees was remanded for reconsideration in light of appellate court's disposition.


OUTCOME: Judgment in favor of defendant Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation regarding retroactivity of rule it adopted was reversed because Texas law expressly prohibited the retroactive application of any rule enacted by defendant. Moreover, in light of the court's reversal, the question of whether plaintiffs were entitled to attorney's fees was reversed and remanded for reconsideration.

Gaston v. State


No. 05-97-01040-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4823



June 30, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 27, 1999.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 10/27/1999
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Gaston v. Dretke, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 2181 (N.D. Tex., Feb. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F96-34127-RI.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by the Criminal District Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a jury conviction for murder. He contended a jury charge was fundamentally defective and that his counsel rendered ineffective assistance by not objecting to the instruction. Defendant argued that the mandatory instruction was fundamentally defective because it erroneously informed the jury he could earn time off the period of incarceration through good conduct. On review, the court found when the trial court asked if there were any objections to the charge, defense counsel responded, "No, Your Honor." The court noted that a defendant who affirmatively stated he had no objection to a jury charge had voluntarily relinquished his right to challenge on appeal any error in that charge. Moreover, the court noted the trial court was mandated to give the precise instruction complained of pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a). Because the trial court could not have erred in giving an instruction mandated by legislation, defendant's counsel could not have been have been ineffective for failing to object to the legislatively mandated instruction. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of murder because defendant had relinquished his right to challenge the charge on appeal when he stated he had no objection to the jury charge at trial. The court also noted that defense counsel could not have been have been ineffective for failing to object to a proper and legislatively mandated instruction.

Simpson v. State


No. 06-98-00306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4735


June 28, 1999, Submitted  
June 29, 1999, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 195th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court No. F97-01940-PN.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of orders of the 195th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), that entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting appellant of aggravated assault and sentenced him, with an enhancement, to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant individual was on trial for two separate offenses of aggravated assault. Evidence presented at trial showed that appellant was surprised by two women as he was attempting to steal a car. As one woman fled, appellant fired his pistol at her. Appellant then robbed the other woman at gunpoint. As appellant fled the scene, he shot at a man who had given chase. The jury found appellant guilty of both charges of aggravated assault. The trial court then conducted a punishment phase on each charge. During that phase, appellee prosecution introduced evidence of an extraneous offense in which appellant stole a woman's purse at gunpoint. Appellant did not file any objection, and he stipulated to evidence that he had been convicted of several other crimes. The trial court, finding the enhancement allegation true, then increased the offense to a first degree felony from a second degree felony. Based on the increase, the trial court sentenced appellant to life imprisonment. Appellant sought review, contending the sentence was grossly disproportionate. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence because appellant failed to preserve the alleged error for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of conviction and sentence because appellant failed to preserve for review the alleged error that his sentence was grossly disproportionate to the nature of the offense and amounted to cruel and unusual punishment.
