Beasley v. State


No. 05-98-00835-CR, No. 05-98-00836-CR, No. 05-98-00837-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4766



June 29, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 1. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MC97-B-4925-D, MC98-A-0208-D, MC97-B-4924-D.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 1, Dallas County (Texas), that found appellant guilty of operating a motor vehicle with an expired license plate, operating a motor vehicle with an expired vehicle inspection certificate, and failing to maintain financial responsibility, and imposed fines for each charge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant individual was issued citations for operating a motor vehicle with an expired license plate, with an expired vehicle inspection certificate, and for not maintaining financial responsibility. The municipal court found appellant guilty on all three charges. Appellant sought review in the county court of appeals. The county court of appeals heard motions and conducted a trial de novo. After trial, appellant was found guilty on all three charges and fined 10 dollars, 10 dollars, and 35 dollars on the three charges, respectively. The county court of appeals, however, expressly stated that the verdict and its findings were not final, pending appellant's 30-day probation. Appellant sought review within the 30-day period. The court dismissed the appeal, even though appellee prosecution asserted the matter was properly before the court because the court lacked jurisdiction until there were final convictions or judgments.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appeal seeking review of convictions for operating a motor vehicle with an expired license plate, with an expired vehicle inspection certificate, and for not maintaining financial responsibility because the court was without jurisdiction due to the lack of final guilty verdicts, findings, or judgments.

 

482 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re Living Ctrs. of Am., Inc.


NO. 14-99-00401-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


10 S.W.3d 1; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 9654



June 25, 1999, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from PROBATE COURT # 3, Harris County; Jones, Jerome, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for Writ of Mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators filed a petition for a writ of mandamus arguing that the Harris County Probate Court Number Three (Texas) judge abused his discretion by refusing to remove himself pursuant to their objection under Tex. Gov't Code § 74.053.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued relators for personal injuries allegedly suffered by decedent as a result of alleged abuse and neglect while a resident at relators' healthcare center. First probate judge assigned to the case voluntarily recused himself. The case was then assigned to a visiting judge pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code § 25.0022. Relators filed an objection to the visiting judge pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code § 74.053(b), but the judge denied relators' objection. Relators' filed a petition for a writ of mandamus. The court denied relators' petition for mandamus relief. The court ruled that mandamus relief was only available if the lower court violated a duty imposed by law or clearly abused its discretion. The court found that Tex. Gov't Code § 25.00261 did not apply to the assignment of judges in the probate courts. The court also determined that the case was correctly assigned to the visiting judge under Tex. Gov't Code § 25.0022. The court found that relators' objection to visiting judge's assignment pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code § 74.053(b) was invalid. Thus, the visiting judge had not abused his discretion or violated a duty imposed by law in denying relators' objection.


OUTCOME: The court denied relators' petition for a writ of mandamus because it found that the lower court judge had not abused his discretion or violated a duty imposed by law when he refused to remove himself pursuant to relators' objection.

 

483 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Wise County Bail Bond Bd.


NO. 2-98-315-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


995 S.W.2d 881; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4653



June 24, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 271ST DISTRICT COURT OF WISE COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 271st District Court of Wise County (Texas) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee board in appellant's action challenging appellee board's denial of his application for a bail bonds license.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Bail Bond Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372p-3, appellee board denied appellant a bail bond license because he had been convicted of two felony offenses. Appellant challenged the denial and the court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Appellant contended that his driving while intoxicated felony was not an offense of moral turpitude. Appellant also alleged that his other conviction for theft occurred prior to an amendment of the Act. The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee because appellee did not err in denying appellant a license. The amendment to the Act specifically made the Act retrospective such that appellant's theft conviction could be considered by appellee. The court determined that it was the legislature's intent that the phrase "involving moral turpitude" only modified misdemeanor offenses. A felony offense did not have to involve moral turpitude to be considered by appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee board because appellee board properly denied appellant's application for a bail bonds license based on his two prior felony convictions. The Bail Bond Act allowed appellee board to consider his theft and driving while intoxicated convictions in making its determination.

 

484 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Texas Health Enters. v. Geisler


NO. 2-98-026-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


9 S.W.3d 163; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4654



June 24, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order on Cause October 5, 2000. Petition for Review Granted August 24, 2000. As Corrected August 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 158TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and rendered in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties sought review of a decision from the 158th District Court of Denton County (Texas), which awarded plaintiff estate and beneficiary actual and punitive damages and prejudgment interest under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.008(b) in a wrongful death and survival action arising from defendant owner's and manager's negligence while decedent resided at defendants' nursing home


OVERVIEW: Defendant nursing home owner and manager asserted there was insufficient evidence to support the award of damages in plaintiff estate and beneficiary's wrongful death and survival action. Because of defendant manager's failures to provide adequate staff, plaintiffs' decedent's needs were not met and the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of defendant manager's negligence and gross negligence. A limitation on punitive damages was not constitutionally prohibited, but the trial court did not err in capping the punitive damage award because Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem Code Ann. § 41.008(b) included compensatory damages. The trial court also did not err in including wrongful death damages in computing the cap because the actual damages to be quadrupled encompassed the actual damages awards to all plaintiffs. Prejudgment interest was not a part of plaintiffs' actual damages and the inclusion of such in the computation of the punitive damages cap was reversed. Because there was evidence that plaintiffs brought the wrongful death action on behalf of all beneficiaries joinder of plaintiff beneficiary's brother was not required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed where the lower court's calculation of damages against defendant nursing home owner and manager properly included all actual damages and plaintiff beneficiary's brother was not a necessary party to plaintiff estate and beneficiary's wrongful death and survival action. However, prejudgment interest was not properly included in actual damages, and that portion of the lower court's judgment was reversed.

Aguilar v. State


NO. 14-99-00157-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4682



June 24, 1999, Rendered  
June 24, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 806089.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged denial of a pretrial writ of habeas corpus by the 262nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), from which appellant sought the writ on the grounds that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 261.101(a), which required a person with knowledge of child abuse to report the instance immediately, was unconstitutionally vague on its face.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by information for failing to immediately report knowledge of child abuse, pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 261.101(a). Appellant sought relief through an application for a pretrial writ of habeas corpus, which was denied. In the underlying case for violation of the statute, appellant pled nolo contendere. Appellant challenged the lower court's denial of his request for a writ and maintained that the statute was unconstitutionally vague on its face and failed to define the term "immediately." The court dismissed appellant's action for want of jurisdiction. The court reasoned that, because appellant pled nolo contendere and was therefore convicted, appellant's request for pretrial relief was moot. Moreover, because appellant was convicted, he had an adequate remedy at law in that the constitutional challenge of the state statute could be raised on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant's challenge of the lower court's order denying appellant's request for a pretrial writ of habeas corpus. The court reasoned it did not have jurisdiction over the action because appellant pled nolo contendere and was convicted; thus, the application for pretrial relief was moot. Further, appellant had an adequate remedy at law because the issue of the statute's unconstitutionality could be raised on direct appeal.

Hotze v. Brown


NO. 14-98-00394-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4696



June 24, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Motion for Rehearing Denied August 23, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 129th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 98-08746. Hon. Patrick Mizell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 129th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that found that appellant had no standing and granted cross-appellee's application for a temporary injunction, in an action in which cross-appellee filed an action against appellees seeking to declare an order prohibiting discrimination based on sexual orientation invalid, and preclude its enforcement by temporary and permanent injunction.


OVERVIEW: Cross-appellant mayor signed an executive order that prohibited discrimination based on sexual orientation. Appellant and cross-appellee sued cross-appellant mayor and cross-appellant city, asking the court to declare the order invalid and preclude its enforcement by temporary and permanent injunction. Cross-appellants filed a motion to dismiss, claiming appellant and cross-appellee had no standing. The lower court found appellant lacked standing and granted cross-appellee's application for temporary injunction. By interlocutory appeal, appellant challenged the dismissal and cross-appellants challenged the denial of the motion as to cross-appellee. The court of appeals affirmed the lower court's decision. The court found that appellant lacked standing because appellant did not establish a justiciable interest because his complaint failed to show that the subject matter of the litigation affected him differently than other citizens. The court also found that cross-appellee did possess standing to bring suit against cross-appellants when he alleged in his complaint that cross-appellant mayor's action usurped cross-appellee's power as a council member to make employment rules.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the lower court's decision that found that appellant lacked standing and dismissed his action against appellees when the court found that appellant did not establish a justiciable interest, because his complaint failed to show that the subject matter of the litigation affected him differently than other citizens.

Munoz v. State


No. 11-98-00179-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


996 S.W.2d 901; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4698



June 24, 1999, Decided  
June 24, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 259th District Court of Jones County.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 259th District Court of Jones County (Texas) that denied his motion to dismiss an untimely returned indictment charging him with possession of a deadly weapon in a penal institution pursuant to former Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art 32.01 (1966).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to a charge of possessing a deadly weapon in a penal institution and was sentenced to four years confinement. He challenged his conviction, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss an untimely returned indictment under former Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32.01, which required that an indictment be returned during the next term of court after a defendant's arrest. In affirming, the appellate court rejected appellant's arguments that the indictment was not timely returned because it was not returned during the next term of court after his arrest and that his motion to dismiss, although filed after the indictment's return, was timely brought. Article 32.01 had no application once the indictment was returned, even though it was returned by the grand jury at a subsequent term of court; thus, appellant's motion was not timely. Further, at the time of his arrest, appellant was incarcerated after a felony conviction. He was not improperly detained in custody to answer for the weapon possession charge and suffered no deprivation of his freedom other than those he already suffered as a convicted felon.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the trial court properly denied appellant's motion to dismiss the untimely returned indictment under the former statute, because this provision had no applicability once an indictment was returned, even though it was returned by the grand jury at a subsequent term of court.

Texas Workers' Compensation Comm'n v. Texas Builders Ins. Co.


NO. 03-98-00341-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


994 S.W.2d 902; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4470



June 17, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Denied November 20, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-05784, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a decision of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas) holding that appellee insurer was entitled to reimbursement from appellant Subsequent Injury Fund and an award of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, Workers' Compensation Commission (Commission), the Subsequent Injury Fund (Fund), and the Executive Director of the Commission (Director) challenged a lower court judgment reversing a Commission decision awarding benefits to a claimant; and, because appellee insurer had already paid the benefits, holding that appellee was entitled to reimbursement from appellant Fund, as well as to the award of attorney's fees. The lower court had reversed the Commission's decision because claimant had failed to answer the lawsuit, and the judgment in favor of appellee was therefore a default judgment and not a judgment on the merits of the claim. Appellants claimed that under those circumstances, appellee was not entitled to reimbursement. The court disagree, first holding that the trial court had jurisdiction, because, despite appellants' claim to the contrary, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 410.205(c) waived sovereign immunity and allowed for judicial review. The court further held that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 410.032(b) specifically required the reimbursement and that the award of attorney's fees was valid. The court therefore affirmed the lower court's decision.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision, granting appellee insurer reimbursement from appellant Fund for benefits appellee had paid to a claimant and awarding attorney's fees to appellee, was affirmed because the controlling statutes provided for judicial review, mandated the reimbursement, and allowed attorney's fees.

Dean v. State


No. 10-98-224-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO

June 16, 1999, Delivered  
June 16, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law Ellis County, Texas. Trial Court # 98-10019-CR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the County Court at Law, Ellis County (Texas), convicting defendant of evading detention pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.04(a) (1994).


OVERVIEW: A conviction of evading detention was affirmed because the officer reasonably attempted to detain defendant to investigate an expired license plate with no registration sticker attached. Defendant failed to stop when the officer attempted to pull her vehicle over, and she was convicted of evading detention under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.04(a) (1994). The appellate court affirmed the conviction, finding an investigatory stop lawful because the officer had a reasonable suspicion that defendant had violated the vehicle registration laws. Because defendant did not object to the jury instructions, she was required to show on appeal that any error in the instructions caused egregious harm. No such harm resulted from instructions on dealer license plates or the prosecutors' comments on the evidence. Defendant also failed to preserve for review her claims as to speedy trial and whether the court provided the jurors with the jury handbook.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because the officer had reason to detain defendant upon observing an expired license plate without a registration tag and because defendant failed to preserve for review any objections to the jury instructions.

Margraves v. State


NO. 14-97-00271-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


996 S.W.2d 290; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4329



June 10, 1999, Rendered  
June 10, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand August 16, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 5567. State's Petitions for Discretionary Review Refused November 24, 1999. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Denied January 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 85th District Court. Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 24, 423-85. Langley, J.D., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university board member sought review of a decision from the 85th District Court, Brazos County, Texas, which denied appellant's motion for a new trial and entered judgment convicting appellant of official misconduct in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 39.02(a)(2). Appellee State of Texas alleged that appellant improperly used a university aircraft to attend his son's graduation under the guise of official business.


OVERVIEW: Appellant university board member secured an official invitation to attend his son's graduation. Appellant and his wife flew to the graduation in a university airplane. Appellee State of Texas indicted appellant for official misconduct in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 39.02(a)(2). Following a jury trial, the lower court entered judgment convicting appellant as charged and denied appellant's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction and rendered a judgment acquitting appellant. The appellate court determined that because appellant conducted business while on the trip, such a mixed use did not violate § 39.02(a)(2). The court held that the statute did not provide adequate notice that a public official could be prosecuted for the mixed use of state property.


OUTCOME: Decision of the lower court convicting appellant university board member of official misconduct for using a university plane to attend his son's graduation and to conduct official university business was reversed and a judgment of acquittal was rendered. The court found that the evidence was legally insufficient to support a conviction under the statute for a mixed use of state property.

Holtzclaw v. State


NO. 01-98-01306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4343



June 10, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 2. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9827858.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 2, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. §§ 49.01, 49.04. Defendant moved to suppress his breath test results and dismiss certain allegations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of driving while intoxicated (DWI). Defendant was charged with DWI by having a blood/alcohol concentration of 0.10 or more and by losing the normal use of his mental or physical faculties from alcohol under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. §§ 49.01, 49.04. Defendant moved to suppress his breath test results, to dismiss the 0.10 allegation because the State did not preserve his breath test sample, and to declare certain statutes and regulations concerning breath tests unconstitutional. The trial judge denied the motions and found defendant guilty. Defendant challenged the denial of his motions. The reviewing court found defendant's challenges related only to the breath test. Defendant did not challenge the information's loss-of-use paragraph or the sufficiency of the evidence supporting it. Neither did he move below to suppress any evidence other than his breath test results. Therefore, the court held that even had the trial judge erred in denying defendant's motions, the error would have been harmless because the judgment would still stand on the loss-of-use allegation alone. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that even if the trial judge erred in denying defendant's motions, the error would have been harmless. Defendant failed to challenge the information's loss-of-use paragraph or the sufficiency of the evidence supporting it.

Schenekl v. State


NO. 2-98-386-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


996 S.W.2d 305; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4349



June 10, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted January 5, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 3 OF DENTON COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the County Criminal Court No. 3 of Denton County (Texas), finding him guilty of boating while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. § 31.124 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of boating while intoxicated. He challenged the decision arguing that the enforcement provision of the Water Safety Act (Act), Tex. Parks & Wild. Code Ann. §§31.001, 31.124 (1991), violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and that he was denied a speedy trial. Specifically, he argued that the officer's stopping of his boat simply to check for water safety equipment violated his right to be free from unreasonable search and seizure. The court disagreed noting that the seizure, while suspicionless, was analogous to a sobriety checkpoint and furthered the promotion of a legitimate government interest in protecting its boaters. The court also found that the detention was not unreasonable and that, given the detachability of various safety items, the only reasonable way to check for the equipment was a mid-river seizure. The court further held that, even though the trial was delayed, appellant never asserted his right to a speedy trial and did not suffer the requisite prejudice. The court then affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for boating while intoxicated was affirmed because the stopping of the boat to check for safety equipment was not unreasonable and it furthered a legitimate government interest. Appellant also did not assert his right to a speedy trial and suffered no prejudice because of the delay.

State v. Lloyd


No. 10-98-122-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


994 S.W.2d 362; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4267



June 9, 1999, Delivered  
June 9, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 82nd District Court Robertson County, Texas. Trial Court # 96-08-15, 174-CV.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Texas sought review of a decision from the 82nd District Court, Robertson County, Texas, which pursuant to the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 417.003(a), awarded counsel of appellee employee one-third of appellant state's workers' compensation subrogation lien. Appellee employee had pursued a negligence claim against a third-party.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state employee was injured in an automobile accident during the course of his employment. Appellee settled a negligence lawsuit he brought against a third-party driver. Appellant State of Texas did not actively participate in the lawsuit. The trial court awarded appellee's counsel one-third of appellant state's workers' compensation subrogation lien for attorney fees pursuant to the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 417.003(a). Appellant state contended § 417.003(a) was unconstitutional because it permitted a private attorney to represent a state agency. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the lower court. The appellate determined that appellant state challenged the wrong statute, but that even if it had challenged the appropriate statute, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 417.001, its challenge would fail because that provision did not violate Tex. Const. art. IV, § 22 because it did not unequivocally supplant the Attorney-General in his authority to prosecute the suits of the state.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court awarding appellee's counsel one-third of appellant state's workers' compensation subrogation lien as attorney's fees was affirmed. The court found that the applicable statute was constitutional as it merely allowed appellee to recover his fees from appellant state's subrogation lien and did not authorize appellee employee to institute an action to recover appellant state's lien.

Security Life of Denver Ins. Co. v. Ferguson


No. 05-98-01738-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4102



May 28, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 23, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 192nd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-02149-K.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer brought an interlocutory appeal from certification of two classes of life insurance policy purchasers from the 192nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), asserting that the lower court abused its discretion in certifying the class because it failed to conduct a rigorous analysis of class certification prerequisites and because the classes did not satisfy the criteria of Tex. R. Civ. P. 42(a) or 42(b)(4).


OVERVIEW: The court considered whether the lower court erred in granting class certification. Concluding that no abuse of discretion was shown, it affirmed that decision. Appellant insurer provided no authority that required the lower court to set forth reasoning for its ruling. Thus, appellant insurer did not demonstrate that the lower court failed to conduct a rigorous analysis. Further, the record provided some evidence in support of commonality as required by Tex. R. Civ. P. 42(a) and appellees' claims were typical of the absent class members. Thus, the record supported the finding that appellees were adequate class representatives. Where there was some evidence to support a conclusion of predominance, the court declined to reverse the lower court's certification ruling. It also held that it could not say the lower court abused its discretion in finding a class action was a superior method of adjudication. There was no reversible error or abuse of discretion, and the court affirmed the class certification order.


OUTCOME: Where there was no requirement for findings as to the lower court's reasoning, appellant insurer could not show a failure to conduct a rigorous analysis of class certification prerequisites, and the court found no abuse of discretion as to certification of the class.

Marquez v. State


NO. 14-97-00683-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4061

May 27, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 711,938.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of aggravated robbery in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the evidence supported the jury's resolution of appellant's insanity defense in favor of appellee State. The court found that appellee offered expert testimony to rebut appellant's insanity defense and that it was within the province of the jury to resolve the contradictory evidence. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.01(a), the provision dealing with the insanity defense, was not overly broad, because case law limited attacks based on overbreadth to the context of U.S. Const. amend. I. The court failed to find that § 8.01(a) was unconstitutionally vague due to its failure to define the common terms "know" and "wrong." The court concluded that the terms should be accorded their plain meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, because the jury did not err in resolving appellant's insanity defense in favor of appellee State, and the statutory provisions addressing the insanity defense were not overly broad or vague.

State v. Stevenson


NO. 2-94-510-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


993 S.W.2d 857; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 4094



May 27, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 2 OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of granting of motion to suppress evidence on a driving under the influence charge under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d § 4 , in appellee's favor, in the County Criminal Court N0. 2 of Tarrant County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prosecution sought review of the grant of appellee driver's motion to suppress statements made at an accident scene under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 4. Appellee hit a roadside sign while driving while intoxicated and his wife was injured. When the police arrived, appellee initially claimed his wife was driving. Upon further investigation of the accident scene, the police questioned appellee about whether he was really the driver. After appellee admitted driving, the police administered a sobriety test. The court first concluded under the plain language of the accident statute, appellee was not in custody because he was neither required to make any statement to the police or remain at the scene when the injured passenger was his wife and presumed to already have the knowledge the statute required a driver to impart to the injured party. The court reversed and remanded, concluding appellee was not entitled to Miranda protections until police formally arrested him even though he was required to remain at the scene pursuant to an investigative stop because the stop at most escalated from a consensual encounter to an investigative detention.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded judgment which sustained appellee's motion to suppress evidence, in appellant's favor, because appellee was not entitled to Miranda protections when he was neither required to remain at accident scene or give oral statements to police pursuant to an accident reporting statute and he was not in custody when focus shifted to him and at most converted a consensual encounter to an investigative detention.

Roy v. State


No. 05-97-02027-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3933



May 25, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F97-23147-WK.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment by the Criminal District Court No. 4. Dallas County (Texas) convicting appellant of burglary of a habitation, assessing a $ 300 fine, and placing appellant on community supervision for four years.


OVERVIEW: While appellant and his ex-girlfriend were eating at a restaurant, man one and man two entered ex-girlfriend's house and took television sets, a computer, a video set recorder, as well as other property. Appellant went with man three to pawn some of the stolen property. Appellant contended that the evidence was factually insufficient to support his conviction, specifically arguing that the weight of the evidence showed that he was not involved in the burglary and that man two was not credible because man one testified that appellant was not involved in any plan to burglarize ex-girlfriend's home. After reviewing all the evidence, the court concluded that the finding of appellant's guilt was not so against the great weight of the evidence as to be clearly wrong and unjust. The court rejected appellant's argument that his fine was unconstitutional, finding that the $ 300 fine was within the range of punishment allowed by statute, and that because appellant had not shown he was imprisoned for failure to pay his fine, assessment of a fine did not violate his equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that the finding of appellant's guilt was not so against the great weight of the evidence as to be clearly wrong and unjust and that appellant's fine was not unconstitutional.

Birnbaum v. Alliance of Am. Insurers


NO. 03-97-00660-CV, NO. 03-98-00208-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


994 S.W.2d 766; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3739



May 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied March 2, 2000. Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled May 4, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 98TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 97-09206 & 97-09206-A, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING AND HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Cause No. 03-97-00660-CV; Reversed and Injunction Dissolved in Cause No. 03-98-00208-CV.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a state department of insurance, an attorney general, and an individual, sought review in a consolidated appeal of orders from the District Court of Travis County, 98th Judicial District (Texas), which granted temporary and permanent injunctions on the applications of appellees, automobile insurance companies and trade associations. Both injunctions prohibited appellant department from releasing information to appellant individual.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellees, automobile insurance companies and trade associations, in their action to enjoin the disclosure by appellant department of insurance of certain quarterly market reports, and dissolved a permanent injunction. The reports contained information concerning written premiums, policy and membership fees, and other data. The court found that the quarterly market report information was not excepted by the Texas Public Information Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 552.112, because insurance companies were not financial institutions within the meaning of the section and the section was a permissive exception that the government could waive. The trial court did not, however, abuse its discretion in granting a temporary injunction on the ground that the report information amounted to trade secrets. Accordingly, the court affirmed that part of the trial court judgment issuing a temporary injunction on the ground that the report information constituted trade secrets, but modified the temporary injunction to, among other things, delete that part of the order authorizing disclosure of information to appellee association.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a grant of summary judgment to appellees and dissolved a permanent injunction because the report information was not excepted from disclosure. The court affirmed a grant of a temporary injunction because the information amounted to trade secrets, but modified the injunction to allow disclosure of information supplied by nonparty insurers and deleted that part of the order authorizing disclosure to appellee association.

 

499 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of Lubbock v. Cornyn


NO. 03-98-00631-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


993 S.W.2d 461; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3744



May 20, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-08513A, HONORABLE MARY PEARL WILLIAMS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and officials, sought review of a decision of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment affirming appellee attorney general's ruling that confidential reports were public records required to be released because the information statutorily required to obtain them was contained in public dispatch logs.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, city and officials, asserted that certain accident reports were confidential by virtue of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 47 (since repealed). Appellee attorney general had ruled that dispatch logs, from which the requirements of § 47(b)(a)(D) necessary to obtain the accident reports could be obtained, were public records within the meaning of the Texas Public Information Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 552.001-.353, by letter opinion. Based upon the doctrine of separation of powers, the court affirmed, rejecting appellant city's assertion that it had discretion to withhold accident reports from individuals who took advantage of the dispatch logs to obtain confidential information. The discretion sought would permit appellant city to sit as a legislative and judicial body, as well as an executive body. The court also rejected appellants' assertions that the issue of intervenor requestor's standing was ripe for consideration, as the standing issue could bear on the counterclaims intervenors asserted against appellant that remained pending before the trial court and had no bearing on the trial court's grant of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court upholding appellee attorney general's ruling that dispatch logs were public information was affirmed, and appellants, city and officials, did not have the power to withhold confidential accident reports where the information required to withhold them was publicly available in dispatch logs.

Young v. State


NO. 14-95-01080-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3916



May 20, 1999, Rendered  
May 20, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law NO. 5. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9516298.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County, Texas, convicting him of driving while intoxicated. Appellant argued, inter alia, that (1) the jury charge was fundamentally defective; (2) Texas Penal Code Ann. § 49.04 was unconstitutional; (3) the evidence was insufficient to support a judgment; and (4) the state improperly introduced evidence of extraneous misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for driving while intoxicated. Appellant contended that the jury charge was erroneous because it did not require a culpable mental state, but the court concluded that it had never been necessary to plead scienter in a prosecution for driving while intoxicated. Rather, the court held that appellant could be convicted of DWI even though he might have in good faith believed that he was competent to drive. Appellant further contended that Texas Penal Code Ann. § 49.04 was unconstitutional because it did not require a mens rea element. However, the court determined that there was a presumption that the statute was valid and that appellant had not met his burden of establishing its unconstitutionality. The court also concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and that appellant had not preserved his objection to extraneous misconduct evidence, because he had not objected to the testimony at trial. Therefore, the court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated, holding that the jury charge was not defective because a culpable mental state was not required for DWI, the statute was not unconstitutional, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, and appellant had not preserved his objection to extraneous misconduct evidence because he had failed to object at trial.

 

501 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


DeRuy v. Garza


No. 04-98-00830-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


995 S.W.2d 748; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3892



May 19, 1999, Delivered  
May 19, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 98-CI-13831. Honorable Michael Peden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment of the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), that granted appellee doctor's motion for summary judgment on the basis of the statute of limitations in an action for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: After appellant patient learned her gall bladder problem was misdiagnosed as biliary cancer, she sued appellee doctor for malpractice. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment on the grounds the suit was barred by the statute of limitations under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4509i, § 10.01 (Vernon Supp. 1999). Appellant sought review, and the court reversed and remanded. Under § 10.01, a two-year statute of limitations period was applied to medical malpractice claims. Where misdiagnosis was alleged, the date of the misdiagnosis or failure to diagnose was the date the limitations period began running, and the continuing nature of the diagnosis did not extend the tort for limitations purposes. Here, the date of appellant's misdiagnosis was more than four years prior to her filing suit. However, she did not discover the misdiagnosis until one year before filing suit. Therefore, § 10.01, as applied to appellant was unconstitutional because it was impossible for her to bring the action before she knew of it. A statute that unreasonably abridged a right of redress was a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor dismissing appellant patient's medical malpractice suit was reversed and remanded because the statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to her. The statute cut off her right to sue appellee before she learned of the misdiagnosis that gave rise to her claim.

Sparkman v. State


No. 06-98-00030-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


997 S.W.2d 660; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3556


May 12, 1999, Submitted  
May 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Pro Se Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at law. Smith County, Texas. Trial Court No. 1-84863-96.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the County Court at Law, Smith County (Texas), convicting him of operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving with a suspended license. Appellant challenged his conviction, raising numerous arguments. The court rejected appellant's arguments and affirmed his conviction. Although the judge should not have signed the judgment because he had recused himself, the court remanded the case to the trial court for reformation of the judgment by the judge who presided over the trial, to sign it. The lower court did not err in denying appellant's motion to quash, contending the complaint and information were vague because the information sufficiently tracked the statutory language of the provision of the Transportation Code that appellant violated. The court lacked jurisdiction over appellant's argument that suspending his license was unconstitutional for automatically depriving him of a property right. Because the Transportation Code provided for a separate appeal from the suspension of a driver's license, the court could not review the suspension of appellant's license as part of his appeal. Appellant's equal protection challenge failed because he did not show he was a member of a class treated differently from others in the same class.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction for operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license affirmed and case remanded for the judge who presided over the trial to sign the judgment.

Graham v. State


NO. 14-97-00840-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3564



May 13, 1999, Rendered  
May 13, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 733816.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal sought review of a ruling from the 178th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of forgery of a commercial instrument in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.21.


OVERVIEW: Complainant had lost her daily planner and appellant criminal confessed to a police officer that she redeemed a store merchandise credit slip (slip) and threw the rest of complainant's property in the trash. Appellant was indicted for forgery of a writing. The state amended the indictment to charge appellant with forgery of a commercial instrument. Appellant moved to quash the indictment, but the trial court denied the motion. Appellant was convicted and sought review. The court found that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.21 was not unconstitutionally vague, particularly regarding appellant's specific conduct. Further, the court found that the indictment was sufficient to charge appellant with forgery of a commercial instrument because appellant exchanged the slip for merchandise and knew her actions were unlawful. The court found that the trial court did not error in denying appellant's motion to quash the indictment because the indictment was sufficient on its face to provide adequate notice to appellant. In addition, the court found that any rational trier of fact could find beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant's statement referred to the forgery of complainant's slip.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction and because there was no error in the indictment or charge.

GRAVES v. STATE


NUMBERS 13-97-535-CR through 13-97-546-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


994 S.W.2d 238; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3635



May 13, 1999, Delivered  
May 13, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused as Untimely Filed September 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 130th District Court of Matagorda County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 130th District Court of Matagorda County, Texas, of twelve charges of sexual assault, the court assessing concurrent 16-year sentences.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant on 12 charges of sexual assault perpetrated on complainants who were all female parishioners and students of a school at which he was pastor and principal. Appellant asserted the evidence regarding the sexual assault of certain complainants was legally insufficient to sustain his conviction because neither victim made a timely outcry and their testimony was uncorroborated. He argued that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.07 required that an alleged victim who was 14 years of age or older at the time of the alleged offense must either make an outcry statement within six months of the incident or there must be evidence to corroborate her testimony. Appellant argued that the 1993 amendment to art. 38.07 to eliminate the outcry requirement if the victim was under the age of 18 was unconstitutional because it was in effect an ex post facto law. The court held that art. 38.07 was merely a procedural change and did not allow conviction on less evidence than was required when the offense was committed. Thus, the law in effect at the time of appellant's trial in 1997, the version amended in 1993, applied. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on charges of sexual assault on the grounds that the evidence against defendant was overwhelming. An amendment to the statute eliminating the outcry requirement for certain complainants was constitutional because it was merely a procedural change.

Tucker v. State


NO. 01-98-00833-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3693



May 13, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 780140.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 183rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting of him of possession of cocaine. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress all evidence seized during a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by police after he committed a traffic violation. Before stopping the vehicle, a license check revealed the owner of the vehicle had an outstanding arrest warrant for traffic violations. The officer then frisked defendant to search for weapons, felt a bulge in one of his pockets, and suspected that it was crack cocaine. He asked defendant what the bulge was, and defendant replied that it was crack. After the court denied his motion to suppress the seizure of the evidence and that statement that the bulge was crack cocaine, defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine. The court of appeals affirmed the conviction, holding that police were entitled to conduct a pat down search because there was a reasonable suspicion defendant was armed. Furthermore, the court stated that because the officer felt an object whose shape identified it as contraband, a warrantless seizure was justified.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of possession of cocaine. The court held that the officer had the right to perform a frisk during a traffic stop in order to be sure that defendant was not armed and defendant voluntarily told the police officer that the bulge in one of his pockets was crack cocaine. Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying the motion to suppress evidence.

 

506 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. State


No. 05-97-01004-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3526



May 12, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from The Criminal District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F96-00098-LH.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Criminal District Court of Dallas County (Texas), defendant was convicted of aggravated assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02 (1994). The jury assessed punishment at twenty years confinement in the state penitentiary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While "tripping" on "wack," a combination of marijuana, PCP, and embalming fluid, defendant put a gun to his friend's face and shot him one time. The victim survived despite massive injuries. After finding defendant guilty of aggravated assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02 (1994), the jury assessed punishment at twenty years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support defendant's conviction. There was no evidence that the shooting occurred because of any event other than defendant's voluntary act of pulling the trigger. Moreover, under § 8.04(a), which satisfied the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, voluntary intoxication was no defense because it could neither render a physical action involuntary nor negate a culpable mental state. While the "bodily injury" element of aggravated assault was a "result of conduct" element, the use of a deadly weapon was a "nature of conduct" element. Thus, it was not error to include both definitions of intentionally in the charge. Finally, no evidence supported a § 6.01(a) voluntariness instruction as to defendant's physical body movements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault, holding that the evidence was legally and factually sufficient, a Texas penal statute providing that voluntary intoxication was not a defense to the commission of a crime met the constitutional requirements of due process, the trial court's jury charge defining intentional was proper, and the trial court correctly refused defendant's requested jury charge on accident.

Texas Alcoholic Bev. Comm'n v. Amusement & Music Operators of Tex.


NO. 03-98-00579-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


997 S.W.2d 651; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3364



May 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Granted July 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 5561. Petition for Review Dismissed May 4, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 98-06901, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant administrative agency appealed the entry of a temporary injunction by the District Court of Travis County (Texas) barring defendant from relying on an interpretation of gambling devices pending determination of a declaratory judgment action by plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: A temporary injunction barring defendant administrative agency from relying on an interpretation of gambling devices was affirmed pending the outcome of a declaratory judgment action filed by plaintiff, an association of amusement machine operators. Association members operated eight liners that were similar to slot machines and dispensed gift certificates. Based on a state attorney general opinion, defendant issued memoranda to its agents defining prohibited gambling devices to include eight liners. Plaintiff association could not sue on behalf of its members for a declaration that seizure of the machines would be unconstitutional or for an injunction prohibiting such seizures. However, it could seek to enjoin defendant from relying on invalid rules as that action would not require participation of individual members of plaintiff. Defendant's memos were rules under the state administrative procedure act because enforcement of guidelines in the memos would affect every eight liner owner. Plaintiff did not have to sue defendant's director individually because the trial court had jurisdiction under the administrative procedure act to issue an injunction against a state agency.


OUTCOME: Entry of a temporary injunction barring defendant administrative agency from relying on an interpretation of gambling devices was affirmed. Plaintiff association established a probable injury and a probable right to recovery in its challenge to constitutionality of the interpretation because its members would be affected by defendant's use of the interpretation in enforcement of penal code gambling device provisions.

Cook v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3407

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: After he was arrested and charged with misdemeanor driving while intoxicated (DWI), appellant refused to submit to a requested breath test. Thereafter, appellant moved to suppress the evidence, claiming that he was subjected to an illegal detention, search, and seizure. The trial court denied appellant's motion. Appellant pleaded no contest to the charge, and the court found appellant guilty and sentenced him to 180 days in jail, probated for a period of two years. Appellant challenged, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress and asserting that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 was unconstitutional. Smith v. State


NO. 14-97-00949-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


993 S.W.2d 408; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3439



May 6, 1999, Judgment Rendered  
May 6, 1999, Opinions Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 27, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5406.

On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-26668. Hon. Brian Rains, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing En Banc Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for rehearing en banc of his appeal from the revocation of his bond and his incarceration at the conclusion of a hearing on his petition for habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony theft involving fraudulent insurance claims. At a state habeas corpus proceeding, defendant contested the constitutionality of bond conditions imposed on him following his conviction. At the hearing, the state presented four witnesses who testified that defendant had violated the conditions. The trial court revoked defendant's bond and ordered him taken into custody. The trial court's action was affirmed. At the original hearing when bond conditions were imposed, defendant indicated he understood that if the conditions were violated he would be taken into custody. Defendant failed to object at his habeas corpus hearing to testimony by state witnesses regarding his violations of bond conditions, and defendant failed to request a continuance. While defendant was entitled to due process protections of notice and a reasonable opportunity to be heard regarding revocation of his bond, a written motion by the state to revoke the bond was not required by statute or by due process.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for rehearing en banc was overruled, and his incarceration at the conclusion of his habeas corpus petition hearing for violation of bond conditions was affirmed. The state's presentation of evidence of violations of conditions at the hearing did not have to be preceded by a written motion to revoke defendant's bond and provided due process notice.

University of Tex. Health Science Ctr. at San Antonio v. Mata & Bordini, Inc.


No. 04-98-00547-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


2 S.W.3d 312; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3269



April 30, 1999, Delivered  
April 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied August 24, 2000. Motion for Rehearing Denied June 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 97-CI-03595. Honorable Patrick J. Boone, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), that found that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 417.003 applied to defendant and awarded plaintiff law firm an apportionment of attorney fees out of defendant's subrogation interest in a third-party award in favor of defendant's employee, and denied the request for attorney fees. Plaintiff appealed from the portion of the order that denied its request for additional fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff law firm pursued a third-party action on behalf of defendant's employee, who had received workers' compensation benefits from defendant. After settlement was obtained, defendant requested payment of its statutory subrogation lien. When defendant refused to pay plaintiff fees pursuant to Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 417.003, plaintiff filed a declaratory suit. The parties moved for summary judgment. The trial court ruled that § 417.003 applied to defendant, awarded plaintiff an apportionment of fees out of defendant's subrogation interest in the third-party settlement, and denied both parties fees in the declaratory judgment action. The parties appealed and the order was affirmed. The appellate court held that sovereign immunity was waived for apportionment actions and that the assessment of attorney fees to a private attorney after a third-party action in which the attorney general declined to participate did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers. Res judicata did not apply, the state court was the appropriate forum to rule on plaintiff's claim for fees, and the court acted reasonably in ruling that each party should bear its own fees for the instant action.


OUTCOME: The order that awarded plaintiff law firm an apportionment of attorney fees out of defendant's subrogation interest in a third-party settlement and refused to award additional attorney fees was affirmed. Sovereign immunity was waived for apportionment actions, the assessment of attorney fees to a private attorney did not violate separation of powers, res judicata did not apply, and the court acted reasonably in declining to award additional fees.

Jimenez v. State


NO. 01-96-00187-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


992 S.W.2d 633; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3262



April 29, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Denied November 1, 2000. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 24, 1999.
Affirmed by Jimenez v. State, 32 S.W.3d 233, 2000 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 81 (Tex. Crim. App., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 180th District Court Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 703807. Hon. D. M. Stricklin, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 180th District Court Harris County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of aggravated assault and sentenced him to 15 years imprisonment, claiming the jury instruction was unconstitutional and violated his rights to Due Process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant suspected that his girlfriend-victim was seeing another man. When the victim came home, appellant threatened her with a gun and forced her to have sex. The victim during this time pushed the gun away, which went off, blowing off her right hand and seriously injuring her left hand. Appellant was indicted for attempted capital murder. The case was tried to a jury, which found appellant guilty of aggravated assault. Appellant challenged his conviction, arguing that the jury instruction was unconstitutional. The court held that the jury instruction properly gave an instruction on reasonable doubt as a standard of proof of extraneous offenses at the punishment phase of the trial. The court also determined that the jury instruction as to good-conduct time was incorrect as a matter of law, violated appellant's Due Process rights, and was unconstitutional under the state and federal constitutions. However, the court concluded that considering the record as a whole, the entire charge, the nature of the offense, and the punishment assessed, appellant had not shown the erroneous jury instructions resulted in such egregious harm that he did not receive a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and held that even though appellant's jury was given an incorrect statement of the law, which violated appellant's rights to Due Process, the error was harmless, and appellant received a fair and impartial trial.

In re Estate of Chavana


No. 04-97-00904-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


993 S.W.2d 311; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3183



April 28, 1999, Delivered  
April 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Remanded by Guajardo v. Chavana, 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 3329 (Tex. App. San Antonio, May 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of October 7, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6205.

From the County Court at Law No. 1, Webb County, Texas. Trial Court No. 10,089. Honorable Raul Vasquez, Judge Presiding.
In re Estate of Chavana, 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6205 (Tex. App. San Antonio, 1998)



DISPOSITION: APPELLEE'S MOTION FOR REHEARING GRANTED IN PART, DENIED IN PART; AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Decedent's son appealed from a decision by the Webb County Trial Court (Texas), granting decedent's illegitimate daughters' motion for summary judgment, in an action brought seeking a declaration of intestate heirship. Decedent's son argued that it was error to grant his sisters' motion for summary judgment on the issue of heirship, in holding his sisters were the heirs of decedent, and in denying his motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted decedent's illegitimate daughters' motion for summary judgment in an action to determine heirship, decedent's son appealed. The court held that the appeals court statement, to the effect that daughters' claims to intestate heirship were without merit, did not create a controlling law of the case that must be followed in all subsequent litigation. The law of the case doctrine was discretionary and could not be used to reach an unconstitutional result. Further, when the case was remanded from the appeals court, it was sent back without instruction and the case then stood on the trial court's docket as if it had never been tried. The court held daughters could not be denied the judicially enforceable right to lay claim to an estate on the basis of legitimacy unless the denial was substantially related to an important state interest. The court held that daughters demonstrated by a preponderance of the evidence they were decedent's biological descendents. Evidence included affidavit by decedent's sister, documents in which decedent acknowledged his relationship, and copies of checks decedent sent to children dividing equally property sold by the decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment acknowledging decedent's daughters' claim to heirship. Appeals court statement that daughters' claims were without merit did not create controlling law of the case. Law of the case doctrine could not be used to reach an unconstitutional result. Daughters demonstrated by a preponderance of evidence they were decedent's biological descendents. Evidence included documents in which decedent acknowledged his paternity.

Williams v. State


No. 05-97-01230-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 3115



April 27, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 363rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F96-51636-IW.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of decision from the 363rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) convicting him of murder. Appellant contended that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support his conviction as a principal and as a party, that the trial judge erred in failing to apply an abstract definition of causation to the facts of the case in the jury charge, and that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his murder conviction. Appellant alleged insufficiency of the evidence, trial court error in failing to apply an abstract definition of causation to the facts in the jury charge, and unconstitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 . Appellant contended the victim was already dead when appellant shot him and that the trial judge erred in failing to apply an abstract jury instruction on causation. The court disagreed, where appellant and other perpetrators all shot the victim multiple times, and each shooter inflicted fatal wounds; appellant's actions were alone sufficient to cause the death, and appellant was not entitled to the instruction. Appellant contended that § 19.02 unconstitutionally violated his due process rights because it shifted the burden of persuasion to appellant to show he acted in the heat of sudden passion. The court concluded that under Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a), to preserve a complaint for appellate review, appellant must present a timely, specific objection at trial, and failure to make objection waived even constitutional errors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's murder conviction where the evidence was sufficient to support his conviction and the trial judge did not err in failing to apply an abstract definition of causation to the facts in the jury charge. Further, the constitutionality of a statute was not preserved for appellate review because a timely, specific objection was not presented at trial.

In re S.B.


No. 04-98-00535-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2992



April 21, 1999, Delivered  
April 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 73rd Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 98-JUV-00481-A. Honorable Andy Mireles, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the 73rd Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), for intentionally causing bodily injury to an elderly person, and engaging in delinquent conduct. He argued that Tex. Fam. Code § 53.045(a)(7) (1996), upon which his conviction was based, was vague and violated Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19 because it did not define the minimum age at which a juvenile offender's sentence could be determined.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to intentionally causing bodily injury to an elderly person, and was found to have engaged in delinquent conduct. The judge committed defendant to a youth commission for five years. Appellant sought review in this court, asserting that the trial court erred in failing to grant his pre-trial motion to quash the petition. Specifically, he argued that Tex. Fam. Code § 53.045(a)(7) (1996), upon which his conviction was based, was unconstitutionally vague and violated Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19 because the statute did not define the minimum age at which a juvenile offender's sentence could be determined. This court affirmed the trial court's judgment, concluding that § 53.045(a)(7) applied to appellant because he was a child who engaged in delinquent conduct, as the terms were statutorily defined, and committed the penal offense of injuring an elderly person, one of the enumerated offenses. The court further held that § 53.045(a)(7) was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave a person of average intelligence fair notice that his contemplated conduct was forbidden, it created little or no risk of arbitrary enforcement, and it proscribed appellant's conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for intentionally causing bodily injury to an elderly person, and engaging in delinquent conduct. The court concluded that the statute upon which appellant's conviction was based was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave a person of average intelligence notice that his contemplated conduct was forbidden, it created little risk of arbitrary enforcement, and it proscribed appellant's conduct.

Murphy v. Jones


NO. 01-97-01285-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2757



April 15, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 12th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 18,796.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prison inmate appealed from a decision by the 12th District Court, Walker County (Texas), which dismissed his action against appellees, a correctional institution and officers, as frivolous. Defendant alleged that his constitutional rights had been violated under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate injured his hand while cleaning pipes and brought an action against appellees, the correctional institution and officers, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging his constitutional rights had been violated while incarcerated. Appellees moved to dismiss. The trial court granted the motion and appellant sought review. The reviewing court stated that the trial judge had broad discretion to dismiss prisoner lawsuits if the suit was frivolous or had no arguable basis in law pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §14.003. Appellant argued that when he was injured he was under the authority of one officer. However, appellant did not sue that officer but brought action against three other supervisory officers. Therefore, appellee contended there was no arguable basis in law for appellant's claim because appellant never claimed that appellee supervisory officers affirmatively participated in the acts that injured him. Because appellant did not allege, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, that appellee supervisory officials affirmatively acted to cause the injury or implemented unconstitutional policies that caused the injury, the trial judge did not err. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed an order dismissing a civil rights action by appellant inmate because appellant did not allege that appellee supervisory officers affirmatively participated in the acts that injured him. The court found that appellant's claim had no arguable basis in law and that the trial court was correct in dismissing the lawsuit as frivolous.
