Jones v. State


NO. 03-97-00592-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2782



April 15, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TOM GREEN COUNTY, 51ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. A-95-0545-S, HONORABLE DICK ALCALA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the District Court of Tom Green County, 51st Judicial District (Texas), revoking his community supervision and imposing against him the sentence previously assessed resulting from his conviction for possessing more than four ounces of marihuana on which the controlled substances tax had not been paid, in violation of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 159.201.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was placed on community supervision in lieu of imprisonment for seven years as a result of his conviction for possessing more than four ounces of marihuana on which the controlled substances tax had not been paid, in violation of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 159.201. Appellant's supervision was revoked for use of controlled substances without a doctor's prescription. Appellant sought review of that revocation and the court affirmed. The court found that appellant signed two written statements admitting to the use of cocaine after he tested positive for such use and that admission of one instance was sufficient to support the revocation. The court found that appellant's request to reverse the revocation order for denial of a speedy hearing in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12, § 21(b) was without merit because the issue was not raised on appeal of the denial of his writ of habeas corpus. The court concluded that violation of the speedy hearing statute was not an error that tainted the decision to revoke or that mandated a reversal of the revocation order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order revoking appellant's community supervision and imposing against him the sentence previously assessed resulting from his conviction for possessing more than four ounces of marihuana on which the controlled substances tax had not been paid. The court found that appellant's written admission to the use of cocaine in violation of his supervisory conditions was sufficient to support revocation.

Chandler v. Chandler


No. 08-97-00484-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


991 S.W.2d 367; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2834



April 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 3, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2404. Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled November 12, 1999. Released for Publication June 14, 1999. Rehearing Denied June 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 41st District Court of El Paso County, Texas. TC # 77-1540.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged a decision of the 41st District Court of El Paso County (Texas), which denied appellant's motion for rehearing and petition for review of the divorce decree between himself and appellee wife.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband challenged the lower court's decision to award his ex-wife a portion of his military retirement benefits. Appellant claimed that his wife had been previously married and that there was no record of a valid divorce from her first husband. A jury determined that appellee did not knowingly deceive appellant about her previous marriage. Based on this decision, the court did not set aside the parties' property settlement. Appellant later filed several lawsuits in different jurisdictions seeking to have the settlement agreement set aside. The lower court then permanently enjoined appellant from filing any new actions regarding the same matter. The appellate court held that appellant's claims regarding bias on the part of the judge were waived because appellant failed to object in a timely manner. The appellate court also held that appellant's request to have his previous marriage declared void were part of the original proceedings and were therefore barred by the doctrine of res judicata. Finally, the appellate court upheld the lower court's permanent injunction entered against appellant in order to prevent appellant from harassing appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant husband's motion for rehearing and petition for review of the divorce decree between himself and appellee wife. The court upheld a permanent injunction issued by the lower court to prevent appellant from filing further lawsuits regarding the same claims.

Reed v. State


NUMBER 13-93-680-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


991 S.W.2d 354; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2839



April 15, 1999, Delivered  
April 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1999


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by jury for the offense of aggravated sexual assault in the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas). Defendant's appeal on remand was based on challenges to the legal and factual sufficiency of the evidence and allegations of improper jury argument by the prosecution.


OVERVIEW: After a trial by jury, defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child under the age of 14. Defendant's case was remanded to the trial court on another issue and after that proceeding resulted in affirmation of his conviction, he appealed on two additional grounds. Defendant challenged the legal and factual sufficiency of the evidence against him. Upon review, the court held that the jury's verdict was not so contrary to the overwhelming weight of the evidence so as to be clearly wrong and manifestly unjust. Defendant also challenged the content of the prosecutor's closing argument. The prosecutor referred to other alleged crimes in his closing, which were not admissible as evidence. Because the appellate court held that this error was not corrected at the trial court level and that the error was not harmless, defendant's case was reversed and he was granted a new trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant prevailed on appeal and his conviction was reversed due to improper jury argument by the prosecution, wherein the prosecutor referred to other alleged criminal acts supposedly committed by defendant.

Webb v. State


NO. 14-96-01453-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


991 S.W.2d 408; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2862



April 15, 1999, Rendered  
April 15, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 182nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 731,934. Hon. Bob Burdette, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for retaliation in the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas). On appeal, defendant contended that the statute for retaliation was unconstitutionally vague; that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support a conviction; that the trial court committed error; and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for retaliation on several grounds. Defendant alleged that the statute for retaliation, under which he was convicted, was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. On appeal, the court found that the statute gave fair warning of what conduct was prohibited and the consequences for the violation, and therefore was not vague or overbroad. Defendant also contended that the evidence was factually and legally insufficient to support a guilty verdict. The appellate court found that a rational trier of fact could have found that defendant's actions constituted retaliation and therefore the evidence was both factually and legally sufficient. Defendant's last two contentions, that the trial court committed error and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, were found to be without merit. The court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was not reversed on appeal and the court found no merit in defendant's contention that the statute for retaliation was unconstitutionally vague. The court also found that defendant's conviction was supported by the evidence and that there was no reversible error by the trial court. The court found that defendant received effective assistance of counsel at his trial.

Maxcey v. State


NO. 14-97-00305-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


990 S.W.2d 900; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2868



April 15, 1999, Rendered  
April 15, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9649776. Gilbert, Jeff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of driving while intoxicated. Appellant contended that his motion to suppress evidence was improperly denied.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for driving while intoxicated, claiming the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence. Appellant contended the arresting officer did not have probable cause to suspect appellant of driving while intoxicated or to arrest him for the offense. The court affirmed the conviction, finding the evidence supported a finding of probable cause. The court determined that the officer was legally investigating an automobile accident caused by appellant. The court found that during the course of that investigation the office noticed an odor of alcohol on appellant's breath, noticed that his speech and appearance were abnormal, and noticed his eyes were glassy. The court concluded that all of the foregoing, together with statements regarding appellant's driving, gave the officer probable cause to believe that appellant was driving while intoxicated. The court did not consider appellant's allegations regarding the conclusory nature of the stipulations or regarding the incorrect warnings that he was given because appellant failed to preserve those issues for appeal pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a)(1)(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant for driving while intoxicated, finding no error in the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress. The court determined that the evidence supported a finding of probable cause because the arresting officer was legally investigating an accident caused by appellant and in the course of that investigation concluded appellant had been driving under the influence of alcohol.

In re NationsBank


NO. 01-98-00582-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2739



April 14, 1999 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator bank filed a petition for a writ of mandamus following a decision from the 215th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied relator's motion to transfer venue in a bond trust breach of fiduciary duty action.


OVERVIEW: Tax exempt bonds were issued by a public housing authority. Relator bank sold the bonds to the public as the original bond indenture trustee. Plaintiffs, purchasers of the bonds, filed an action against several defendants, including relator, alleging that the rehabilitation project was not completed and relator was negligent in failing to insure that only authorized issuance costs and expenses were paid to the underwriter at bond closing. Plaintiffs also contended that relator otherwise breached its fiduciary duties. Relator's motion to have the action transferred to the county where its principal office was located was denied by the lower court. On review, the court found that there was no prima facie evidence in the record that relator's principal office was located in the county where it sought to remove the action. Venue was proper in the county in which the principal office of any of the corporations was located. The court thus denied relator's petition for a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator's petitioner for a writ of mandamus directing a change of venue because venue was proper in the county where the principal office of any of the corporations was located, and there was no prima facie evidence that relator's principal office was located in the county to which it sought removal.

Nieto v. State


No. 10-98-180-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


990 S.W.2d 874; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2773



April 14, 1999, Delivered  
April 14, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 25th District Court Guadalupe County, Texas. Trial Court # 97-0260-CR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 25th District Court Guadalupe (Texas) convicting him of aggravated assault, for which he was sentenced to eight years in the Institutional Division of the Texas Department of Criminal Justice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated assault and sentenced to eight years in prison. On appeal, appellant asserted two points of error. First, appellant argued that the statutory amendment that elevated the classification of the offense of aggravated assault from a third-degree felony to a second-degree felony violated the equal protection clause. Appellant's point, however, was decided directly against him in a prior case. It had been held that the amendment to Texas Penal Code Ann. § 22.02 was not in violation of the equal protection clause or constitutionally unsound. Next, appellant argued that he was denied reasonably effective assistance of counsel at the guilt-innocence and the punishment phases of the trial in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. 10. Appellant failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence, however, his ineffective assistance claim. Appellant did not show that counsel's performance was deficient by norms of the community to the extent that counsel failed to function as the "counsel" guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI, nor did appellant show that counsel's performance prejudiced him. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated assault. The statutory amendment, which elevated the classification of aggravated assault to a second-degree felony, did not violate the equal protection clause, and appellant failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.

Perry v. State


NO. 09-97-00219 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2802


December 17, 1998, Submitted  
April 14, 1999, Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 1st Judicial District Court. Newton County, Texas. No. 4348.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his judgment of conviction for the crime of indecency with a child in the 1st Judicial District Court of Newton County (Texas). Defendant contended that the trial court impermissibly admitted evidence of defendant's prior sex crime conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of indecency with a child and appealed that conviction. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly admitted evidence of a prior indecency conviction over his objection. The trial court admitted this evidence on rebuttal, after defendant's attorney attacked the credibility of the victim witness and the victim's moral character. The appellate court held that defendant's attorney attempted to make the victim, a 6-year old boy, look like the sexual aggressor. Therefore, it was not error for the trial court to admit defendant's prior offense, because evidence that defendant had been the sexual aggressor on a prior occasion involving a minor. The court held that defendant's prior bad act was admissible to show intent, motive, or absence of mistake. Defendant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for the crime of indecency with a child was affirmed. The appellate court held that the trial court properly admitted evidence of defendant's prior sex crime conviction to show intent, motive, or absence of mistake.

Haufler v. State


No. 04-97-00771-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2805



April 14, 1999, Delivered  
April 14, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 198th Judicial District Court, Kerr County, Texas Trial Court No. B97-175. Honorable Emil Karl Prohl, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the 198th Judicial District Court, Kerr County (Texas), which convicted him on three counts of aggravated sexual assault of a child. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a continuance, in denying his motion for change of venue, and in allowing certain witness testimony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on three counts of aggravated sexual assault of a child. He first appealed his judgment of conviction on the basis that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a continuance. On appeal, the court held that there was no error because defendant willingly changed attorneys three times and was warned after the second time that the court would not grant a continuance. Second, defendant contended that the court erred in denying his motion for change of venue due to the unfavorable treatment of his case in the press. Upon review, the appellate court found that the newspaper article at issue simply gave appellant's name and the crime charged, and did not constitute sufficient evidence of prejudice. Third, defendant objected to certain witness testimony, especially that of the victim. Defendant claimed that due to the fact that the victim was four years old at the time she testified, she was not a competent witness. The appellate court found no error and found that the record established that the victim was able to differentiate between the truth and a lie. Defendant's other contentions were found to be without merit and his conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant was not granted relief on appeal and the court affirmed his conviction on three counts of aggravated sexual assault of a child. The court held that the trial court did not commit reversible error in denying defendant's motion for a continuance, in denying his motion for change of venue, and in allowing certain witness testimony, including that of the child victim.

Fullers Jewelry, Inc. v. Dallas Cent. Appraisal Dist.


No. 05-96-01776-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2666



April 12, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an ad valorem tax case, appellant jeweler sued appellee agency challenging appellee's appraisal of its inventory for two tax years. After a non-jury trial, the 44th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) rendered judgment in favor of appellee and appellant took exception.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned three jewelry stores that were subject to an ad valorem tax. In the two tax years at issue, appellant challenged appellee agency's appraisal of its inventory. The county appraisal board affirmed the valuation. Appellant then filed suit pursuant to Tex. Prop. At trial, the court heard evidence from both sides and determined that the valuation was proper based upon Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.01(a) (1992). Appellant took exception. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that appellant's inventory was properly valued pursuant to § 23.01(a) and that there had been no abuse of discretion by the trial court that warranted a reversal because there was sufficient evidence to support the court's findings.

526 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Barletta v. State


No. 06-98-00052-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


994 S.W.2d 708; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2582


March 24, 1999, Argued  
April 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 12, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 115th Judicial District Court. Upshur County, Texas. Trial Court No. 11,946.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant, convicted of intoxication manslaughter, sought reversal of the sentence imposed by a sentencing jury of the 115th Judicial District Court, Upshur County (Texas) on the grounds that inadmissible and unduly prejudicial evidence was admitted at sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of intoxication manslaughter. At his jury sentencing hearing, the trial court permitted the jury to be informed of appellant's prior juvenile delinquency adjudication for vehicular manslaughter and allowed the jurors to hear victim impact testimony. On appeal, appellant argued that allowing the jurors to learn of his juvenile delinquency adjudication was error since at the time he committed intoxication manslaughter the adjudication was inadmissible at sentencing. Appellant further argued that the admission of victim impact testimony was unduly prejudicial. The appellate court affirmed. It reasoned that, as to the juvenile delinquency argument, neither the ex post facto clause of the federal nor the state constitution was implicated inasmuch as the change in admissibility was a procedural rather than a substantive matter. As to the victim impact testimony, the court held that the claim was not preserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's sentence for intoxication manslaughter. The trial court did not err in admitting appellant's juvenile delinquency adjudication for vehicular manslaughter since a statutory modification allowing admission of the evidence after appellant's crime was procedural rather than substantive in nature. The court further held that appellant's objection to victim impact testimony was waived.

Wright v. Fowler


NO. 2-98-070-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


991 S.W.2d 343; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2640



April 8, 1999, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 236TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of summary judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision from the 236th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellee doctor in a malpractice suit arising out of elective cosmetic surgery and procedures.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient sued appellee doctor for malpractice arising out of elective cosmetic surgery and procedures. After the court granted summary judgment to appellee, appellant sought review. On appeal, the court held that because appellant waived his appeal of summary judgment for systematic injury, the court addressed the points only as they related to the local injury claim. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee because the record showed that appellee conclusively proved that appellant's medical negligence action was barred by the statute of limitations. In addition, appellant failed to plead a deceptive trade practices (DTP) cause of action that was not barred by the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code § 17.46 (b). The court noted that appellant merely recast his malpractice claim as a DTP claim to avoid the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee doctor because the record showed that appellee conclusively proved that appellant patient's medical negligence action was barred by the statute of limitations.

Texas Dep't of Pub. Safety v. Benoit


NUMBERS 13-97-685-CV & 13-97-690-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


994 S.W.2d 212; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2684



April 8, 1999, Delivered  
April 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court of Calhoun County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of county court at law reversed and appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On consolidated appeals, appellant challenged an order from the County Court of Calhoun County (Texas) that prohibited appellant from suspending appellees' driver's licenses after appellees were arrested for driving while intoxicated and their licenses suspended by an administrative court. Appellant contended that the trial court was without jurisdiction to hear appellees' appeal from the administrative court. Tex. Transp. Code Ann. 524.041(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged an order that prohibited appellant from suspending appellees' driver's licenses after appellees were arrested for driving while intoxicated and their licenses suspended by an administrative court. On consolidated appeals, the court reversed the order that prohibited appellant from suspending appellees' licenses. The court agreed with appellant's claim that the trial court was without jurisdiction to hear appellees' appeal from the administrative court's decision because appellees failed to comply with Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 524.041(c) by not sending by certified mail copies of their petition to appellant and the state office of administrative hearings. The court rejected appellees' claim that § 524.041(c) was directory and not mandatory, that they made only a legal, and not a factua,l challenge to the administrative decision, and that the requirement was not jurisdictional. The court analogized § 524.041(c) to other administrative appeals and the case law interpreting such statutes, and ruled that appellees' failure to comply with § 524.041(c) divested the trial court of jurisdiction over their appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that prohibited appellant from suspending appellees' driver's licenses for driving while intoxicated. The trial court was without jurisdiction to entertain appellees' appeal from the administrative license suspension because appellees did not send a copy of their petition by certified mail to appellant and to the state office of administrative hearings, as required by statute.

Wehmer v. State


No. 05-98-00002-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2507



April 6, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 3-80751-96.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 3 of Collin County (Texas) convicting her of unlawfully carrying a weapon in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02(a), because the statute was vague as to what constituted the proscribed conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawfully carrying a weapon in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02(a). The reporting officer testified that he found a handgun on the floorboard of defendant's car when dispatched to defendant's car in a ditch. Defendant claimed the common law defense that she was on her way home from the location where she received the gun. Defendant appealed on grounds that she was denied a fair trial, and that the weapon statute was vague for failure to give fair notice of the forbidden conduct. The court found that the gun on the floorboard of the car was on or about her person within the meaning of the statute. The court affirmed the conviction, holding the evidence clearly showed that the gun was on or about defendant's person, and the statute set a clear standard that an ordinary person would know what constituted the proscribed conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed because the evidence showed that the gun was on or about defendant's person, and the statute set a clear standard that an ordinary person would know what constituted the proscribed conduct.

McGlothlin v. Cullington


NO. 03-98-00205-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


989 S.W.2d 449; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2388



April 1, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied December 13, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 8292.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-01888, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas), dismissing for want of prosecution her medical negligence claim against appellee doctor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued appellee doctor for medical malpractice. The Insurance Commissioner found appellee's insurance carrier impaired, and the suit was temporarily stayed. Ninety days after the stay lapsed, appellee filed a motion, under the Texas Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, to compel appellant to file a cost bond. The court ordered appellant to file the bond. Appellant claimed by affidavit that she could neither pay the bond nor retain an expert to provide an expert report on causation. The trial court dismissed her case for failure to comply with art. 4590i, § 13.01(a). Appellant challenged the dismissal, contending the cost bond and expert report requirements violated federal and state due process protections. The court affirmed. Because the record lacked evidence of appellant's financial inability to comply with art. 4590i, § 13.01, she failed to meet her burden of showing that the statute did not meet constitutional requirements. Further, because the statute addressed the important state interest of containing medical malpractice insurance costs, it was not a special law under the Texas constitution.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing appellant's medical negligence claim affirmed because she failed to prove financial inability to comply with its requirements and failed her burden of showing that the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act did not meet constitutional requirements.

Rice v. State


NOS. 14-97-00620-CR, 14-97-00623-CR, and 14-97-00640-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2473



April 1, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 97-15267, 97-10063, & 97-10062.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, Reversed and Remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her convictions for two misdemeanor driving while intoxicated charges and one failure to stop and give information charge, entered upon her guilty pleas, from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County (Texas). Appellant contended that the trial court improperly denied her motion to suppress and improperly refused to declare Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged her convictions, entered upon her guilty pleas, for two misdemeanor driving while intoxicated (DWI) charges and one charge of failure to stop and give information. The court reversed and remanded one DWI conviction because the sentence imposed by the trial court was less than the minimum punishment mandated by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.09(a), rendering the sentence and conviction void. The court then affirmed appellant's other convictions, rejecting her claim that the trial court improperly denied her motion to suppress, as there was no probable cause for her arrest. The court ruled that because the parties had entered stipulated facts regarding the arrest, and because appellant not had objected to those facts at trial, she had waived error arising out of the conclusory stipulated facts. Finally, the court rejected appellant's claim that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061, which permitted evidence appellant's refusal to take a breath test to be admitted, was unconstitutional. The court ruled that such evidence was relevant, that the statute did not violate appellant's due process rights, and that it was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and reversed and remanded in part appellant's convictions for driving while intoxicated (DWI) and failure to stop and give information. Because the trial court's sentence imposed for one DWI offense was less than the minimum punishment mandated by statute, that sentence was void and the conviction was reversed. The statute regarding admissibility of appellant's refusal to take a breath test was not unconstitutional.

1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 2443

April 1, 1999, Opinion Filed

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 09/08/1999
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Harrison v. Thaler, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 74910 (S.D. Tex., Apr. 22, 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Harrison v. Dir., Tex. Dep't of Crim. Justice-Corr. Insts. Div., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 185440 (E.D. Tex., Aug. 1, 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Harrison v. Stephens, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25513 (S.D. Tex., Jan. 7, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 751713.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him by a jury for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon. The jury assessed his punishment at 36 years imprisonment, which was enhanced by two prior felony convictions. Appellant raised several issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Following several disputes, appellant put a small automatic pistol to his girlfriend victim's head and shot her once. Appellant was convicted by a jury for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, and his punishment was assessed at 36 years imprisonment because it was enhanced by two prior felony convictions. Appellant challenged the conviction, raising several assignments of error. The court held appellant's plea of true to the indictment's enhancement paragraphs and his stipulation to the evidence of the prior convictions thereby waived his challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence supporting those enhancement allegations. The court also rejected appellant's argument that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at the punishment stage because there was nothing in the record which reflected that his trial counsel encouraged him to enter a plea of true to the enhancement allegations and stipulate to evidence of his prior convictions. The court also found the statutory instructions given to the jury were not "misleading" and were relevant to appellant's offense; the trial court did not err in submitting the unobjected to statutory instructions. The order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, and his resulting sentence of imprisonment that was enhanced by two prior felony convictions, was affirmed. Among other findings, the court held that appellant waived any challenge to the sufficiency of evidence supporting certain enhancement allegations as he pleaded true to the enhancement paragraphs in the indictment and stipulated to the evidence of his prior convictions.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions by the County Criminal Court No. 5, Dallas County (Texas), for three counts of criminal simulation, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.22(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for selling Disney, Nike, and Guess items from his store that were not authentic. Appellant was convicted of three counts of criminal simulation, in violation of Tex. Miami Indep. Sch. Dist. v. Moses


NO. 03-98-00326-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


989 S.W.2d 871; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1987



March 25, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied August 26, 1999. Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled October 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-12031, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant exemplary school district sought review of a District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), decision that held that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 39.112 did not remove exemplary school districts from Tex. Educ. Code Ann. ch. 41's wealth equalization provisions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant exemplary school district sought review of a trial court decision that held that appellant was not exempt from Tex. Educ. Code Ann. ch. 41's wealth-equalization provisions by Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 39.112. The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The "requirements and prohibitions" that appellant was exempt from under § 39.112 referred to educational and not financial impositions. Such an interpretation did not contradict Chapter 41's plain language and was supported by legislative history. Section 39.112 waived educational oversight for districts such as appellant with the highest educational achievement standards, but did not waive their required participation in the school finance system. The trial court decision was not an advisory opinion because it involved a present controversy and not merely hypothetical issues. The trial court did not err in failing to strike intervenors' pleadings or in allowing intervention in the instant action. Allowing intervention was within the discretion of the trial court and the intervenors had an interest in the outcome of the case at bar because it involved a constitutionally efficient and equitable school system.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed a trial court decision that held that appellant exemplary school district was not exempt from statutory wealth equalization provisions, but rather only educational "requirements and prohibitions"; such was consistent with school financing goals and legislative history. The instant action involved an actual controversy and allowing intervention by interested parties was with the trial court's discretion.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), which denied appellant relief in a pretrial habeas corpus proceeding that appellant initiated after he was charged with a misdemeanor offense of violating a city camping ban ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a habeas corpus application after he was charged with a misdemeanor offense of violating a city camping ban ordinance. Appellant sought pretrial relief, alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court granted and issued the writ, held a hearing without allowing the admission of evidence, and denied appellant relief on the ground that he had an adequate remedy at law: direct appeal from the municipal court. 540 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Williamson v. State


No. 05-97-01340-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


990 S.W.2d 404; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1892



March 19, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F93-01558-KI.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Criminal District Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), upon a sentence imposed by a jury at a new trial solely on appellant's punishment for his burglary conviction. Appellant alleged that the exclusion of evidence exonerating him from guilt violated Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.03, § 3 and art. 44.29(b), and that the trial court miscalculated his credit for time already served.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced for burglary. After habeas proceedings, the court remanded the case for a re-trial solely on the punishment phase pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. 44.29(b). At the re-trial, the trial court did not permit appellant to introduce evidence pertaining to his guilt, and entered judgment on the jury's determination of punishment. On appeal, the court held that the phrase in Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 44,29(b) allowing a defendant to offer evidence of the circumstances of the crime was redundant with the same phrase in Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a), and that the phrase referred only to circumstances relevant to assessing punishment, and not to appellant's guilt. Thus, the exclusion of exonerating evidence was not error. However, the trial court erred in calculating the amount of credit that appellant was entitled to for the time he had already spent in jail. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment but modified it to give appellant the correct amount of credit against his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment on appellant's new trial on the punishment phase, although the court modified the sentence by recalculating the credit for time served. The court held that appellant had a statutory right to introduce evidence relevant to sentencing, but he had no right, statutory or otherwise, to introduce evidence pertaining to his guilt. Thus, the trial court properly excluded exonerating evidence at the re-trial.

Hawkins v. Comm'n for Lawyer Discipline


No. 08-97-00515-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


988 S.W.2d 927; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1856



March 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1962. Released for Publication May 14, 1999. Rehearing Overruled May 12, 1999. Petition for Review Denied September 2, 1999.
53.7(F) mot. for extension of time filed by, 07/08/1999
Petition for review denied by, 09/02/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Hawkins v. Texas Comm'n for Lawyer Discipline, 529 U.S. 1022, 120 S. Ct. 1426, 146 L. Ed. 2d 317, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1962 (2000)
Related proceeding at Disciplinary Bd. v. Hawkins (In re Hawkins), 2001 ND 55, 623 N.W.2d 431, 2001 N.D. LEXIS 71 (2001)
Related proceeding at In re Disciplinary Action Against Hawkins, 802 N.W.2d 362, 2011 Minn. LEXIS 551 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: (TC # 41,132). Appeal from 385th District Court of Midland County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed judgment as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the 385th District Court of Midland County (Texas) finding that he violated Tex. R. Prof'l Conduct 1.01(b)(1), 1.15(c), and 1.15(d) by intentionally disobeying a court order to represent an indigent and committing other egregious acts. Appellant urged, among numerous claims, that he was forced to defy the court order by the professional conduct rules.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment as modified finding that appellant attorney violated Tex. R. Prof'l Conduct 1.01(b)(1), 1.15(c), and 1.15(d) and suspending him from the practice of law for one year followed by a probated suspension. Appellant intentionally disobeyed a court order to represent an indigent, falsely told the indigent that the judge found he was not entitled to an attorney, ignored notices, and failed to communicate with the indigent regarding the content of notices. The court rejected appellant's various claims, including that due process violations occurred, that the Rules were vague, that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient, and that he was forced to defy the judge because appellant deemed himself incompetent to represent the indigent, and that the ethical rules placed the determination of competence solely on appellant. Appellant failed to consider the more specific rules concerning court appointments, which required that appellant continue representing the indigent despite good cause for termination. The court agreed that the judgment incorrectly stated that it was agreed and modified the judgment to delete any reference to an agreed judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that appellant attorney violated professional rules of conduct. The court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to support the conclusion that appellant violated the ethical standards at issue. Appellant's various grounds for appeal lacked merit, except that the judgment incorrectly stated that it was agreed. The judgment was modified merely to delete any reference to an agreed judgment.

Williams v. Clarke


NO. 09-98-479 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1880


March 11, 1999, Submitted  
March 18, 1999, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 60th District Court Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. B-157,999.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 60th District Court, Jefferson County, Texas, which granted appellee summary judgment on the grounds that appellant's claims for medical malpractice were barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought suit against appellee for medical malpractice. Appellee thereon moved for summary judgment on the grounds that appellant's claims were barred by the statute of limitations, which was granted by the trial court. On appeal, the court found appellant had not filed suit until well after the expiration of the two-year limitations period. Consequently, her suit was barred by the provisions of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1999). The court found no evidence attached to appellant's response to the motion for summary judgment establishing that appellee's failure to tell appellant, at the time of the surgery, that he used non-absorbable stitches amounted to fraud or fraudulent concealment. Additionally, because appellant failed to sue for nearly two years after learning of the alleged injury, the court concluded that, as a matter of law, appellant did not file suit against appellee within a reasonable time after discovering her alleged injury. Therefore, the open courts defense raised by appellant did not save her lawsuit from the statute of limitations. Appellant's action was thereby barred by the statute of limitations, and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment, which granted appellee summary judgment on the grounds that appellant's claims for medical malpractice were barred by the statute of limitations, was affirmed as proper after appellant's two points of error were overruled.

Jackson v. State

March 16, 1999, Decided

DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the judgment of the 282nd Judicial District Court of Dallas County (Texas), favoring plaintiff and sentencing defendant to 25 years' imprisonment for delivery of a controlled substance (cocaine).


OVERVIEW: Following the revocation of defendant's deferred adjudication community supervision, he was adjudged guilty of delivery of a controlled substance (cocaine) and sentenced to imprisonment for 25 years. Defendant contended that his sentence violated his state and federal constitutional rights because it was grossly disproportionate to the crime and inappropriate to the offender. Even though defendant failed to preserve his alleged error for appeal, the appellate court held that his sentence did not amount to cruel and/or unusual punishment under the federal and state constitutions because it was not grossly disproportionate to the offense for which he was convicted. The sentence was the minimum punishment that could be assessed under the facts of the case. Moreover, the trial court gave defendant three chances to successfully complete his community supervision before finally revoking it.


OUTCOME: Defendant's 25-year sentence for delivery of a controlled substance was affirmed because it did not constitute cruel and/or unusual punishment under the state and federal constitutions. Defendant's sentence was not grossly disproportionate to the offense for which he was convicted.

Lemon v. State


NO. 14-96-00413-CR and 14-96-00423-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1695



March 11, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 183rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), in which the court entered judgment revoking deferred adjudication for two counts of robberies and imposed a sentence accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Judgment revoking deferred adjudicating for two counts of aggravated robberies was affirmed. In affirming the lower court's judgment, the appeals court held that appellant could not appeal a determination to adjudicate guilt. The court further held that appellant failed to establish that he was denied any constitutional rights. The appeals court held that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12, § 9(c) authorized the use of the presentence investigation report to assist the trial court in determining the appropriate punishment after defendant pled guilty or nolo contendere. The appeals court also held that the sentence imposed on appellant was within the statutory range of punishment and was not so plainly disproportionate as to shock the sense of humankind and, thus, constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment revoking the deferred adjudication for two counts of robberies because it was within the lower court's power to enter adjudication and because appellant was not denied any constitutional rights.

North Am. Refractory Co. v. Easter


NUMBER 13-97-791-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


988 S.W.2d 904; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1756



March 11, 1999, Delivered  
March 11, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Denied September 13, 2000. Petition for Review Denied May 18, 2000. Rehearing Denied April 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 357th District Court of Cameron County, Texas. Tr.Ct.No. 95-02-773-E.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a manufacturer of asbestos-containing products, sought review of a 357th District Court of Cameron County (Texas) decision that, after a jury trial, found it liable under the Alabama Extended Manufacturer's Liability Doctrine on theories of negligence and products liability in consolidated actions by appellees, exposed workers and their spouses, and awarded appellees damages for personal injuries and loss of consortium.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, manufacturer of asbestos-containing products, challenged a trial court decision, after a jury trial, that held that appellant was liable on negligence and product liability theories under the Alabama Extended Manufacturer's Liability Doctrine and awarded appellees, exposed workers and their spouses, damages for personal injuries and loss of consortium. The appellate court affirmed the trial court decision. There was sufficient legal and factual evidence that appellant's product proximately caused appellees' injuries because it was shown that appellant's product's emitted dust with dangerous levels of asbestos and that appellee workers came into frequent contact with the dangerous substance. Compensatory damages were justly awarded based on properly admitted expert testimony regarding appellee workers' health woes, and there was no indication that the jury was improperly influenced by passion or sympathy. The consolidation of appellees' actions was proper because they shared common factors and the consolidation did not unfairly prejudice appellant. Punitive damages were properly awarded and were not unconstitutionally excessive based on appellant's conduct.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed a trial court decision that held appellant, a manufacturer of asbestos-containing products, liable under negligence and product liability theories and awarded appellees, exposed workers and their spouses, damages for personal injuries and loss of consortium. There was sufficient evidence of causation, of the severity of appellees' injuries, and that appellant's conduct was reprehensible to support the jury's decision.

Hamby v. Dysart


NO. 07-98-0101-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1630



March 10, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 108TH DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 82,503-E; HON. ABE LOPEZ, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Portion of final summary judgment denying Hamby recovery upon his claims arising under 42 U.S.C. § 1983 reversed, and all other aspects affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an order from the 108th District Court of Potter County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant magistrate and defendant city in an action for malicious prosecution, false imprisonment, abuse of process, intentional infliction of emotional distress, interference with contract, violation of state constitutional rights, denial of due process, and violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant magistrate and defendant city for malicious prosecution, false imprisonment, abuse of process, violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and other claims. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendants, and plaintiff appealed. The appellate court reversed the portion of the judgment that denied recovery for the civil rights claim and affirmed the remaining portions. Defendant magistrate's actions were protected by judicial immunity when he complained to defendant city about noise from plaintiff's business that was disrupting court operations. His acts were judicial in nature and within his jurisdictional authority. Sovereign immunity was inapplicable to defendant city to the extent that intentional torts gave rise to a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Where plaintiff was never imprisoned or otherwise detained, false imprisonment could not constitute a basis for relief under § 1983, but none of the defenses proffered by defendant city warranted denial of the purported § 1983 claim based on malicious prosecution. Defendant city failed to meet its burden of establishing the absence of a policy, practice, or custom as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: In an action against defendant magistrate and defendant city for malicious prosecution, false imprisonment, abuse of process, intentional infliction of emotional distress, interference with contract, violation of state constitutional rights, denial of due process, and civil rights violations, the portion of the judgment that denied plaintiff recovery for his civil rights claims was reversed and the remaining portions were affirmed.

Republic Western Ins. Co. v. State


NO. 03-98-00235-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


985 S.W.2d 698; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1435



March 4, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-09374, HONORABLE MARY PEARL WILLIAMS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant renters challenged the order of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas), which issued a temporary injunction enjoining appellant from engaging in the unauthorized business of insurance in violation of Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 1.14-1.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court did not err in issuing a temporary injunction against appellant renters for violating Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 1.14-1 and that the injunction was not void for vagueness. Appellants had brought a declaratory action maintaining that they were not violating art. 1.14-1 by offering various moving-related insurance packages to their customers. Appellee state counterclaimed seeking to enjoin appellants' practice of selling the packages as the unauthorized sale of insurance. Finding that appellants had engaged in the unauthorized business of insurance, the trial court granted appellee's motion for an injunction. In construing the statute the court found that the legislative intent sought the broader goal of deterring unauthorized insurance business in general. In light of the determination the court found that it was not error to issue the injunction because appellants had engaged in the unauthorized business of insurance prohibited by art. 1.14-1. The evidence also established that appellants acted as local recording agents in the sale of insurance. The injunction was not overly broad because it prevented appellants from circumventing it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which enjoined appellant renters from selling insurance packages because the sales constituted the unauthorized business of insurance and the injunction was specific enough to prevent appellant renters from circumventing it.

Davis v. City of Palestine


NO. 12-95-00180-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER

February 26, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of August 27, 1997, Reported at: 973 S.W.2d 319, 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4749.

APPEAL FROM THE THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF ANDERSON COUNTY, TEXAS. Hon. Sam Bournias, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's summary judgment for City on issue of unconstitutional taking remanded, and trial court's judgment in all other respects affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owners sought review of an order from the Third Judicial District Court of Anderson County (Texas) granting summary judgment to appellee city in appellants' action under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 et seq., for damages to their business property and an unconstitutional taking of their business property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant business owners brought suit against appellee city under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 et seq., for damages to appellants' business property and an unconstitutional taking of their business property. On remand from the Texas Supreme Court, the trial court granted summary judgment for appellee. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's summary judgment order on the claim of unconstitutional taking. The trial court erred in granting summary judgment on the basis of the statute of limitations because appellee had not articulated this argument. Although appellants had failed to plead the necessary intent for an unconstitutional taking, appellee did not establish its lack of intent. With respect to appellants' other claims, the court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment order because appellants had merely pleaded mental anguish and not personal injury or death. Because mental anguish based solely on negligent property damage was not compensable, the trial court had correctly granted summary judgment on appellants' tort claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order granting summary judgment for appellee on the issue of an unconstitutional taking because the trial court granted summary judgment on the basis of the statute of limitations, although appellee did not make this argument. The court otherwise affirmed the trial court's summary judgment order because appellants did not allege personal injury or death.

Dispensa v. University State Bank


NO. 14-97-00380-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


987 S.W.2d 923; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1231



February 25, 1999, Judgment Rendered  
February 25, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 280th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-46087. Lindsay, Tony, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 280th District Court, Harris County (Texas), granting partial summary judgment to appellee, dismissing appellant's collateral attack on the six-year-old default judgment against him, and denying his bill of review of the default judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellee bank obtained a default judgment against appellant. Six years later, appellant filed a bill of review and a suit collaterally attacking the judgment. The trial court found for appellee, and the court affirmed the trial court's judgment on appeal. Appellant had received notice of the default judgment shortly after it was entered. Because he did not attempt to have the default judgment set aside at that time, he lost his right to attack the judgment by a bill of review. Appellant could not rely on extrinsic evidence regarding lack of jurisdiction in his collateral attack on the default judgment. The default judgment's recital of valid service was conclusive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order because appellant had notice of the default judgment shortly after its entry and did not take steps to have the judgment set aside and because appellant could not use extrinsic evidence to establish that the trial court had lacked jurisdiction over him when it had entered the default judgment.

Parker v. Galveston Cent. Appraisal Dist.


NO. 14-97-00892-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1242



February 25, 1999, Rendered  
February 25, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 10th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-CV-0978.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 10th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, which granted the summary judgment motion of appellees, appraisal district and county review board, in appellant's action for review of a denial of appellant's application to have his property appraised as "qualified open space land" under Tex. Tax Code §23.51 (1992). Appellant contended that he was denied due process and an opportunity to be heard.


OVERVIEW: Holding that appellant had not followed the procedural requirements to obtain review of the denial of his request for appraisal under Tex. Tax Code § 23.51 (1992), and that he had not been denied due process, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that appellant had failed to file a timely written protest of the denial of his application, as required by Tex. Tax Code § 41.44. The court found no evidence that appellant had protested the matter within 30 days of receiving his tax bill, which indicated that his property had not been appraised as open space under § 23.51. Because he had not complied with § 41.44, appellant was not entitled to a hearing. The court also noted appellant's failure to comply with Tex. Tax Code §§ 41.411(c), 42.08, which required him to pay the undisputed portion of his taxes before the delinquency date as a prerequisite to obtaining a final determination of his protest. The court held that § 42.08 did not violate the open courts provision of the state constitution. The court also held that appellant was not denied due process, because he received notice of the denial of appraisal, and had an opportunity to be heard after that time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for appellees, appraisal district and county review board, because appellant had not complied with the procedural prerequisites for obtaining review of the denial of his appraisal request. The court held that where, after notice, appellant had failed to file a timely protest, and had not paid the undisputed portion of his tax by the delinquency date, he was not entitled to review.

Lummus v. State


NO. 14-97-00338-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1255



February 25, 1999, Rendered  
February 25, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9651914.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated, Tex. Penal Code § 49.04 (Supp. 1998), on appellant's plea of no contest. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion to suppress, in declaring Tex. Transp. Code § 724.061 constitutional, and in refusing to suppress evidence of his breath test refusal.


OVERVIEW: Holding that appellant had failed to preserve his objection to the stipulation of facts at the suppression hearing, the court affirmed a DWI conviction. The court noted that appellant had not argued below that the stipulation was merely conclusory. Therefore, pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a)(1)(A), appellant had waived this complaint. Nevertheless, the court concluded that the stipulation contained evidence competent to show that the officers had reasonable suspicion to detain and probable cause to arrest appellant. The court found that because the officers saw appellant turn the wrong way down a one-way street, they had probable cause for a traffic stop. When they noticed that appellant smelled of alcohol, had difficulty exiting his vehicle, speaking, and paying attention, they had reasonable suspicion to conduct a DWI investigation. The court rejected appellant's contention that the state had to prove that the field sobriety test administered was reliable. The court rejected without comment appellant's claims that Tex. Transp. Code § 724.061 (Pamph. 1999) was unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress evidence of appellant's breath test refusal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated. The court held that appellant had not preserved for review his claim that the stipulation in the motion to suppress consisted of conclusory statements, and not facts which would support a detention or arrest. The court also held that there was no basis in law for requiring the state to prove that its field sobriety tests were trustworthy indicators of intoxication.

Suarez v. State


NO. 14-97-00342-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1256



February 25, 1999, Rendered  
February 25, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9700702.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15, Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated, on appellant's plea of nolo contendere. Declaring Tex. Transp. Code § 724.061 constitutional, appellant claims the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, and denying his motion to suppress evidence of his breath test refusal.


OVERVIEW: The court declined to review the denial of appellant's blanket suppression motion. The court held that the ground appellant asserted as error, that the stipulation for the motion contained conclusory statements and did not set forth the reasons why the arresting officers concluded that appellant was intoxicated at the time of his arrest, was not argued to the trial court on the motion, as required by Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a)(1)(A) to preserve the issue for appeal. As to appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of Tex. Transp. Code § 724.061, the court noted that appellant had pleaded no contest to the charge against him. Accordingly, appellant lacked standing to assert the constitutionality of § 724.061, because his refusal to submit to blood alcohol concentration testing was never offered in evidence against him. Therefore appellant could not establish that the operation of the statute prejudiced him, and his challenge was merely hypothetical. Finally, the court held that a warning read to appellant in connection with the blood test, which tracked the language of Tex. Transp. Code § 724.015, was not void, and did not render his refusal to take the test involuntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for DWI. Because appellant had not attacked a stipulation of facts as conclusory at his suppression hearing, he waived the issue on appeal. The court held that appellant lacked standing to assail an evidentiary statute's constitutionality, because he did not go to trial, and the evidence was not offered against him. The court also held that appellant's refusal to submit to a blood test was voluntary.

Cameron v. State


No. 04-97-00350-CR

Nelson v. State


NO. 09-97-335 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1259


October 22, 1998, Submitted  
February 24, 1999, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 1-A District Court. Tyler County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 8641.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by the 1-A District Court, Tyler County (Texas), that convicted defendant of retaliation while incarcerated at a correctional facility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant inmate was convicted of retaliation while incarcerated at a correctional facility. The indictment charged defendant with retaliating by striking an officer at the unit. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, contending that the indictment was untimely under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32.01 (1989) because he was not indicted until nine days after his arrest. The prosecution responded by asserting that defendant was not detained to appear in answer to a criminal accusation and, therefore, Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32.01 did not apply. Based on the testimony and documents admitted during the hearing, the appellate court concluded that defendant was not arrested and detained to answer the retaliation charge but that he remained imprisoned as a consequence of his earlier conviction. The restrictions and loss of privileges he incurred did not change the status of his detention. Accordingly, the court overruled defendant's motion and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant's motion to dismiss the retaliation conviction and affirmed the judgment. The court held that defendant was not protected by a state statute because defendant was not detained to appear in answer to a criminal accusation. Defendant was detained due to his earlier conviction.

 

557 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Richards


NO. 07-98-0038-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


991 S.W.2d 32; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 1145



February 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Dismissed May 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 3 OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 97-559,464; HONORABLE PAULA LANEHART, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of the judgment from the County Court at Law No. 3, Lubbock County (Texas), terminating her marriage to appellee husband.


OVERVIEW: Appellee husband sought a no-fault divorce. Appellant wife excepted to the portion of appellee's petition alleging grounds for the divorce and requested a jury trial, but the trial court denied her motion for a jury trial and granted the divorce. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 6.402 did not deny appellant access to the courts or deny her equal protection of the laws. Appellant had the right to a jury under Tex. Const. art. I, § 15 because there were questions of material fact to be resolved at the time she made her request. The error, however, was harmless because an instructed verdict would have been proper at the conclusion of the final hearing. Appellee's relevancy objections to appellant's interrogatories were not an admission that appellee had no admissible evidence on the issue of the insupportability of the marriage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because appellant was not denied access to the courts or the equal protection of the laws, any error in denying appellant's jury request was harmless, and appellee's objections to appellant's interrogatories were not an admission that appellee had no admissible evidence on the issue of the marriage's insupportability.

559 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Medford v. State


NO. 03-97-00769-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


990 S.W.2d 799; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 862



February 11, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand of June 15, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 3986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CALDWELL COUNTY, 274TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-174, HONORABLE THOMAS KENYON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Rendered in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the District Court of Caldwell County, 274th Judicial District (Texas), denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence and his subsequent conviction for the offenses of felony escape and possession of cocaine in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.06(a)(1), (c)(1) (1994), and Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(a), (b) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped and frisked by a police officer, who found crack cocaine in appellant's pocket. Appellant then fled from the officer. After later being apprehended, appellant was convicted of the offenses of felony escape and possession of cocaine in an amount less than one gram in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.06(a)(1), (c)(1) (1994) and Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(a), (b) (1998). On appeal, appellant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence and challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to support his escape conviction. The court affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress as well as appellant's cocaine conviction because it found that, under the totality of the circumstances, the officer had sufficient grounds to fear for his own safety to justify frisking appellant's outer clothing for weapons. However, the court found the evidence legally insufficient to support appellant's conviction for felony escape because there was not a showing that the arrest had been completed before appellant fled. Thus, appellant's conviction for escape was reversed.


OUTCOME: The decision below denying appellant's motion to suppress and convicting appellant of cocaine possession was affirmed because the court agreed that the police officer had sufficient grounds to justify frisking appellant. However, appellant's conviction for felony escape was reversed because there was no showing that an arrest of appellant had been completed before appellant fled from police officers.

Watt v. State


NO. 03-97-00213-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 869



February 11, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0955583, HONORABLE JON N. WISSER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), convicting him of capital murder in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2). On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. Appellant's due process rights were not violated by the redaction of his statement and the statements of appellant's co-defendants or by the trial court's denial of appellant's untimely motion to sever. Appellant's argument that he was afforded ineffective assistance of trial counsel failed because the record did not support appellant's position that his attorney functioned ineffectively when he withdrew appellant's pretrial motion to sever. The trial court did not err in refusing to suppress appellant's written statement because appellant was fully advised of his rights and voluntarily confessed. The crime of capital murder was not unconstitutional because the mandatory life sentence for capital murder was not cruel and unusual punishment. Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. § 37.071 and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.31(a) did not violate appellant's right to trial by jury because appellant had no right to a jury trial for the assessment of punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because appellant's due process rights were not violated by the redaction of his statement, appellant's trial counsel was not ineffective, appellant's written statement was a voluntary confession after appellant was fully advised of his rights, and the crime of capital murder did not violate appellant's right to a jury trial or appellant's right to be free of cruel and unusual punishment.
