Lopez v. State


NO. 03-97-00661-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


990 S.W.2d 770; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 871



February 11, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CALDWELL COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-008, HONORABLE ROBERT T. PFEUFFER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the District Court of Caldwell County, 22nd Judicial District (Texas) for two offenses of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02(a)(1)(B)(i)(iii), (2)(B).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted and tried seven months later for aggravated sexual assault. At his trial, the state introduced evidence of past convictions. Appellant's conviction and sentence under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02(a)(1)(B)(i)(iii), (2)(B) were upheld. The version of the speedy trial statute applicable to appellant's case had been held constitutional. Appellant did not timely apply for relief under the statute. He did not file his motion until over 19 months after he was indicted. An examination of the appellate record failed to reveal the date of appellant's arrest or his bail bond. Without that information, it was not possible for the court to tell when the next term of court expired. Appellant's testimony did not open the door for impeachment past the usual parameters of Tex. R. Evid. 609. However, the trial court gave an adequate limiting instruction to the jury in the court's charge. The prior convictions were limited to the credibility of appellant's testimony, and the jury was told not to consider them for any other purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because appellant did not timely apply for relief and failed to prove he was not indicted timely, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion by allowing evidence of appellant's prior convictions to be presented at the guilt/innocence stage of the trial.

Williams v. Houston Firemen's Relief & Retirement Fund


NO. 01-98-00681-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 893



February 11, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 281st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 97-09970.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of January 21, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 332.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial judge's order granting the Fund's jurisdictional plea.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fireman challenged an order from the 281st District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted appellee retirement fund's motion to dismiss appellant's administrative action seeking judicial review of the denial of his retirement credit transfer under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6243e.2(1), for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant fireman joined the fire department and appellee retirement fund. Appellant sought credit for years of service working in other fire departments toward his retirement with appellee. While his request was pending, appellee adopted a new interpretation of the retirement credit transfer statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6243e.2(1), § 16(a). The new interpretation held that years worked outside the city could be credited to appellee only if the former city also had a statutory firefighter's fund. Thus, appellee denied appellant's retirement credit request. Appellant sued appellee for its denial. Appellee moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and the trial court dismissed appellant's claims. The appellate court affirmed the order, holding that appellant could not challenge appellee's credit decision until the earliest possible date he would be eligible to retire, as described by statute.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order granting appellee retirement fund's motion to dismiss appellant fireman's case regarding the denial of his retirement credit transfer for lack of jurisdiction because no right of judicial review of appellee's administrative agency's action existed until appellant was eligible to retire.

Rodriguez v. Texas Workforce Comm'n


NUMBER 13-97-334-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


986 S.W.2d 781; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 978; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8453



February 11, 1999, Opinion Delivered  
February 11, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied June 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 156th District Court of San Patricio County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: That part of trial court's judgment assessing court costs against appellant REVERSED and judgment RENDERED that costs occasioned by trial and this appeal are taxed against Texas Workforce Commission. Remainder of trial court's judgment AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of decision from the 156th District Court of San Patricio County (Texas) which affirmed the decision of appellee, Texas Workforce Commission, denying appellant unemployment benefits. Appellant contended that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 201.011 and 207.049 were in conflict, and that and Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 201.011(1)(B) and 207.049 violated the Texas Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, city employee, sought review of decision affirming denial by appellee, Texas Workforce Commission, of unemployment benefits. Appellant suffered a work related injury. His employment was terminated and he filed for unemployment benefits while receiving workers' compensation benefits. Appellee found lack of compliance with Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 201.011, and denied claim. Appellant argued if he had applied for unemployment benefits at time he was terminated, he would have been disqualified by Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 207.049, because he was receiving worker's compensation benefits; such disqualification prevented him from applying within time limit of Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 201.011, and the two statutes conflicted. The court disagreed, holding that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 201.011 required appellant to file his claim within the time limit, not file and qualify. Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 207.049 did not address filing a claim. Appellant argued Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 201.011(1)(B) and 207.049 violated Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3 and 19. The court concluded appellant did not address violations of Texas Constitution until appeal and those issues were not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The judgment assessing court costs against appellant was reversed and the remainder of the trial court's judgment was affirmed. Texas Labor Code sections were not in conflict and Code sections did not violate the Texas Constitution.

Sandoval v. State


No. 04-97-00720-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 814



February 10, 1999, Delivered  
February 10, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Ex parte Sandoval, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 426 (2007)
Petition for discretionary review refused by In re Sandoval, 2008 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 277 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 13, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 226th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 97-CR-1652. Honorable Sid Harle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 226th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), which certified appellant to stand trial as an adult and convicted him of capital murder. Appellant argued he had been harmed by the prosecutor's improper jury argument. Appellant also argued that the automatic life sentence provision of the Texas capital murder statute had been unconstitutionally applied to him based on his age.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was certified to stand trial as an adult and was convicted by a jury of capital murder. The trial court sentenced him to life in prison. Appellant argued on appeal that he had been harmed by the prosecutor's improper jury argument. Appellant also argued that the automatic life sentence provision of the Texas capital murder statute was unconstitutional as applied to him because, because, at the time of the offense, the statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §8.07(a), prohibited the adjudging of a person under 15 years of age guilty of a crime. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. First, the court found that the prosecutor had not impermissibly shifted the burden to produce evidence. The court found that the remark questioned by appellant was merely a proper deduction by the prosecutor of the evidence provided. Second, the prosecutor was not found to have commented on appellant's failure to testify. The comment at issue was found to have been aimed at another witness. Finally, the court found that the automatic life sentence was not unconstitutional as applied to appellant because appellant was 15 at the time of the offense.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for capital murder and his automatic life sentence were affirmed. The prosecution was not found to have impermissibly shifted the burden to produce evidence. Furthermore, the prosecution was not found to have commented on appellant's failure to testify. Finally, the automatic life sentence provision of the Texas capital murder statute was properly applied because appellant was 15 at the time of the offense.

Robinson v. Thaler


No. 06-98-00109-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 732


February 4, 1999, Submitted  
February 5, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 102nd Judicial District Court. Bowie County, Texas. Trial Court No. 98-C-0844-102.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Arguing that the trial court abused its discretion by dismissing his appeal before appellees had answered his suit and before conducting a hearing, appellant inmate sought review from the 102nd Judicial District Court (Texas), which dismissed his lawsuit against various officers and employees of the state Department of Criminal Justice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate filed a lawsuit against employees of the department of criminal justice for alleged violations of his rights, privileges and immunities guaranteed by constitutional provisions and statutes. The trial court dismissed the lawsuit stating that the realistic chance of success was slight, and that the lawsuit was frivolous. On appeal, appellant contended that the trial court abused its discretion by dismissing his appeal before appellees had answered his suit and before conducting a hearing. The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal finding that it was not mandatory for the court to conduct a hearing to decide whether the suit should have been dismissed under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. § 14.004(c). The court found that because the claim was frivolous, the trial court was statutorily permitted to dismiss the suit before service. Therefore, because appellees were never served, the court did not abuse its discretion by dismissing the case before they filed answers. The court held that the dismissal of the lawsuit did not constitute a denial of appellant's right of access to the courts under Tex. Const. art. I, § 19 and under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The judgment of dismissal was affirmed because the trial court did not abuse its discretion by dismissing his appeal before appellees had answered his suit and before conducting a hearing, because it was not mandatory for the court to conduct a hearing to decide whether the suit should have been dismissed, and because the claim was frivolous.

Adams v. State


No. 05-96-01813-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 791



February 5, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Adams v. Dretke, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 32946 (N.D. Tex., Dec. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 265th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F96-43666-JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 265th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), convicting appellant of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's single point of contention on appeal was that the trial court's punishment charge was fundamentally erroneous because it contained an instruction on parole law that was confusing and misleading. Appellant acknowledged that the instruction was legislatively mandated by the code of criminal procedure under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1999). Appellant nevertheless asserted that the trial court erred in giving the instruction because it was confusing and misleading. The court found that it could not conclude that the trial court erred in giving an instruction required by the code of criminal procedure, and further found that it would have been error had the trial court failed to give the instruction. The court also rejected appellant's assertion that a jury could not rationally consider the existence of parole law without considering the manner in which it would apply to him, finding that the parole law instruction clarified for jurors a law about which they tended to speculate, and was not confusing or misleading.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court held that the trial court was required by statute to give the jury instruction contested by appellant and that the instruction was not confusing or misleading.

Brinkley v. Texas Lottery Comm'n


NO. 03-97-00252-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


986 S.W.2d 764; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 684



February 4, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-14591, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee of gambling machines appealed from an order of the District Court of Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment and dismissed plaintiff's declaratory judgment suit that requested the court declare that certain machines were not gambling devices within the meaning of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(B)(4) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff licensee of gambling machines was told he could no longer place his gambling machines in a bingo parlor after the lessor received a letter from defendant lottery commission. Plaintiff did not have a lottery license. Plaintiff filed a declaratory judgment suit that requested the court declare his machines were not gambling devices within the meaning of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(B)(4) (1998). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, and plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed because the separation of powers doctrine prevented courts from issuing advisory opinions. Because plaintiff did not hold a lottery license and was not personally affected by defendant's letter, any opinion would have been advisory. The court found plaintiff was not entitled to an injunction because defendant did not threaten any action, and injunctions were only proper to prevent a party from engaging in an activity. The court found the letter written by defendant was within its powers; therefore, it was not within the definition of the Tex. Gov. Code Ann. § 2001.038, which permitted declaratory judgment suits to determine the validity of administrative actions.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court that dismissed plaintiff's suit was affirmed because plaintiff was not personally affected by defendant's actions, thus the court could have only issued an advisory opinion, which was a violation of the separation of powers doctrine. Plaintiff was not entitled to an injunction because such a remedy was only proper to prevent defendant from engaging in an activity and defendant did not engage in or threaten action.

WBD Oil & Gas Co. v. Railroad Comm'n


NO. 03-97-00002-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


35 S.W.3d 34; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 683; 148 Oil & Gas Rep. 447



February 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing En Banc Overruled January 19, 2001. Concurring Opinion on Motion for Rehearing January 19, 2001. Substituted Dissent on Motion for Rehearing January 19, 2001, for Withdrawn Dissent of February 4, 1999.
Petition for review granted by, 09/20/2001
Reversed by, Remanded by R.R. Comm'n v. WBD Oil & Gas Co., 104 S.W.3d 69, 2003 Tex. LEXIS 9, 46 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 442 (Tex., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-07116, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed appellant's suit for want of jurisdiction. Appellants suit challenged the validity of field rules promulgated by appellee Railroad Commission of Texas for oil and gas fields in the Texas panhandle.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Railroad Commission of Texas enacted field rules to govern the drilling, completion and operation of wells in the Texas Panhandle. After being sued for allegedly violating certain of theses rules, appellants, oil and gas companies, filed the present lawsuit to determine the validity and applicability of the rules. In the petition, appellants sought declaratory relief that the rules violated various state and federal statutes and constitutional provisions. The trial court dismissed appellants' case on jurisdictional grounds. On appeal, the court concluded that the trial court did have jurisdiction to review the validity of the rules pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 2001.038 for three reasons: because the rules fell within the statute's definition of "rule" and meet the general requirements for an administrative rule; the proceeding through which the rules were adopted did not qualify as a "contested case" under the statute; and appellee was statutorily required to use trial-type procedures in promulgating field rules. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's order dismissing appellants' suit and remanded the cause to that court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision dismissing appellants' action challenging the validity of certain administrative rules was reversed and remanded where the court concluded that the trial court did have jurisdiction to review and determine the validity of the rules at issue.

Lynn v. Board of Law Examiners


NO. 03-97-00478-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 677



February 4, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 261ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-05917, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Travis county, 261st Judicial District (Texas), which affirmed an order of appellee Board of Law Examiners that appellant lacked the good moral character required for admission to the state Bar.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected appellant's argument that appellee Board of Law Examiner's finding -- that appellant lacked the moral character required for Bar admission -- was unsupported by substantial evidence. Rejecting the claim, the court pointed to appellant's unauthorized practice of law, his violation of accountancy regulations under which he was licensed as an accountant, the provision of auditing services in violation of federal agency standards, and ruled that appellant's testimony attacking witnesses was not credible. Further, there existed a rational connection between appellant's negative character traits and the likelihood of client injury or obstruction of justice. Nor was the statute regulating the unauthorized practice of law unconstitutionally vague, as it provided clear warning of proscribed conduct. An injunction and consent order barring certain appellant activity was not res judicata as to his moral character, as they did not involve appellee concerns. Due process objections of appellant lacked merit, as he received notice of his hearing and was heard. Finally, no right to a jury trial attached to a suit for appellate review of appellee's administrative decision.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed that appellant lacked the good moral character required for admission to the Bar of Texas, because substantial evidence revealed appellant's unauthorized practice of law and violation of accountancy standards for licensed accountants, as client injury or obstruction of justice likely, as controlling statute on unauthorized practice of law not constitutionally vague, and as due process rights of appellant observed.

 

571 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


White v. State


No. 06-98-00145-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


988 S.W.2d 277; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 672


February 2, 1999, Submitted  
February 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 265th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court No. F-9800804-NR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the 265th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) for failing to register as a sex offender. Appellant claimed that his punishment under the sex registration statute violated the ex post facto clause of the Texas Constitution and that the law was unconstitutionally applied to him because it added an additional punitive measure to an act previously committed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for failing to register as a sex offender. He sought review of the conviction claiming that his punishment under the sex registration statute violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws because the statute was not in effect when he was convicted of a sex-related offense. Appellant also claimed that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to show that he knowingly or intentionally failed to register as a sex offender. The court affirmed the conviction first explaining that the statute did not violate the ex post facto clause of the Texas Constitution because the duty to register was a collateral consequence of a guilty plea that was remedial rather than punitive in nature. Further, although the penal institution failed to advise appellant of his registration requirements upon release, the evidence showed that his parole officer so informed him and thus no error was shown by prosecuting him for failure to register within seven days of being so informed. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction based on appellant's admission that he was told he was required to register but did not do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for failure to register as a sex offender. The court explained that the statute was not an ex post facto law because the duty to register was a collateral consequence of a guilty plea that was remedial rather than punitive in nature. Further, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction based on appellant's admission that he was told he was required to register but did not do so.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO

January 29, 1999, Delivered  
January 29, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied March 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court at Law No. 8, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 243480. Honorable Karen Crouch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant government sought review of a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 8, Bexar County, Texas, which reversed an order from the administrative court revoking appellee driver's license following an arrest for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: This appeal involved a license revocation resulting from a driving while intoxicated arrest. In two points of error, appellant government challenged the trial court's reversal of the finding against appellee driver by the administrative court. Appellant argued that appellee did not prove to the county court that the administrative law judge's decision was arbitrary or capricious or not supported by substantial evidence. OUTCOME: The judgment of the county court was reversed and the order of the administrative court, which revoked appellee driver's license, was reinstated because there was substantial evidence on the record to support the finding that appellee was driving while intoxicated.

Flores v. State


No. 06-97-00053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 648


November 2, 1998, Submitted  
January 29, 1999, Decided  
January 29, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 735739.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a conviction for the offense of aggravated assault upon a public servant from the 182nd Judicial District Court, Harris County, (Texas), contending trial court error by submitting a basis for conviction not authorized by statute and submitting a basis for conviction that was unconstitutional, and other error, including the failure to order a hearing to determine appellant's competency to stand trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was driving erratically when he was stopped by police officers, refused to comply with their demand to see his driver's license and proof of insurance, challenged the officers' authority, and then drove away dragging an officer. Appellant was convicted of aggravated assault upon a public servant in the trial court and appealed his conviction, contending that it was not authorized by statute, and other error, including the failure to order a hearing to determine his competency to stand trial. The court examined all of appellant's contentions of error and affirmed the trial court judgment against appellant. The court determined that because appellant had understood the charges against him but still insisted that he was to act as is own counsel, had conducted a vigorous voir dire of the jury panel, and had examined witnesses thoroughly, he was competent to have stood trial, and that his eccentric conduct was not a trigger for the court to hold an incompetency hearing. The court found that appellant had exercised his constitutional rights with reasonable understanding of the proceedings against him. The court overruled appellant's assigned errors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment against appellant because he had understood the charges against him, insisted that he was to act as is own counsel, had conducted a vigorous voir dire of the jury panel, and had examined witnesses thoroughly. The court overruled all of appellant's contentions of error, concluding that appellant had exercised his constitutional rights with reasonable understanding of the proceedings against him.

 

574 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. State


NO. 12-97-00334-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


993 S.W.2d 133; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 726



January 29, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 114TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF WOOD COUNTY TEXAS. Hon. Cynthia S. Kent.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the 114th Judicial District Court of Wood County (Texas), convicting appellant for the offense of aggravated sexual assault of a child, alleging that Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 38.37, which allowed the admission of evidence of extraneous incidents, was unconstitutional because it reduced the burden of proof to a standard less than beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: The events relating to the offense for which appellant was charged and convicted took place at appellant's home. The victim was 8 years old and friends with appellant's son. Victim testified that appellant initiated sexual contact with him. Victim also testified, over appellant's objection, to two extraneous incidents. Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.37 was unconstitutional on its face because it effectively reduced the burden of proof to a standard less than beyond a reasonable doubt, and therefore, violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. By its very terms, article 38.37 did not alter the burden of proof in the enumerated offenses. The article did not address the burden of proof. The trial court's charge did not alter the burden of proof. Article 38.37 did not impermissibly lessen prosecution's burden of proof because prosecution was required to prove every element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. Article 38.37 allowed introduction of extraneous offenses between a defendant and a child victim to show the states of mind of the defendant and child and their relationship. Appellant's conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child, holding that prosecution's burden of proof was not impermissibly lessened because prosecution was still required to prove every element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt.

McCuller v. State


NO. 12-96-00358-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


999 S.W.2d 801; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 689



January 29, 1999, Opinion Delivered  
January 29, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: This opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 7, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7704.

APPEAL FROM THE 241ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS. Hon. Diane DeVasto, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded to trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed a motion for rehearing, challenging a decision of the 241st Judicial District Court of Smith County (Texas), and pointing out that appellant had four previous convictions that were not reflected in the opinion. Appellant had been found guilty of injury to a disabled individual, his wife, and had challenged his conviction on appeal, contending trial court error in overruling his motion to suppress certain photographs.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a motion for rehearing, stating that appellant had four previous convictions not reflected in the court's opinion. Appellant had challenged his trial court conviction of injury to a disabled individual, his wife, contending trial court error in overruling his motion to suppress certain photographs of the interior condition of their home that had been taken by the independent executor of the estate of the owner of the house. The court overruled the state's motion for rehearing, withdrew their original opinion, and substituted a corrected opinion that made reference to the appellant's prior misdemeanor convictions for driving while intoxicated, criminal trespass, carrying a prohibited weapon, and theft by check. The court could not determine whether the photographs taken of the squalid conditions where appellant's disabled wife lived with him, for which appellant had sought suppression, had a substantial and injurious effect or influence in determining the jury's verdict. However, because appellant's wife had possession of the house where she lived with appellant, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court judgment because it could not determine whether photographs taken of poor conditions in the home where appellant's disabled wife, who had possession of the house, lived with him had a substantial and injurious effect or influence in determining the jury's verdict. The court overruled the state's motion for rehearing and issued a corrected opinion stating appellant's prior misdemeanor convictions.

Gonzales v. State


NO. 03-97-00484-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 436



January 28, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMAL COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR95-327, HONORABLE BILL BENDER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction from the District Court of Comal County, 22nd Judicial District No. CR95-327 (Texas), for unlawfully appropriating more than $ 20,000 but less than $ 100,000 without effective consent in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), (b)(1) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Victim had suffered a stroke and appellant was a neighbor who, for a fee, helped care for victim. Victim regained most of his physical strength, but continued to have difficulty speaking. Victim's daughter visited and noticed a new car in appellant's driveway. A bank employee informed daughter that victim and appellant had been at the bank and victim had attempted to withdraw an undetermined sum of money. Victim had recently withdrawn large sums of money from other accounts. Appellant produced a notarized statement in which victim stated that he was giving the car to appellant. A decision convicting appellant of unlawfully appropriating the money in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), (b)(1) (1994) was affirmed. Victim was impaired in his ability to make reasonable, rational decisions, and someone who saw victim frequently should have known that. A rational fact-finder could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant exercised control over the car. The verdict was not so contrary to the overwhelming weight of the evidence as to be clearly wrong or unjust. The words "diminished" and "capacity" were easily understood by a person of ordinary intelligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because victim suffered from a diminished capacity to make rational decisions, the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support the jury's verdict, and the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

Aguilar v. State


NO. 01-97-00482-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 502



January 28, 1999, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 737,222.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of indecency with a child, challenged his eight-year sentence from the 183rd District Court, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled no contest to the charge of indecency with a child and was sentenced. On appeal, he complained that his conviction was void because the judge reviewed his pre-sentence report prior to making a finding of guilt and that his eight-year sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment prohibited by U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. As to the pre-sentence report, the appellate court held that the judge's review of the report did not violate appellant's due process rights. Specifically, the court found that appellant's guilt was established before the trial court even ordered the pre-sentence report. The sole use of the report, the court said, was to aid in determining whether to give appellant deferred adjudication or a probated sentence. As to the cruel and unusual punishment claim, the court held that appellant failed to inform the court what was unique about his case that would support this claim. Further, the court said, the trial court assessed punishment within the range proscribed by law. Thus, because the appellate court found no merit to appellant's arguments, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment against appellant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant. Appellant was unable to show that the trial court improperly used his presentence report and how his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment.

Gates v. State


NO. 14-97-00083-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 515



January 28, 1999, Rendered  
January 28, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 730,819.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of possession of less than one gram of cocaine in violation of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115(b) (1992 and Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of possession of less than one gram of cocaine. The court held that probable cause existed to search defendant because the search was incident to defendant's arrest for failing to signal two lane changes in violation of Tex. Transp. Code § 545.104. The court found that the trial court's decision to give credit to the officer's fact rendition was not clearly erroneous. The drug evidence seized during the search was thus properly admitted. Defendant's sentence was properly enhanced under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(A)(1), (2) (1994 and Supp. 1999) because defendant's crime was a state jail felony and it was uncontroverted that he had been previously convicted of two felonies. Defendant failed to establish that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 1.15 denied him the opportunity to present evidence or violated his compulsory process and due process rights. Defendant waived all of his rights under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 1.14, and there was no requirement that he specifically waive his compulsory process right. The court therefore affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of possession of less than one gram of cocaine was affirmed because the search that produced the incriminating evidence was incident to a lawful arrest and the trial court's decision to believe the officer's testimony was not clearly erroneous. Defendant's sentence was properly imposed under the sentencing guidelines and defendant failed to prove that his compulsory process rights were violated or not waived.

Lewis v. State


NO. 14-96-00410-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 524



January 28, 1999, Rendered  
January 28, 1999, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 693,393.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him, following a jury trial, of capital murder and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial court decision that convicted him of capital murder after a jury trial and sentenced him to life in prison. The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Appellant's conviction was supported by sufficient evidence. The evidence was factually sufficient to support the finding that appellant intended to kill his victim in the course of a robbery. A witness' statement that was made in the context of the victim's description of the events made immediately after he was shot was admissible under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 803(a) as a hearsay exception for excited utterances. A jury instruction was sufficient to remove any prejudicial effect of a prosecutor's improper closing argument. The state's capital murder scheme was constitutional. The capital murder sentencing scheme did not violate appellant's due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and U.S. Const. amend. XIV and did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. Since appellee, the state, waived the death penalty in the instant capital murder case, the enhancement element was waived and there was no need to offer mitigating factor evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision convicting appellant of capital murder and sentencing him to a mandatory life sentence. Sufficient evidence supported appellant's conviction and no prejudicial procedural errors occurred. A jury instruction removed any prejudice caused by improper prosecutorial closing arguments. Appellee state's capital murder scheme did not violate due process or constitute cruel and unusual punishment.

Lorton v. Dolcefino


NO. 01-97-00545-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


986 S.W.2d 69; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 526



January 28, 1999, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 189th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-043872. Hon. Carolyn Marks Johnson, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered judgment that LaHaie take nothing on his claims.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant media companies sought review of a decision of the 189th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied appellants' motion for summary judgment on appellee building inspector's claim for libel and related claims.


OVERVIEW: Appellee building inspector claimed that he was libeled by appellant media companies as a result of a broadcast aired by appellants. Appellee also made claims for intentional infliction of emotional distress, tortious interference with employment relations, and negligence. Appellee's claims were based on a broadcast aired by appellants that showed film footage of appellee and his colleagues eating at a local restaurant for free due to their status as city building inspectors. The implication of the broadcast was that appellee had a quid pro quo relationship with the restaurant owner. Appellee was transferred to a different department as a result of the broadcast and received a reprimand from his employer. The appellate court reversed denial of summary judgment on appellee's claims, holding that appellee, as a member of a group, had no cause of action for defamation because any libelous statements were directed at the group and did not single him out. Further, the court denied appellee's claims because the statements complained of were substantially true. The appellate court held that appellee was to take nothing on his claims against appellants.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed denial of appellant media companies' motion for summary judgment on appellee building inspector's claim for libel and related claims because appellants' statements regarding appellee were aimed at a group of inspectors as a whole and were substantially true.

State v. Operating Contractors


NO. 03-97-00497-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


985 S.W.2d 646; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 534



January 28, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-14621, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County (Texas) holding that appellant was liable to appellee subcontractors for the unconstitutional taking of a vested property right held by appellees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state hired a contractor to construct and staff numerous emissions testing facilities in designated areas. The contractor hired appellee subcontractors to run each individual testing facility. After the sites were operational, the state enacted legislation that decentralized emissions testing. The sites were closed down and appellant eventually settled out of court with the original contractor. Appellees sued appellant, claiming that their right to run the facilities was a vested property right and appellant's conduct was an unconstitutional taking. The trial court agreed and awarded judgment in favor of appellees. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that the subcontractors did not have a vested property right in running the facilities, as there was no privity of contract between appellant and appellees. Without a vested property right, there was no unconstitutional taking and no damages. Appellees could not prevail on their contract claim because of appellant's sovereign immunity and appellees' waiver in their signed contract.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment because appellees had no vested property right in the contract between appellant and the original contractor, inasmuch as there was no privity of contract running between appellant and appellees.

SWZ, Inc. v. Board of Adjustment


NO. 2-97-220-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


985 S.W.2d 268; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 565



January 28, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied April 22, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 348TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sexually oriented business sought review of a decision form the Tarrant County District Court (Texas), which granted appellee municipal adjusting board's motion for summary judgment on appellant's claims that appellee improperly denied a specialized certificate of occupancy to operate a sexually-oriented business because it conflicted with Fort Worth, Tex., City Code app. A, Ord. 3011, § 18A(B)(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sexually oriented adult business applied for a specialized certificate of occupancy to operate at a location that was within 1000 feet of an existing church. The city in which appellant sought the permit had a local ordinance, Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 243.006(a) (1999); Fort Worth, Tex., City Code app. A, Ord. 3011, § 18A(B)(2) that restricted such establishments from operating within 1000 feet of a church, school, public park, residentially-zoned property, designated historical or cultural district, or other sexually-oriented business. Appellee adjustment board denied appellant's permit. Appellant sought judicial review of the denial, and the lower court granted appellee board's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed, reasoning that despite the fact that one of the church's halls was not connected to the church, the hall fell within the ordinance's definition of a church because people regularly assembled there for activities intended primarily for purposes connected with religious worship. The ordinance was sufficiently narrowly tailored to achieve the city's interest and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Decision of the lower court granting appellee adjustment board's motion for summary judgment on appellant's claims that it was entitled to a specialized operating permit was affirmed. The appellate court held that appellant failed to establish that appellee board's decision was illegal or that appellee board abused its discretion in denying appellant's application.

Medina v. State


NO. 07-98-0054-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


986 S.W.2d 733; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 435



January 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 29, 1999. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 158TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY; NO. F-97-0523-B; HONORABLE PHILLIP VICK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 158th District Court of Denton County (Texas), which convicted him, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(a)(2)(A) (Supp. 1999), for sexual assault of a child. Appellant asserted the statute imposed disparate treatment based solely on the age of the actor in violation of U.S. Const. and Tex. Const., and appellant was entitled to discover the criminal juvenile records of the victim and a state witness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for sexual assault of a child, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(a)(2)(A) (Supp. 1999). Appellant challenged the judgment, asserting the statute imposed disparate treatment for the same act based solely upon the age of the actor in violation of the equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. and Tex. Const., and the trial court erred in denying his discovery request for the criminal juvenile records of the victim and a state witness. The court held appellant's equal protection claim was reviewable, although raised for the first time on appeal, because he challenged the constitutionality of the statute itself. The court held the creation of an affirmative defense for underage children not more than three years older than the child with whom they had engaged in sexual conduct, based on the recognition of a difference in judgment, maturity, and ability to control conduct between children and adults, was not violative of equal protection. The court held appellant's request for criminal juvenile records was properly denied because he failed to establish good cause, materiality, and that the state had the information. The conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed because the creation of an affirmative defense for underage children based on the recognition of a difference in judgment, maturity, and ability to control conduct between children and adults was not violative of equal protection, and because appellant's request for criminal juvenile records was properly denied because he failed to establish good cause, materiality, and that the state had the information.

In re Luebe

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


983 S.W.2d 889; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 336



January 21, 1999, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied In re Luebe, 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 2597 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., Apr. 2, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 257th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Hon. Linda Motheral, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Court orders Sheriff of Harris County to release Mark D. Luebe from all restraint, including $ 250 bond posted in this case to secure his release.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought habeas corpus relief and argued that the order of commitment of the 257th District Court, Harris County, Texas, illegally restrained him.


OVERVIEW: The trial court judge held relator in contempt of court for not paying his child support and ordered that he be incarcerated for three days for criminal contempt and, thereafter, for civil contempt, until he paid the arrearage. Relator claimed he was indigent and requested appointed counsel pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 157.163(b)(d) (1996). The trial court judge refused to appoint counsel for relator because it found that relator had not attempted to borrow money from relatives to hire an attorney. Therefore, the trial court judge signed an order stating that relator was not indigent and not entitled to counsel. Relator was jailed for 23 days before he was granted bail. Relator sought habeas corpus relief arguing that he was illegally restrained under the trial court's order of commitment. The habeas court set aside the trial court's order of commitment and held that whether or not relator had attempted to borrow money from relatives was an improper factor for the trial court to consider in determining relator's indigency. Therefore, the court found that the trial court unconstitutionally deprived relator of his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court set aside relator's order of commitment and held that the trial judge improperly considered whether relator had attempted to borrow money from relatives to hire an attorney in determining whether realtor was indigent. The court found that the trial court wrongly deprived relator of his right to counsel.

OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of three misdemeanor offenses of outdoor burning under the Texas Clean Air Act and assessed punishment. Appellant challenged the decision, and the court of appeals affirmed the lower court's decision. Lara v. Williams


NO. 2-97-069-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


986 S.W.2d 310; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 247



January 14, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Granted January 27, 2000. Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Denied February 18, 1999. Counsel Amended February 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 352ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TEXAS, AND TARRANT COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Former inmates and county resident plaintiffs appealed a summary judgment by the 352nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) for county and county sheriff defendants on plaintiffs' claims that a religious education program in a county jail violated freedom of religion and equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: Disputed questions of fact concerning operation of a segregated unit in a county jail in which inmates were taught fundamentalist Christian principles required reversal of summary judgment and remand to determine whether the unit violated the Establishment Clause of U.S. Const. amend. I. Although county and county sheriff defendants contended there was a policy against proselytizing in the unit, plaintiff former inmates and county residents produced evidence that instructors were attempting to convert inmates to Christianity. However, county resident plaintiffs had no standing as taxpayers because defendant sheriff did not spend public tax money on the unit that he would not spend otherwise in operating the jail. A claim by an inmate that he was denied free exercise of religion by not being provided with the same accommodations as the Christians could be dismissed on summary judgment because an incidental burden on protected religious conduct was reasonable in relation to operation of the prison. Equal protection claims also were properly dismissed because there was no evidence of a sufficient number of inmates of other faiths to justify similar units for them.


OUTCOME: While summary judgment for county and county sheriff defendants was affirmed as to free exercise of religion and equal protection claims of plaintiff former inmates and county residents, disputed questions of fact regarding defendants' operation of a segregated unit in a county jail for teaching fundamentalist Christian principles required reversal of summary judgment on Establishment Clause grounds.

Sullivan v. State


No. 05-96-01472-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


986 S.W.2d 708; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 112



January 12, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 291st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F95-25250-MU.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 291st Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted appellant of indecency with a child, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant worked part-time delivering pizza. Upon making a pizza delivery to complainant's home, appellant engaged the complainant, a 10-year old boy, in conversation. Appellant then reached down and rubbed the boy's chest both inside and outside of the boy's shirt. Appellant was charged and he pleaded guilty to the offense of indecency with a child, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1). On appeal, appellant argued that the statute under which he was convicted failed to make a gender distinction between touching the breast of a male and a female child, and thus failed to provide fair notice, contrary to due process requirements. He contended that touching the breast of a male child would not ordinarily be considered sexual in nature. The court held that the statute was constitutional. It determined that it was touching accompanied with the requisite sexual intent that was criminal, and not merely touching. The statute did not prohibit innocent touching of a male child. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: Order convicting appellant of indecency with a child was affirmed because the requisite sexual intent accompanying the touching distinguished the offense from innocent touching of a child. Thus, the statute criminalizing the offense was constitutional for giving requisite notice of the intent.

Horizon/CMS Healthcare Corp. v. Auld


NO. 2-98-083-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


985 S.W.2d 216; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 68



January 8, 1999, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Early Issuance of Mandate Granted September 14, 2000. Petition for Review Granted August 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of January 7, 1999.

FROM THE 48TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment affirmed. Because Lexa Auld, Administratrix, is prevailing party in this appeal, court awards her all of appellate costs she has incurred.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a survival action initiated as a personal injury suit, plaintiff, the administratrix of a nursing home patient's estate, and defendant nursing home both appealed a judgment of the Tarrant County District Court (Texas). A jury had awarded the estate $ 2.37 million in actual damages and $ 90 million in exemplary damages for injuries the bedridden patient had suffered due to the nursing home's negligent and grossly negligent medical care.


OVERVIEW: The patient developed severe pressure sores requiring painful debridement due to medical neglect. She died while her personal injury suit was pending. Classifying the nursing home as a health care provider" and the suit as a "health care liability claim" under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1999), the trial court reduced actual damages to $ 1.54 million, plus prejudgment interest and, under former Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.007 (1994), reduced exemplary damages to $ 9.48 million. On appeal, the court rejected the home's argument that art. 4590i, § 11.02 was intended to cap exemplary damages as well as compensatory damages or that prejudgment interest, which was governed by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-1.05, § 6(a) (1994), should have been added to actual damages before capping. Although the damage cap would have been unconstitutional under Texas's open courts guarantee if applied to the patient's common law personal injury claim, it was not unconstitutional as applied to the estate's survival claim. Surveyors' Medicaid inspection reports were properly admitted to prove substandard care and to impeach.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's statutory reductions of the jury's compensatory and exemplary damage awards.

 

589 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Weaver v. Head


No. 06-98-00110-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


984 S.W.2d 744; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 35


November 19, 1998, Submitted  
January 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 188th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 98-819-A.



DISPOSITION: Order of trial court reversed, and cause remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff sought review of the decision of the 188th Judicial District Court (Texas), which issued a temporary injunction that directed him not to rely on an attorney general's opinion to support any attempt to prosecute appellee company for having a particular type of video machine.


OVERVIEW: Appellee company owned and operated video machines. Appellee filed a petition seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against appellant sheriff to prevent him from seizing or shutting down the machines based upon the authority of an attorney general's opinion, which suggested that appellee's machines were gambling devices. The trial court entered a temporary restraining order and restrained appellant from relying on the attorney general's opinion. The court reversed and held that the trial court avoided making an interpretation of the statute in question and circumvented addressing the application of the statute by simply ruling on the attorney general's opinion. The court found that the order that prohibited appellant from relying on the attorney general's opinion, without a showing that it conflicted with a judicial holding or had been declared unconstitutional, was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the temporary injunction that prohibited appellant sheriff from relying on an attorney general's opinion to prosecute appellee company. The court found that allowing the ruling to stand would have provided bad precedent for future cases, would have permitted the trial court to circumvent addressing the application of the statute at issue, and would not provide the relief sought by appellee.

 

590 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Kaczmarek v. State


No. 10-97-137-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


986 S.W.2d 287; 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 25



January 6, 1999, Delivered  
January 6, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court # 9638529.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for operating sexually oriented business without a permit, in violation of Houston, Tex. Code of Ordinances §§ 28-121- 28-135, from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8. Harris County (Texas). Appellant asserted that ordinance violated U.S. Const. amend. I , Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, Tex. Const. art. I, § 6, was unconstitutionally vague, that information was insufficient, and that arrest was unlawful.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for operating a sexually oriented business without a permit in violation of Houston, Tex. Code of Ordinances §§ 28-121- 28-135. The court found that the ordinance did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I or Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, when the ordinance was a reasonable time, place, and manner restriction and did not give the police chief unbridled discretion. The court held that appellant did not have standing to challenge the ordinance under Tex. Const. art. I, § 6 when the "church distance" requirement of the ordinance was not the cause of his arrest. The court found that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague when undefined terms could be understood in their ordinary sense and the ordinance was presumed to require a culpable mental state. The court held that the information was sufficient when it provided appellant with notice and tracked the ordinance's language. The court found that evidence seized after appellant's warrantless arrest was admissible when appellant committed violation in presence of police officer. Finally, the court held that prejudicial effect of photos of male dancers did not outweigh their probative value.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court found that the ordinance was a reasonable time, place, and manner restriction that did not give unbridled discretion and that appellant did not have standing to challenge "church distance" restriction. The court found that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, that information was sufficient, and that warrantless arrest was based on probable cause.

 

591 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


McLendon v. Texas Dep't of Pub. Safety


No. 10-97-367-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


985 S.W.2d 571; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 8130



December 31, 1998, Delivered  
December 31, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order on Cause September 14, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court at Law No. 2 Tarrant County, Texas. Trial Court # 97-71329-2.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the County Court at Law No. 2 Tarrant County (Texas), that he was ineligible for a concealed handgun license because he pleaded guilty to a felony offense and was placed on probation, even though he was subsequently discharged from the probation and the charges were dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The lower court determined that appellant was ineligible for a concealed handgun license because he pleaded guilty to a felony offense and was placed on probation, even though he was subsequently discharged from the probation and the charges were dismissed. On appeal, the court found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29ee) provided in general terms that a person who had served a felony probation was not eligible for a handgun license regardless of whether he was discharged from the probation. However, the statute did not address the situation where a defendant had been discharged from probation, his conviction had been set aside, and the indictment dismissed under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 7. Having considered the broad definitional provision of art. 4413(29ee), § 1(4) and the more specific clemency provision of art. 42.12, § 7, the in pari materia rule suggested that the latter controlled over the former. Because appellant did not have a prior felony conviction as that term was defined by art. 4413(29ee), he was eligible for a concealed handgun license. The court reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision below that disqualified appellant from obtaining a license to carry a concealed handgun because of his prior felony conviction, on the grounds that that conviction was set aside and dismissed. A clemency provision controlled over the definition of the term "convicted" found in the statute which would otherwise have disqualified appellant.

 

592 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. California


NO. 09-97-539 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 8142


November 27, 1998, Submitted  
December 31, 1998, Opinion Delivered  
December 31, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 284th District Court. Montgomery County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 96-09-02999.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtors sought review of a decision of the 284th District Court, Montgomery County (Texas), which denied their motion for a protective order against appellee board, which sought post-judgment discovery.


OVERVIEW: Appellee board obtained a judgment against appellant debtors in another state. Appellee filed its judgment in Texas pursuant to the Texas Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 35.005 (1997) (the Act), and sought post-judgment discovery. Appellants argued that the Act was unconstitutional. The reviewing court disagreed and upheld the denial of their motion for a protective order. Appellants received notice of the hearing and were in attendance with counsel. When a defendant is served with a notice of filing foreign judgment in a suit where he claims he did not receive service of process, the defendant may challenge the jurisdiction of a sister state by demonstrating that the sister state's exercise of in personam jurisdiction offends due process of law. Here, the Act provided them an adequate opportunity to contest the judgment.


OUTCOME: A decision that denied appellant debtors' motion for a protective order against appellee board, which sought post-judgment discovery, was affirmed because the relevant act provided appellants an adequate opportunity to contest the foreign judgment.

In the Interest of J.G.


No. 04-97-00950-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 8015



December 30, 1998, Delivered  
December 30, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 225th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-CI-14010. Honorable Martha Tanner, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Mother and presumed husband sought review of a judgment rendered by the 225th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas) that held that appellee was the child's father.


OVERVIEW: Child was born during the marriage of appellant mother and appellant presumed father. Almost five years later, appellee filed a petition to establish his paternity. In response to appellee's petition, appellant mother moved to dismiss appellee's petition pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 160.110(f). The statute mandated dismissal of a paternity suit under certain conditions, including passage of a statute of limitations. The trial court rendered judgment declaring appellee to be the child's father. Appellant mother and presumed father sought review of the judgment. Appellee argued that appellants waived their right to rely on the statute of limitations contained in § 160.110(f) by raising it in a motion to dismiss rather than in an answer. The court disagreed with that contention utilizing a rule of civil procedure. Appellee argued his paternity claim was not barred because it was filed less than two years after he was first told that appellant mother's son was his child. The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee. The discovery rule did not apply to paternity actions. Appellee's paternity action was clearly barred by the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The trial court reversed the judgment finding that appellee was child's father because under the Texas Family Code the suit to establish paternity was barred by the statute of limitations. The court rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellee and remanded to consider appellant presumed father's motion requesting an order designating him to be child's father.

 

594 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Dolcefino v. Turner


NO. 14-97-240-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


987 S.W.2d 100; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 8085



December 30, 1998, Rendered  
December 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 165th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-32914.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant television station and reporter challenged a decision from the 165th District Court, Harris County (Texas) in favor of appellee politician and attorney in a libel suit, contending the complained of statements were true or otherwise not actionable and there was no clear and convincing evidence of actual malice in the contents in two broadcasts.


OVERVIEW: A jury found against appellant television station and its reporter and in favor of appellee attorney and politician in a libel suit. The suit arose out of two television news broadcasts aired by appellants days before the run-off election for mayor of Houston between appellee and another. The broadcasts questioned the role appellee may have played in, and what he knew about, an attempted multi-million dollar insurance scam. The scheme involved one of appellee's clients who had reportedly drowned while sailing but was in fact still alive. On appeal, appellants asserted that the complained of statements were true or otherwise not actionable and there was no clear and convincing evidence of actual malice. The court found no clear and convincing evidence that appellants knowingly broadcast false statements about appellee. The corroborating evidence appellants uncovered was sufficiently probative to negate a jury finding of actual malice. Appellants' efforts to conceal the source of the story, although deceptive, did not constitute clear and convincing evidence that appellant reporter entertained serious doubts as to the truth of the broadcasts. The court reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the verdict below in favor of appellee politician and attorney and against appellant television station and its reporter, on the grounds that the record did not contain clear and convincing evidence to support the jury's finding of actual malice. In the absence of actual malice, the judgment could not stand. The court rendered judgment that appellee take nothing.

McMillan v. Texas Natural Resources Conservation Comm'n


NO. 03-98-00010-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


983 S.W.2d 359; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7981



December 29, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-15219, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which affirmed the order adopted by the administrative law judge in favor of appellee public entities in a case regarding appellees' imposition of standby fees on appellant's undeveloped property under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 49.231(a)(1) (1999) and 30 Tex. Admin. Code § 293.141(a) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner owned 40 acres of land. Appellee public entities imposed an annual standby fee on "undeveloped property" within appellee utility district's boundaries. Appellant's property was excused from the fees for three years pursuant to a negotiated settlement between appellant and appellee utility district. Appellee utility district applied to appellee Natural Resources Conservation Commission (commission) to impose standby fees on appellant's property. Appellant protested and an administrative law judge that appellee utility district receive the requested authority. The commission adopted the recommendation in a final order. Appellant brought suit in the trial court for judicial review of the order, an order which it affirmed in its judgment. The court looked to appellee commission's interpretation of the definitions of "undeveloped property" and "available capacity" under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 49.231(a)(1) (1999) and 30 Tex. Admin. Code § 293.141(a) and affirmed the trial court's judgment. Appellant fell within both definitions and could be assessed standby fees, regardless of the prior agreement between appellant and appellee utility district.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against appellant landowner and in favor of appellee public entities. The court held that appellee's interpretations of "undeveloped property" and "available" were not plainly erroneous. A prior determination of appellant's standby fees did not bar a subsequent determination of fees under res judicata. Finally, standby fees were a local assessment and not unconstitutional ad valorem taxes.

In re Scariati


NO. 07-98-0317-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


988 S.W.2d 270; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7991



December 28, 1998, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Denied petition for habeas corpus application in part, and dismissed the remainder without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an action for habeas corpus relief and requested discharge from an allegedly illegal confinement for contempt after the trial court determined that petitioner failed to comply with the directives of a prior divorce decree.


OVERVIEW: A trial court sentenced petitioner to six months confinement, to run concurrently, for each failure to comply with his responsibilities under a divorce decree. The trial court further ordered that petitioner remain confined until he paid past child support, court costs, attorney's fees, uninsured medical expenses, and health insurance expenses. Petitioner sought habeas corpus relief, asserting that the contempt order impermissibly denied him the chance to earn good time credit, attached the specifics of the motion to enforce and the contempt order. The court held that petitioner was not denied the chance to earn good time credit because the trial court's sentence did not specify a particular release date. The court further held that it had no jurisdiction to grant relief from the civil contempts because no review was available until the criminal contempt sentence expired. The court also determined that even if it agreed on petitioner's points of error on the contested portions of the contempt finding, he would still be subject to the sentence on the uncontested portion, as the sentences were imposed to run concurrently.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's request for habeas corpus relief from the trial court's order for criminal and civil contempt for petitioner's failure to comply with the provisions of his divorce decree was denied. The court determined that the trial court did not improperly deny petitioner the chance to earn good time credit, and the balance of petitioner's contentions were premature until expiration of the criminal contempt sentence.
