London v. State


NO. 07-98-0025-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7899



December 22, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 181ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF RANDALL COUNTY; NO. 8806-B; HONORABLE SAMUEL C. KISER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 181st Judicial District Court of Randall County (Texas) that entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting appellant of aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with the aggravated sexual assault of his nine-year-old daughter. At trial, the victim gave her testimony via closed circuit television, and appellant's attorney was not permitted to be in the same room with the child as she testified. After the jury returned a verdict of guilty and assessed punishment at 50 years of confinement, the trial court imposed sentence. Subsequently, appellant sought review. On review, the court affirmed because appellant's right to confrontation was not violated when the victim was allowed to testify without the presence of appellant's attorney in the room; there was no need for the trial court to make specific findings in the record before allowing the victim to testify by closed circuit television; having the victim testify from outside the courtroom without an explaining instruction to the jury did not deny appellant the presumption of innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of conviction because the procedures used at trial that allowed the victim to testify by closed-circuit television did not violate appellant's right to confrontation; appellant was not harmed by the failure to specifically instruct the jury on the procedures; the record supported the decision to allow the closed-circuit testimony.

Cearley v. State


NO. 07-98-0109-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7861



December 18, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY; NO. 0590208D; HONORABLE EVERETT YOUNG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of sexual assault on an indictment that was amended by the state prior to trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of sexual assault and sentenced. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the evidence was sufficient to support his conviction because there was evidence that the victim's consent to sexual activity was not given and that appellant knew that her impairment was such that resistance was not reasonably expected. The court held that it was not improper for the trial court to allow the state to amend the indictment because the amended indictment alleged the same criminal offense as the original indictment, and appellant did not claim that he lacked notice to the extent that he was prevented from preparing a defense. The court held that appellant waived his right to assert error based on the grounds that Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 28.10 was unconstitutional in that it violated his constitutional right to be indicted by a grand jury because he failed to assert this in the trial court. However, the court held that appellant's indictment did not violate his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of sexual assault. Evidence sufficiently supported the conviction because the victim did not consent, and appellant knew her impairment was such that resistance was not reasonably expected. It was proper to allow the state to amend the indictment because it alleged the same criminal offense, and appellant did not lack notice to the extent that he was prevented from preparing a defense.

Gravis v. State


NO. 03-97-00581-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


982 S.W.2d 933; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7731



December 17, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-2904, HONORABLE WILFORD FLOWERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas), which found him guilty of capital murder and aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: When appellant argued that the state made improper jury arguments, the court held that the arguments were permissible because they constituted proper pleas for law enforcement, and did not refer to the demands of the community. The court also held that counsel's trial strategy in failing to request a jury instruction on dependent personality disorder was not so deficient as to constitute ineffective representation by counsel, since the defense of dependent personality disorder was not well established. The court affirmed because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.02 was not unconstitutional on its face and as applied to appellant because it required the state to show that appellant had both the mens rea to engage in a conspiracy and the culpable mental state to commit the underlying felony, and thus did not excuse the state from pleading and proving a culpable mental state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction under statute allowing appellant to be convicted of a felony committed by a conspirator because the state was required to show that appellant had the mens rea to engage in a conspiracy and the culpable mental state to commit the underlying felony.

 

600 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


NO. 2-96-488-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


984 S.W.2d 732; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7775



December 17, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 176TH DISTRICT COURT OF HARRIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the 176th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault. After appellant pled "true" to an enhancement paragraph in the indictment, the trial court assessed his punishment at forty-five years' confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. After appellant pled "true" to an enhancement paragraph in the indictment, the trial court assessed his punishment at forty-five years' confinement. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the evidence was legally sufficient to support aggravated sexual assault because the victim's fear of death or serious bodily injury was reasonable. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(2)(A)(ii) was not vague or overbroad because the legislature intended to provide a more serious penalty to sexual assaults that occurred under the circumstance when the perpetrator placed the victim in fear of death, serious bodily injury, or kidnapping. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to show that the fear of the victim was the proximate result of the objective conduct of appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault and sentenced him under an enhancement paragraph in the indictment. The evidence was legally sufficient to support aggravated sexual assault because the victim's fear of death or serious bodily injury was reasonable based on appellant's objective conduct. The statute was not vague or overbroad because of the legislative intent.
